O vos, tres chiers filz, je vos ai acomplit cest livre qui est li derriens de la science de medicine ensamble l’emplissement de lui, et ai fait la fin per ses expositions et par ses declarations.	I have completed this book for you, most dear son, which is the conclusion of the science of medicine together with its contents, and I have finished it by means of explanations and declarations.
Et m’est venu en vision que je le vos acomplisse avec cest traitier, qui est partie de l’uevre de mains, c’est a savoir «cyrurgie».	And it came to me in a vision that I would complete this for you with this treatise, which is the work of hands, namely "surgery".
Et por ceu que l’uevre de mains est fortraite en nostre region et est etraingie dou tout en tout, si est perie li science et decopee, et n’est riens demorez de li fuers que les petites descriptions en livres des anciens que les mains ont muees.	And because the work of hands is prohibited in our region and foreign to all things everywhere, the science and art are perishing and decaying, and nothing remains of it that the hands have not changed from the ancient descriptions in books.
Et de ceu est venue li error et li vanitez, et sont closes les ententions et est aloignie li science.	And from this comes errors and vanity, and intentions are closed and knowledge is distant.
Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation; et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l’uevre avec l’ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.	It seems that I will bring it to life together with the arrangement of this treatise according to the way of exposition and declaration and abbreviation; and I will come together with the forms of fire cauterization instruments, and other tools of work along with the adjustment of the declaration and preparation of them, as necessary.
Et por la raison de ceu que nuls boins maistres de mains n’est trovez en nostre tens, est li ars de medicine eslongié.	And because no good master of hands is found in our times, the art of medicine has grown distant.
Et covient celui qui s’en entremet sormonter en la science d’anathomie, si com Galiens dit, tant qu’il saiche la juement des menbres, et les formes et les conjunctions et les separations d’aus, et aient connissance des osses et des nerf et des brais et le nombre d’ous, et le demenement et des voines movans et des reposans, et dou leu de lor issue.	And one who undertakes this must be summoned in the science of anatomy, as Galen says, until he knows the judgment of limbs, their forms and connections and separations, and have knowledge of bones and nerves and joints and the number of bones, and the movement and rest of veins and arteries, and the location of their exit.
Et por ceu dist Ypocras que li nons avec le non est mout, et avec l’uevre est poc; et meismement en l’art de main.	And so Hippocrates says that "nothing with nothing is something," and the same applies in the art of surgery.
Nos vos disons en l’introite de cest livre que qui n’est conissans des choses devant dites, si se gart qu’il ne chiece en error et qu’il n’ocie les homes; ensi que j’ai veut maintes fois plusors de ces qui s’entremettent de ceste science et si s’abandonent sen science et sens experiment.	We tell you in the opening of this book that one who is not knowledgeable about the aforementioned things should be careful lest he err and cut men; as I have seen many times those who engage in this science, abandoning their science and sense.
Car je vis un fol mire qui copa .i. apostume de scrophules ou col d’une femme, et copa les arteres dou col; por coi tant de sanc issit hors que li femme cheit morte entre ses mains.	For I saw a foolish man who cut one abscess from the neck of a woman and cut the arteries of her neck; hence so much blood came out that the woman fell dead in her hands.
Et vis .i. autre mire qui traït une piere d’un home d’eaige, et li piere estoit grans; si emporta avec li une piece de la vessie, et fut mors li hons dedens .iij. jors.	And I saw another man who pulled out a stone from an old man, and the stone was large; with it, he took a piece of his bladder, and the man died within four days.
Et je i avoie ja esteit apelez por lou traire, et vis la disposition dou malaide et la grandor de la piere, et soi bien s’on lou tailloit il en morroit.	And I had already been called upon to treat it, and saw the condition of the patient and the size of the stone, and knew well that if they cut into it, he would die.
Et vis .i. autre mire qui prist en cure .i. duc de nostre terre qui avoit la jambe brisie, et avec la briseure ot plaie; et li mires plains d’ignorance estraint la brisure sus la plaie as esteles par fort lieure, et ne lassa a la plaie point de xalain, et le lassa ensi .i. termine; et li comanda qu’il ne la desliast mie; et demora ensi que li jambe fut toute enflee et li piez et vint a perdition.	And there was another doctor who treated a duke of our land who had his leg broken, and with the break there was a wound; and the doctors in ignorance set the break above the wound by strong force, and did not leave any splint at the wound, and left it in this state; and he commanded that it should not be released; and it remained like this until the leg swelled completely and the feet came to ruin.
Je fuis apelez por venir a lui, et me hastai por venir deslier la jambe; et quant je l’oi desloie si fut em pais et ne sentit point de dolor.	I was summoned to come to him, and I hurried to come and release the leg; and when I released it, it was peaceful and felt no pain.
Mais toute voie li corruptions estoit ja confermee ou membre, et ne la poi saner; et ne cessa li corrution d’aler par le membre tant que li membres fut dou tout perdus.	But the corruption of the limb was already confirmed and could not be healed; and the corruption did not stop going through the limb until the entire limb was destroyed.
Et vis .i. autre mire qui effondra .i. apostume enchancreit, et puis enflama per le malice de sa signorie.	And a second person who collapses an abscess, enlarges it, and then sets it on fire due to the wickedness of his authority.
Car chancre, quant il est purs d’umor melancolique, ne covient mie qu’on i(l) touche de fer s’il n’est en teil leu c’on puisse toute oster ce que est corrumpus.	For a chancer, when it is filled with melancholic humor, one must not touch it with iron unless it is in such a place that all can be removed that has been corrupted.
Et por ceu, treschier filz, vos est besoig que vos sachiez que oevre de mains est devisee en .ij. divisions: c’est asavoir, huevre ou il a peril en plusors dispositions; et je mostrerai en chescun leu de cest livre ou il a paour et peril.	And for this reason, dear son, it is necessary that you know that the work of hands is divided into two divisions: one in which there is danger in many positions; and I will show in each part of this book where there is fear and danger.
Por coi il est besoig que vos vos en gardez, si que li fol mire ne puissent mal parler de vos.	Because it is necessary that you take care of yourself, so that foolish people cannot speak ill of you.
Si prenez vos armes en cusenson, et entreprenez vos malaides legierement et fermement, et usez de la millor voie si que per la graice de Deu vos venez a salut et soiez loez; et lassiez les maladies espoantables de grief saniteit; et ostez vos armes de ceu que vos fait douter, et aiez foit en vos si que vos puissiez venir de cestui monde a l’autre de gloire.	Take your weapons in custody, and begin with your patients gently but firmly, and use the best method so that by God's grace you come to salvation and be praised; leave aside diseases full of great suffering; remove your weapons from that which causes doubt, and have faith within you so that you can come from this world to the other of glory.
Galiens dist en aucuns de ses amonestemens: «Ne prenez mie en cure male maladie, que vos ne soiez apelez fol mire.»	Galen warns in some of his admonitions: "Do not take care of evil disease, lest you be called a foolish man."
J’ai deviseit cest traitier selonc .iij. chapitres.	I have devised this treatment according to three chapters.
Li premiers chapitres est des cauteres de feu et dé cauteres de medicine ague, et est li chapitres ordenez de lou chief jusques as piez; et des formes des estrumens, et des ferremens de cautere, et de tout ceu qui est necessaire en l’ueuvre.	The first chapters are on fire cauteries and counter-cauteries for ague, and they are arranged from head to foot; also concerning the shapes of instruments, and the tools for fire cautery, and everything necessary in this work.
Li secons chapitres si est de taillier et de percier, et des ventouses et des plaies, et des estractions des saiettes, et des semblans choses; et est li chapitres ordenez et les formes des estrumens.	The second chapters are about cutting and piercing, and about draining and wounds, and the extraction of arrows, and similar things; also arranged and concerning the shapes of instruments.
Li tiers chapitres est de restorer les dislocations et des torcions, et des semblans choses; et est ordeneiz des lou chief jusc’as piez, et des formes des estrumens.	The third chapter is about restoring dislocations and twists, and similar things; it is ordered from the head down to the feet, and the forms of the instruments.
Ainsois que nos nos remembriens de l’uevre, il covient que je die la qualiteit de l’aide et dou nuisement de chescune complexion.	Furthermore, as we remember of the work, it is necessary that I tell you the quality of the aid and the harm of each complexion.
Je dis que li qualiteis de l’aide, et dou nuisement, est li plus longe parole et subtilz science et li secrez reponus; et de ceu parlerent li plusors des saiges, et s’acorderent a ceu; et me soffisent poc lor paroles, car je redous la longesce.	I say that the qualities of the aid and harm are the longest words and subtle science and secret answers; and many wise ones spoke of this, and agreed on it; and they do not satisfy much by their words, for I will shorten the length.
Je dis que cautere aide universement a toute complexion ou il a matiere, fuer que .ij. complexions: c’est a savoir complexion chaude sens matere, et complexion seche sens matere.	I say that cautery helps universally in all constitutions where there is matter, whether it be of the two constitutions: namely hot constitution with matter, and dry constitution with matter.
En complexion chaude et seche ensamble matiere, deviserent aucun et dirent que cautere i est grans aide; et li autre dirent le contraire: que cautere ne vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de sechour.	In the hot and dry constitution along with matter, some have spoken and said that cautionery is of great help; and others say the opposite: that cautionery is not useful for disease caused by heat and dryness.
Car li nature dou feu si est chaude, et ne doit mie estre cureiz de chaude maladie par chalor, ne per sechour; et dist cil qui dist lou contraire que cautere fait grant aide a maladie chaude et seche que vient en cors des homes.	For the nature of fire is hot, and should not be used to cure a hot disease by heat or dryness; and he who said the opposite stated that cautionery provides great help for hot and dry diseases in human bodies.
Car quant tu comperes le cors de l’ome et sa moistor a la complexion dou feu, tu trueves le cors froit.	For when you examine the body of man and its heat to the complexion of fire, you find the body cold.
Et je m’acorde a ceste parole.	And I agree with this statement.
Car je l’ai troveit aucune fois per experiment.	For I have found it to be true on one occasion through experience.
Et toute voie, ne s’en entremette mie fuers que cil qui l’a esproveit, et qui conoit par lonc usaige le chapistre des cauteres, et la diversiteit des complexions des homes, et les dispositions et les causes de lor maladies, et les sorvenues et l’espaice dou tens; des autres complexions n’avons nos mie paour, meismement em maladies froides et moistes.	And every way, do not interfere unnecessarily except for those who have tested it and know through long experience the chapter of cauterizations, and the diversity of the complexions of men, and their dispositions and causes of illnesses, and the occurrences and duration of time; we are not afraid of other complexions, especially in cold and moist illnesses.
Et tuit li mire s’asemblerent et s’acorderent au cautere.	And all the attendants assembled and agreed upon the cautery.
Et sachiez, filz, que cautere ensamble feu si est des secrez des cures, et de plus grant bonteit que cautere de medicine ardant.	And know, son, that a fire cautery is one of the secrets of healing, and of greater goodness than a burning medicine cautery.
Car li feus est simples, et ne vient mie fuers que au membre qui est cuis, et ne nuit a autre membre se poc nom.	For fire is simple, and it affects only the member that is burned, and it harms no other member unless named.
Les medicines ardans vienent de membre a autre en aloignant, et font venir au membre maladies de grief sanation; et par aventure ocit lou malaide.	Burning medicines come from one member to another in spreading, and they bring diseases of severe healing to the sick member; and perhaps they kill the patient.
Li feus por sa hautece et por la bonteit de sa substance ne fait mie ceu, s’il n’i a superfluiteit.	The fire for its high temperature and the goodness of its substance does not do it if there is no excess.
Et ceu vos ai je troveit par experiment et par la longesce dou servise et de l’estude que j’ai mis en l’art, et esteit sus la verteit des choses; et por ceu je m’escuse de la longesce de la parole, car il ne me plait mie que je vos oste le secreit qui est reponus ou feu, et la qualiteit de l’uevre, coment il deboute les maladies des cors, si com li philosophe le dit en demostrant; or le recevez en vos pensees.	And this I have found by experience and through the length of service and study that I have put in the art, and it was above the truth about things; and for this reason, I excuse myself from the length of speech, since I do not want to deprive you of the secret which is hidden concerning fire, and the quality of the work, how it vanquishes diseases of the body, as the philosopher says in demonstration; now receive it in your thoughts.
Et sachiez, fil, que il s’acorderent en quel tens doient estre faites les cauteres, et eslirent prientens.	And know, son, that they agreed on what time the cauteries should be performed and chose companions.
Et je dis que cautere est covenable en tous tens, por ceu que li nuisemens sorvenans est desoz mis par l’aide dou cautere; et meismement se li cauteres est por dolors necessaires fors et hastans que ne puent atendre le tens que plus grans malice ne veigne au membre.	And I say that cautery is appropriate in all times, because the harm occurring is hidden below with the help of cautery; and especially if the cauteries are necessary for pain that cannot be delayed until a greater evil may come to the member.
Et n’i pensez onques, chier fil, si com font li fol mire; car a la maladie qui est sanee par cautere n’a point de revenue; et il le dient ensi; mais il n’est mie si com il cuident, por ce que cauteres nen est que medicine qui mue la complexion, et seche les humors que sont cause de la dolor, et vaut mues que medicine por le hastement de sa valor, et por la vertut de son oevre et de sa signorie.	Do not ever think, dear child, as the foolish do; for a sickness that is healed by cautery has no return; and they say it thus; but it is not so as they believe, because cauteries are not only medicine that changes the complexion, but also dries up the humors that cause pain, and its power is quicker than medicine, and by the virtue of its work and authority.
Et possans chose est que li maladie viegne aucune fois selonc la complexion dou malaide et lou leu de la maladie et sa vertut; et sont assemblees en lui les superfluitez par l’aquisition des viandes et des semblans choses, se ce n’est cauteres administrez em leu ou il ait poc de superfluitez et de moistor, si com cauteres de dens por la dolor, et les semblans choses, et teil dolor ne revient mie; mais ce avient poc.	And sometimes the sickness comes according to the complexion of the patient and the nature of the disease and its power; and superfluidities are collected within it by the consumption of foods and similar things, unless cauteries are administered in that location where there is little superfluity and moisture, such as cauteries for pain, and similar things; but this does not prevent the pain from returning, but it happens rarely.
Et mout de gens n’entendent mie por coi cauteres est apelez li derriens de medecine, et c’est voir; mais il ne croient mie que cauteres vaille aprés medicine, mais lor ententions est fause, et est cauteres li derriens de medicine por ceu que quant nos aministrons manieres de cures en aucune maladie et elles ne valent, adonc administrons nos le cautere, et il vaut.	And many people do not understand why cauteries are called the rear of medicine, but this is true; however, they do not believe that cauteries are useful after medicine, but their beliefs are false, and cauteries are the rear of medicine because when we administer methods of cure in any disease and they do not work, then we administer cautery, and it works.
Adonques apert bien que cauteres est li derriens de medicine, ne mie selonc l’entention des folz mires.	Therefore, it is clear that cauteries are the rear of medicine, not according to the beliefs of foolish masters.
Li ancien dirent que cauteres d’estrument d’or est muedres que de fer, et ne dirent ceu fuers que por la qualiteit de l’or et por la hautece de sa substance; et dirent que li leus de cautere ne fait mie porriture, mais ceu n’est mie voir car je l’ai esprovei, et ai troveit que c’est voir en aucuns homes; et cauteres d’or vaut mues que de fer, si com il lou dirent.	The ancients said that cauteries made of gold are more effective than iron, and they did not say this because of the quality of gold or the nobility of its substance; rather, they said that the metal of a cautery does not promote pus, but this is not true, for I have tested it, and found that it is true in some men; and cauteries made of gold are more effective than iron, as they say.
Et toutevoie quant tu chaufes estrument d’or, tu ne seis mie quant il est chaus par la color de l’or, et s’est tantost refroidiez; et s’on le chaufe trop; si font au feu; et ensi i a assez d’empechement.	And in any case, when you heat [something] intensely with gold, you do not know when it is heated by the color of the gold, and soon it cools down; and if it is overheated, it burns; thus there is enough hindrance to it.
Et por ce usons nos de cautere de feir que nos l’avons mues apparilliet a nostre oevre.	And for that reason, we use the fire cautery which has been fitted to our work.
Or vos ai ordeneit cest chapitre des lou chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que li voie soit plus legiere a trover.	Here I order you this chapter on the head down to the feet, so that the way is easier to find.
dou cautere olivaire	Hot oil cautery
Cist cauteres vaut a moistor et a froidor sus lou cerveil, et en i a dous c’on fait par la cause d’une maladie qui est apelee «soda», et par la cause de maintes humors qui dessendent dou chief as eulz, et as oreilles, et por multitude de songes et dolor de dens et dolor de gorge, et meismement a toutes maladies qui vienent de froidor si com paralisie et sode et apoplexie et semblans maladies.	This cautery is beneficial for both heat and cold in the brain, and it is used to treat a disease called "soda," and various humors that descend from the head to the eyes, ears, and numerous dreams and pain in teeth and throat, and similarly for all diseases caused by cold such as paralysis, soda, apoplexy, and similar diseases.
Li forme de cest cautere si est que li malaides soit espurgiez par medicine solutive mondifiant le chief .iij. nuis ou .iiij., selonc ceu que li vertus et li eaige et li acostumance dou malaide le puet soffrir; et puis fai rere lou chief dou malaide.	The form of this cautery is that the patient is purged with a soluble medicine, cleansing the head for three or four days, according to what the patient's strength and the medicine's properties and the patient's accustomed can bear; then heat is applied to the back of the patient's head.
Et puis le fai seoir croisiet entre tes mains, et mettre ses mains sor som peis; aprés met la racine de ta palme sus la racine de son neis entre ses .ij. eulz; et lai ou venra tes dois moiens, si saigne d’enche puis eschaufe le cautere qui est apelé «olivare», de coi ci est li forme:	And next make the patient sit cross-legged between your hands, and place his hands on a pillow; afterwards, place the root of your palm on the root of his penis between his two eyes; and where your thumbs meet, it will bleed. Then heat the cautery called "olivare", which is described here:
Et le met sor le leu signiet d’encre, et fai en dessendant et en estraignant ta main poc et poc en trestornant; puis lieve ta main isnelement, et rewarde le leu se tu vois l’os .i. sol petit; et se tu ne lou vois, si rencomence le cautere tant que tu voies l’os si com je lou t’ai dit; aprés pren .i. poc de seil, et met en awe et molle coton dedens, et met sor le leu, et li laisse .iij. jors; aprés met sus cotun moilliet en burre; et laisse sus tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés cure la plaie de l’oignement qui est apelez «tetrafarmaçon», tant qu’il soit sanez.	And put it on the place where it bleeds, and draw and tighten your hand little by little while turning it; then remove your hand immediately, and look at the place to see if you see a small bone; and if you don't see it, continue heating the cautery as I have told you until you see the bone. Then take one pouce of oil, put it in soft and warm cotton within, and put it on the place, and leave it for four days; then put moist cotton over it; and let it remain until the burning is removed; afterwards, heal the wound with the ointment called "tetrafarmaçon" until it heals.
Et se dirent li ancien, que quant plus demoure overte li plaie, plus s’espurge; et por ce si aide mues.	And the ancients said that when a wound remains open longer, it purges more; and because of this, they aid movement.
Et dirent aucun de ces que on doit tant lassier le cautere que partie de l’os soit arse, et puis rese on ceu qui est ars de l’os, et soit curez.	And they said to some that the fire cautery should be left so long that a part of the bone is burned, and then reset the burnt part of the bone, and heal it.
Et dient li autre c’on doit le cautere tant lassier sus, et bouter si fort c’on abaite de l’os ausi large comme .i. vertoil que les femmes mettent en lor fusez por ceu que les humors issent mues hors; et doit on lassier la plaie longement overte; aprés le doit on curer et sodeir.	And they said to the others that the cautery should be left so long and pushed in as deeply as a verduil, which are the width of women's needles because the humors come out moist; and then it should be left open for a long time; afterwards, it should be healed and sutured.
Et ces .ij. manieres de cauteres ne me semblent mie estre bones dou tout en tout, fuers qu’en aucuns homes ou il ait voie de paor; et mues me semble que je lou doie laissier; car li chiés li est afoiblis par les solutions continuees de nature, si com nos le tesmoignons ens autres membres; et meisme quant li chiés dou malaide est foibles par nature, et li premiere semblance de cautere est plus salve et muedre por moi, et de celi use je oevre en donques emsamble salut.	And these two methods of cautery do not seem good to me in all things, except for those with fear; and it seems to me that I should leave them; because the chies are weakened by continuous solutions of nature, as we have seen in other members; and also when the chies of the sick person are weak by nature, the first appearance of cautery seems more beneficial and useful to me, and from this usage, I work for salvation.
de l’anciainne dolor dou chief	From the ancient pain of the head
Quant en tout le chief vient dolor croniques, et dure longement, si doit user li malaides yeris et pilules qui sont apelees «cochie», et d’espurgement de chief et d’oiles et d’emplastres; et s’on li fait le cautere que nos avons devant dit, et il ne vaut.	When chronic and long-lasting pain comes in the head, the patient should use wormwood and pills called "cochie", and of purges for the head and oils and plasters; and if they do the fire cautery as we have said before, it is not worthwhile.
Pren warde se li chiés dou malade est de fort nature, et qu’il ne soit trop froit; adonques le cauterize desoz celui cautere un poc que nos avons dit desus.	Take care that the patient's head is of strong nature and not too cold; then cauterize it with a little bit more of the cautery than we have said before.
Aprés fai cautere sus chescune corne dou chief jusc’a l’os, si com devant avons dit, et fai .i. cautere ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz»; et est .i. leus en coi on met ventouses; et alige ta main si que tu ne voises mie jusc’a l’os: li malaides sent trop plus grant dolor en cest cautere que as autres, et je em parlerai aillors; et covient que li cauteres des cornes soient plus subtis que cil dont on cautere la moieneteit dou chief, et c’est li forme:	After doing the cautery on each corner of the head as we have said before, and do one cautery or two called "vasselz"; there is one leek in which ventouses are put; align your hand so that you do not see up to the bone: the patient feels much more pain in this cautery than in others, and I will speak of it later; and the cauteries on the corners should be more subtle than those done on the middle part of the head, and this is its shape:
dou cautere dou chief	The fire cautery of the head
Quant en une partie dou chief vient dolor sodaine, et est estendue li maladie jusc’a l’oil, et li chiés est espurgiez par medicines mondifians, et on a fait les autres cures que j’ai dit en la division des maladies, et tout ceu ne profite mie: adonques li fai cauteres selonc .ij. manieres, c’est a savoir de medicine ague et de feir.	When sudden pain occurs in one part of the head, and the illness extends to the oil, and the head is purged by medicines that cleanse, and other treatments have been performed as I have said in the division of diseases, and all this does not help: then cauteries are applied according to two methods, namely with medicine that burns and with fire.
Li cauteres de medicine ague si est que tu preignes une doce d’alz, et oste l’escorce et le recope .i. poc as .ij. chiés, et puis fent la temple ou li dolor tient en teil maniere que tu puisses reponre la doce d’alz desoz le cuir; et quant elle sera reponuee si le lie et l’estraint bien et le laisse ensi .xij. houres; et puis le deslie et trait fuers la doce d’ail, et laisse la plaie ensi .ij. jors ou .iij.; puis met sus cotun plongiet en burre tant que porreture en isse.	The cautery by burning medicine is as follows: take a piece of aloes and remove the bark and cut it into two halves, one for each cheek, then make an incision in the temple where the pain is in such a way that you can place the aloe under the skin; and when it is placed, hold it firmly and leave it for twelve hours; then release it and apply the juice of the garlic to the aloe-wound, leaving the wound for two or three days; then put cotton dipped in butter on it.
Aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues si fai ceu d’aucunes medicines comburans que j’ai escrites ou dozime traitier des medicines comburans.	After the application of ointment until it is healed; and if you see that such burning medications, which I have written or twelfth treat the burning medications, are used.
Li cautere de fer si est selonc ceste meniere. Chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	The fire cautery is of this kind. Heat the cauter iron to the shape:
Et est apelez «clos» por ceu que li chief est fait a la forme d’un clo ou il ait .i. poc de corbeure, et em mileu a une petite apparance; et le met sor le leu dolorous, et tien ta main et trestorne le feir un poc legierement, tant que li moitiez de l’espés dou keur soit arse; et lieve ta main que li artere n’arde, que est defuers, et decorre habundance de sanc.	And it is called "closed" because the tip is shaped like a claw or has about one finger of curvature, and in the middle it appears small; and place it on the painful spot, and hold your hand and make the iron pierce slightly, until half of the thickness of the desired depth is burned; remove your hand so that the artery does not burn, which is outside, and let abundant blood flow.
Aprés met coton en awe de seil, et met sor le leu par .iij. jors; puis i met coton moilliet em burre, et puis cure le leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vuelz cauterize ceste emigraine avec le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare», a tout la pointe, et te garde de coper l’artere en ceste emigraine qui n’est mie anciaine.	After placing cotton on the wound, leave it for 3 days; then put dampened cotton in butter, and afterwards cure the wound with ointment until it is healed; and if you wish to cauterize this migration with the cautery called "cultellare", at the tip of the blade, be careful not to hit the artery in this migration which should not be old.
de emigraine	from the migration
Quant tu cures emigraine si com nos avons devant dit en divisions des maladies, et ne profite mie, et vois que li cauteres devant dis de la medicine et dou fer ne li soffit mie, adonques covient il que tu eschaufes le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare» tant qu’il soit blans; et seigne ainsois sor le leu doillant une ligne de demi doi de lonc, et oste ta main une fois, et l’estrain que tu ne coper l’artere et que ne viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde de la mandibule que muet quant on menjut, et li ners n’ait regart que la muet et que spasmus ne veigne a malaide, et te warde de decorrement de sanc de l’artere quant elle sera copee, ou copement ait grant paour et meismement a celui que ne s’i conoit, et qui n’est estudians et esprovez; et laisse l’uevre em mi voie; mais je vos dirai coment on restainche sanc quant li artere est copee, et je vos mostrerai a leu ou il afiert en cest livre.	When curing migration as we have previously said in the division of diseases and it does not improve, and you see that cauterization beforehand does not help at all, then it is necessary to heat the cautery called "cultellare" until it becomes white; and hold it against the side of the wound for half a finger's length, and press once with your hand, ensuring not to hit the artery or reach the bone; be careful not to damage the jaw that cannot move when eating, and not to irritate nerves, nor for spasms to come to the patient, and beware of arterial blood leakage when it is cut, or fear greatly, especially those who do not know it, and are not studied and experienced; leave the procedure in progress; but I will tell you how to stop the bleeding when the artery is cut, and I will show you where it should be done in this book.
Et se tu vois que cist cauteres ne soffise mie a la maladie, et li malaides est soffrans, cauterize le enmi le chief ausi com nos avons dit, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et se tu vues, aministre le cautere que nos avons dit ou chapistre de l’estraction de l’artere, avec le cautere qui ait .ij. coutelz; et est cist cauteres millors de celui et plus aidans.	And if you see that this cautery does not help the illness and the patient is suffering, cauterize it near the neck as we have said, and treat the wound until it heals; and if you see, administer the cautery that we have said in the chapter on artery extraction, with a cautery having two blades; this cautery is better than that one and more helpful.
de la dolor des oreilles de part froidor	of the pain from the ears due to coldness
Quant en l’oreille vient dolor de froit, et on i a ovreit de medicines solutives et des autres cures que nos avons dit en la division, et li dolors ne se muet, adonques eschaufe cest cautere qui est apelez «poins», de coi ci est li forme:	When the pain in the ear due to coldness persists despite medications and other treatments as we have said in the division, then heat this cautery called "poins" according to its form:
Aprés pointoie tout entor l’oreille malaide, ou entor les .ij. se la dolor tient en ambedous, et t’esloigne un poc ensus de la racine de l’oreille puis que tu as signiet le leu d’enche; et ait .x. poins entor chescune oreille; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	After marking all around the sick ear, or around the two where the pain is present in both, move away slightly from the root of the ear as you have indicated the spot; and place ten marks around each ear; after curing the spot until it heals.
de la torture de la bouche	of the torture of the mouth
Torture qui doit estre curee par cautere nen est fuers que de celles que muevent de fleume, si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladie; et ne faire point de cautere as semblances que vienent de sechor et de spame de ners.	A torture that is to be cured by cautery is not applicable to those that move due to phlegm, as we have said in the divisions of diseases; and do not perform a cautery on the similar conditions that come from secretion and spasm of nerves.
Quant tu cures ceste semblance de torture qui muet de fleume d’ydres et d’espurgemens de chief et de gargarisme, et ceu ne vaut, adonc covient que tu cauterizes le malaide de .iij. cauteres: l’une en la racine de l’oreille, et l’autre un poc defuers la temple, et le tier en l’ajostement des .ij. levres; et met le cautere en la partie qui apert saine, et li fai cautere endroit le chief de l’oreille desus un poc desoz la corne dou chief, et un autre en la temple ausi longe com uns poce; et laisse le cautere tant sus que li moitiez dou keur soit arse; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	When you treat this type of torture that stems from the flow of idres and purges of the head and throat, which is not effective, then you must cauterize the patient with three cauteries: one in the root of the ear, another slightly beyond the temple, and the third at the corner of the lips; place the cautery in the healthy part and make it cauterize near the top of the ear a little below the skull's horn, and another in the temple as long as a finger; leave the cautery until the middle of the charcoal is burned; and this is the shape of the cautery:
Et est li semblance dou cutellaire que nos avons mise devant, mais il est un poc plus subtilz et covient que li coutelz soit un poc plus gros; aprés cure lou leu si com j’ai devant dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And this is the shape of the scalpel that we have mentioned, but it is slightly more subtle and the blades should be a bit thicker; after curing the wound as I have previously said, ensure it is healed.
Quant apoplexie est ancieinne et tu la cures ensi com nos avons dit, et il ne profite mie, et li malaides n’ait fievre, adonques li fai .iiij. cauteres: .ij. sus les .ij. cornes dou chief, et .i. emmi le chief, et .i. ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz» si com nos avons devant dit, et lou derrien cautere sus la bouche de l’estomac; et soit curez si com nos avons dit devant.	And if apoplexy is long-standing and you treat it as we have said, but it does not help, and the patient has no fever, then make four cauteries: two on the two horns of the head, one in the middle of the head, and one where the wound is called "vasselz" as we have mentioned before, and the last cautery on the mouth of the stomach; cure it as we have said before.
de litargie	of cautery
A cest maladie covient doner au malaide yeres grans et pilules mondifians le cerveil; aprés reis lou chief dou malaide tout, et li met sus l’occipite l’emplaustre de sinapi qui est escrit ou traitier des emplastres; et c’est li maniere dou cautere: si lou fai si com j’ai dit.	For this disease, give the patient large year and pills made of refined cereal; then anoint the head of the patient with a plaster made of mustard seed, which is written or explained in the plasters chapter; and this is the method of cautery: if you do it as I said.
S’il est sanez ensi, boin est; et s’il ne l’est, se li fai .iij. cauteres des emmi le chief en dessendant jusc’a col, et ait d’espaice entre chescun cautere .i. doi de gros; et le cure si com les autres, et se tu i vues ajoster, et li malaides est soffrans, se li fai .i. cautere en mileu; et se mestiers est, .ij. autres sus les .ij. cornes, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare», si com j’ai devant dit.	If it is healthy, it is good; and if not, make him undergo four cauteries of emmer at the head starting from the neck and leaving a space of two fingers between each cautery; and treat as with other diseases, and if you see any improvement, apply one cautery in the middle; and if necessary, apply two more on the temples, and treat until it is healthy; and let the cautery that is called "olive oil" be as I have previously said.
de la froidor dou chief	From the coldness of the head
Il covient que li chief soit mundifiez de yeres et de ceu que nos avons devant dit; aprés reis le chief dou malaide, puis li fai cautere emmi le chief et sus chescune corne, et .i. derrier et .iij. sus l’espinee dou col; et se tu en as plus mestier, et li cors est moiste et li malaides est soffrans, et li maladie est fors, se li fai .iiij. cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos; et li laisse tant que li plus dou keur soit ars, et lieve ta main; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare» que nos avons devant dit.	The head of the patient should be cleansed for years and as we have previously said; after that, cleanse the head of the sick man, then make a cautery in the head and one on each horn, and one behind and three on the spine of the neck; and if you need more, and the body is wet and the sick person is enduring pain, and the disease is out, make four cauterizations on the spine of the back; let it burn until the most painful part is burnt, then rinse your hand; afterwards, cure him until he is healthy, and let the cautery that is called "olivare" as we have previously said.
de l’epilempsie	From the epilepsy
Li epilentiques ne doit useir de cautere fuers que cil qui est fleumatique, et covient premier mondifier le cerveil de yeres et d’autres cures que nos avons dites en la division quant li malaides est grans et soffrans de penre medicine.	Epilentics should not use fire cautery except for those who are fleumatic, and it is necessary first to purify the brain of years and other treatments that we have mentioned in the division when the patient is old and suffers from taking medicine.
Et se c’est uns enfes qui ne lou puisse soffrir, se li fai gargarisme et mastication mondifiant le cerveil sovent avec bones viandes; aprés li reis lou chief em mileu, et i fai .i. cautere selonc ce que nos avons dit devant, et .i. cautere sus lou vassel, et sus chescune corne; et se li malaides est fors et soffrans, se li fai cauteres si com j’ai dit a celui qui ait paralisie et mollification de cors, sus l’espinee dou dos et dou col, et soit li cauteres olivier selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	And if it is an infant who cannot endure it, make gargarism and frequent mastication for purifying the brain with good foods; afterwards rub the head well, and make one cautery according to what we have said earlier, and one cautery on the navel, and on each horn; and if the patient is out of breath and able to endure it, make cauteries as I have said to him who has paralysis and softening of the body, on the spine of the back and the neck, and let the cauteries be olive-shaped according to the manner that I have said.
Se li malaides est enfes, se li fai .i. cautere subtil selonc ceste maniere:	If the patient is an infant, make one subtle cautery in this manner:
Quant par la cause de melancolie sunt les superfluitez ou les moistors corrumpues et fleume grosse, adonques lou cauterize de teils cauteres com nos avons dit a celui qui ait paralisie.	When due to melancholy there are excessive or corrupt humors and thick phlegm, then the fire cautery of such cauteries should be applied as we have said to those with paralysis.
Et se par la cause de melancolie est li superfluitez declinans a melancolie, et est li cors dou malaide moistes, adonc li done a boivre chose par coi li cervelz soit mundifiez, selonc ceu qu’il est devant en la division.	And if due to melancholy the humors are declining towards melancholy and the body of the patient is moist, then give them something to drink by which the brain may be cleansed, as has been described before in the divisions.
Aprés reis lou chief dou malaide; aprés fai .i. torteil de lin bien fait, ausi com .i. cercle, si le met emmi le chief; et li malaides sié croisiez, et soit bien tenus de toutes pars; aprés presente le linement, et vaut mues de burre de berbis ancien; et lou chaufe a feu tempreement, si que li dois s’on li boute le puisse soffrir; aprés vuide le cercle par dedens emmi le chief, et lou laisse refroidier; et fai ce a malaide chescune semaine une fois avec autre governement boin, tant qu’il soit sanez.	After the king (the physician), make one linen bandage well made, like a circle, and place it around the head of the patient; cross the patient, and keep them well held from all sides; then apply the leech, which is worth mullein root of old age; heat it gently so that the patient can bear it; then empty the circle from within the head, and let it cool; do this to the patient once a week with good governance until they are healed.
Ou se tu vues cauterize lou en faisant poins plusors a tot le cautere. Ceste maniere de cautere amoistit le cerveil igaument; et puis met sus coton moilliet en burre et en graisse de geline.	If you wish to perform cauterization, make multiple pricks all over the cautery. This method of cauterizing helps the brain greatly; then place moistened cotton in butter and linseed oil on top.
de l’awe des eulz	of the eyes
Quant awe vient premierement as eulz par les signes que j’ai dit en la division, adonques encomence et done boivre au malaide chose mundifiant le chief, et le warde de toutes moistors, et lou fai suer ou bain plusors fois a jeun.	When the eyes come first with the signs that I have mentioned in the division, then begin and give the patient something cleansing the head, keeping it away from all moisture, and make him sweat or bathe multiple times while fasting.
Aprés li comande a rere son chief, et li fai cautere emmi le chief, et li fai .ij. cauteres sus les .ij. temples se li dessendemens de l’awe est as .ij. eulz ensamble, ou en .i. se li dessendemens est en .i.; et cope a tout le cautere toutes les voines et les arteres que sont desoz le keur, et soient li cautere lonc selon lou large de la temple; et te warde de decorrement de sanc, et se tu vois trop de sanc issir, si li estainche de teil pooir com tu as.	After the patient bends backwards, have a fire cautery applied to his head, and make two cauteries on the two temples where the wound is located or where there are two wounds together; or if there is only one wound, apply the cautery to it. Close all the veins and arteries beneath the skull with the cautery, and let the cautery be long according to the width of the temple; be careful not to let blood flow out, and if you see too much blood flowing, stop it as you are able.
Et je t’enseignerai en l’estraction des arteres et a l’incision la cautele coment tu l’estencheras; et aucune fois fait on cautere ou hatereil desoz les .ij. os derrier.	I will teach you in the extraction of arteries and incision of the cautery how to stretch it; sometimes a fire cautery or some other instrument is made under the two bones at the back.
dou cors des larmes	the heart of tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont ancienes et acostumees et sont sus les voines, ou delez les arteres que sont en l’aparance dou chief defors; et on voit que c’est des superfluitez froides fleumatiques, adonques li fai le cautere que j’ai dit en l’encomencement de l’awe dessendant as eulz: .i. cautere emmi le chief, et .ij. cauteres sus les .ij. temples, et .ij. cauteres ou haiterel desoz les .ij. os; et s’il i a besoigne plus, si le cauterize saigement desus le sorcil a tout .i. petit cautere.	When the tears of the eyes are old and accustomed and are on the veins, or open the arteries that appear outside the head; and it is seen that this is excess cold fluid, then do the cauterization that I have mentioned at the beginning of the awe descending to the eyes: i.e., cauterize in the head, and 2 cauteries on the 2 temples, and 2 cauteries where the temples are below the 2 bones; and if necessary, cauterize skillfully over the eye with a small cautery.
dou cors des larmes par dedens les eulz	inside the body of the eyes
Quant tu le medicines selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et il ne profite mie, adonques done a boivre a malaide .iij. nuis cochies; aprés li reis le chief, et li fai cautere ou mileu dou cautere olivaire; et fai .ij. cauteres dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis» sus les .ij. sorcis, un poc desoz les chevous; et te warde de l’artere que tu ne la coper.	When you treat according to what we have said in the division, and it does not help, then give the patient 4 cooked roaches; after that, give him a head of cabbage or an olive oil cautery; and make 2 cauteries called "clavilis" above the eyebrows, a small amount under the hair; beware of the artery you do not cover.
Et c’est li forme dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis»:	And this is the shape of the cautery called "clavilis":
Quant li papiere de l’oil est mollifie de maladie et de moistor, adonques la cautarize de cest cautere qui est apelez «olivare». de coi ci est li forme:	When the paper of oil is softened by disease and moisture, then the cauterization of this cautery called "olivare" should be done. This is its shape:
Et se tu vues si fai .ij. cauteres sus les .ij. sorcis ausi lons com li sorcilz sont; et n’i lassiez mie la main fors que tant que li tierce partie de la papiere soit arse, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	And if you wish to do two cauterizations on the same two scorptions as long as they are; and do not leave the hand except when the third part of the paper is burned, according to the manner that I have said.
dou poil qui point l’oil	of the hair that pricks the oil
Aucune fois avient que li poil des oilz sont convertit au pardedens, et poignent l’oil, et i fait on cauteres selonc .ij. manieres: c’est a savoir de feu, ou de medicine ardant.	Sometimes the hairs of the eyes are converted to tears and prick the eye; and it makes fire or burning medication cauterization according to two methods: namely with fire or with medicine that is hot.
Ou cautere de feu comande au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient lons et igals; et s’il le poignent a lor nassance, se li estraint les eulz qu’il ne se muevent tant qu’il naissent.	For the fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Quant il naissent et i sont igalz, adonques met le malaide en ton sain; aprés seigne sus la papiere des eulz une figure que soit ausi com li fuelle dou mirte, et soit li comencemens dou signe delez les poilz; puis i met coton moilliet en glaire d’uef et muscillaige de persillion sus l’oil, puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When they have grown and are even, then place the patient on a clean surface; afterward, on top of the eyelashes, draw a figure like the fennel seed, and start from the base of the hairs; then put cotton soaked in egg white and musk oil over the eye, then heat the cautery with this form:
Aprés cauterize sus la figure que tu as signiet poc et poc mout de fois, que li keurs soit ars lai endroit; et li signes de la santeit de l’uevre est que tu voies la papiere retraite, et les poilz levez a la pointure de l’oil; adonques lieve ta main, et laisse ensi .iij. jors, puis i met coton moilliet en burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	After cauterizing the figure that you have pointed out several times, let the sores be burned in that place; and the signs of the healing of the wound are that you see the papyrus recede, and the hairs rise at the tip of the oil; then lift your hand, and leave it like that for 3 days, then put cotton soaked in butter until the burn is healed; after that, apply ointment until it is healed.
Et se aprés ceu vienent li poilz, et li papiere est mollifie adonques rencomence le cautere sus cel leu meisme, si com tu as fait premiers; et se li poil sont defuer, si le cauterize tant que li papiere soit levee a son leu natureil, et soit igals, et ne poignent mie li poil l’oil.	And if afterwards the hairs appear and the papyrus becomes soft, then start the cautery on that same place again, as you did before; and if the hairs are falling out, cauterize it until the papyrus rises to its natural level and is even, and the hairs do not prick at the oil.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient grans et igalz, puis fai de parchemin la forme de la foille de mirte; puis pren de savon fransois et de vive chalz, de chescun une .З., et broie ensamble bien; et le fai hastanment, si qu’il ne refroide, puis en espant sus la forme que tu es fait sicom la foille dou mirte, et met sus la papiere des eulz; et se li maladie tient en .i. oil soulement, si doit on ovrer en .i., et se en ambedous ausi; et met desoz l’oil coton moilliet en abin d’uef; et li chiés dou malaide soit en ton sain et met ton doi mostrant sus la medicine, et presse .i. poc et lou muef toutes les fois que li malaide sent mordication de la medicine, car il sent mordication ausi com de feu.	The burning medicine is that you instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even, then make a parchment in the shape of the myrtle leaf; then take French soap and hot chalk, of each one an ounce, and grind them together well; and make it quickly so that it does not cool, then spread it on the parchment in the same way as the myrtle leaf, and put the hairs on top; and if the patient has only one sore, it should be worked on one, and if both are affected; and place cotton soaked in egg white under the oil; and the patient's hand should be clean and place your finger showing over the medicine, and press a little and move all the time when the patient feels burning of the medicine, for it burns like fire.
Quant tu as ceu fait longement, si oste la medicine a ton doit.	When you have done this (i.e., dislocating the limb), apply the medicine to your shoulder.
Et quant li mordication sera passee, si leve le leu d’awe, et rewarde se tu vois la papiere levee ausi com s’ele estoit levee par constraignement de feu ou par incision; et s’il est ensi, si est bien. Se ceu non, si remet encor de la medicine sus lou leu ou li medicine n’ait ovreit, tant que tes ovraiges soit igalz, et tes eulz mis a point; puis met sus coton moilliet en burre tant que li keurs ars soit cheus, aprés cure le leu de l’oignement qui est apelez «dyafenis» et d’autre, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Once the dislocation has passed, lift up the limb and check if you see the paper lifted in the same way it was raised by heating or incision; if it is like this, then it is good. If not, apply more medicine on the shoulder or where the medicine hasn't worked yet, as long as your efforts are equal and your fingers are positioned correctly; then put cotton dampened in butter on top until the burns have healed, afterwards cure the limb with the ointment called "diaphenis" and others, until it is healthy.
Et se t’est mestier que tu te warde bien a ton ovraige par grant warde qu’il ne chiece point de la medicine as eulz.  Et se li papiere devient mole aprés, et li poil poignent en l’oil, si recomence la medicine sus celui leu qui est mollifiez de la papiere proprement, ensi com tu as fait devant; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme de la fuelle dou mirte:	And if it is necessary for you to guard yourself well at your work so that the medicine does not prick the eyes, and if the paper becomes soft afterwards, and the hairs prick in the oil, then restart the medicine on that limb which has been made moist by the paper properly, as you have done before; afterwards cure it until it is healthy; and this is the form of the fennel seed:
Et saichés que li eul des homes sont divers en grandor et en petitece, et selonc ceu soit tes constraignemens; et ne soit mie reponue li droite voie a celui cui est li estude de cest art.	And know that the eye of man is diverse in size and smallness, according to your constraints; do not deviate from the correct path for him who is studying this art.
de la cure de fistule par cautere	On the treatment of fistula by cautery
Quant tu cures fistule si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladies, et tes cures ne profitent mie, adonques covient il que tu li fais cautere selonc ceste maniere.	When you treat a fistula as we have said in the divisions of diseases, and your treatment does not help, then it is necessary that you perform cautery according to this manner.
Comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain; et teigne li menistres son chief entre tes mains en teil maniere qu’il ne se mueve, ne ne demoinne son chief; aprés met coton moilliet en abin d’uef ou en jus de persillion sus l’oil; aprés chaufe le cautere qui est teilz: et est chevez au chief si com li forme d’une penne de vouteul, ensamble la queil soit li cautere; se tu vues, si soit apointé des l’un chief dusc’a l’autre, et se tu vues, si soit ausi com une tente; mais toutevoie, cist qui est chevez vaut mues por ton ovraige.	Instruct the patient to place his head in your lap; and hold his head between your hands so that it does not move or turn aside; after that put cotton soaked in egg white or in jujube oil over the area; after heating the cautery, place it on the head in such a manner as the shape of a feather from a quill, together with the cautery itself; if you see, it should be pointed from one end to the other, and if you see, it should also be like a tent; but regardless, this which is placed on the head serves for your work.
Aprés presse la fistule s’ele est overte, et en trai la porriture, et la seche; et s’ele est close, si la oevre, et trai fuers la bowe; aprés met sus le cautere chaut forment, et tien ta main au cautere a la partie dou neif ensus de l’oil, que ta mains ne faice folie; et met le cautere en la graisse de l’oil, et la corromp.	After pressing the fistula if it is open, remove the pus and dry it; if it is closed, open it, remove the worms; after that place the hot cautery on top, and hold your hand on the cautery at the part of the neck near the oil, so your hands do not slip; and put the cautery in the oil fat and corrode it.
Se tu viens au comencement dou cautere jusc’a l’os, si serait bien. Se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere encor une fois, et autre se tu en as mestier, et le laisse .iij. jors; aprés i met sus coton moilliet en burre, et lou cure de l’oignement desiccatif tant qu’il soit sanez, et se .xl. jors passent qu’il ne soit sanez, si met sus medicine ague corrosive tant que li os soit descovers; et lou reis selonc ceu que il venrait en son chapistre.	If you start the cautery up to the bone, that is good. If not, continue the cautery again once and another if needed, and let it rest for 3 days; after that put soft cotton in butter on top and cure it with drying ointment until it is healthy, and if after 40 days it is still not healthy, put corrosive medicine on the bone as directed by your king according to his chapter.
Et i a une maniere de cautere de fistule que aucun des anciens dirent. Entens a fistule, et fens le leu; aprés met en la fendure .i. camahan subtil de coi ci est li forme:	And here is a method of cauterizing a fistula that none of the ancients said. Listen to the meaning of the word "fistula" and imagine it as if you were cutting it open, then put one subtle camphor stick (as follows in its form):
et i font a la quantiteit d’une .З. de plonc; et tien ta main ou camahan fermement, et ne se mueve li malaides nes point, que li plons fondus ne corre a son oil; et covient c’on mette sus l’oil a malaide coton moilliet en abin d’uefz ou en awe: li plonc si art lou leu de fistule, et lou saine per mervillouse saniteit.	And they apply the amount of a pound's weight; hold your hand or grip firmly, and let the patient not move at all, so that the lead does not scatter from its oil; it is necessary to put cotton moistened in egg white or oil on top of the oil of the patient: the lead will heal the wound, and the healthy part will recover marvelously.
Et se li fistule est sanee per le cautere que nos avons dit, c’est boin. Se ce non, si covient aministrer pertus au neif, et ramener la fistule au cors dou neif selonc ceu qu’il covient en som propre leu.	If the wound is healed by the cautery that we have said, it is good. If not, it is necessary to administer hot poultices and bring the wound back to the heat of the body as it should be in its own place.
des crevaices en levres	cavities in lips
Mout de fois avienent crevaices en levres que sont apelees «poil», et meismement en levres des enfans.	Often, cracks appear in lips which are called "hairs," and the same happens with children's lips.
Quant tu cures ces crevaices de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et li cure ne profite, adonques eschaufe .i. petit cautere cultellaire selonc ceste forme:	When curing these cracks as we have described in the sections above, and the treatment does not help, then heat a small cautery scalpel in this shape:
Et le met hastanment en celles crevaices tant qu’il viegne jusc’a font; aprés cure le leu de cerote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And apply it immediately to those cracks until it reaches the bottom, then treat the area with cerote (cerotum) until it is healed.
de l’aposteme de la goule	of the abscess of the neck
Quant apostume vient en la racine de la goule ou en l’uve, ou ou palais, ou as racines des dens, aprés fait porriture et ront et est enveillis et devient fistule; et tu le cures si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie: adonques covient il que tu aies .i. cautere selonc la quantiteit de la fistule; aprés le bote ou pertus de la fistule, et tien ta main tant que li fer chaus viegne au font de li, et ou derrien leu; et fai ensi une fois ou .ij., aprés le cure de ce que nos avons dit en cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est curez ensi, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si covient descovrir le leu et oster l’os corrumput, selonc ceu que vos le troverez en son chapistre.	When an abscess comes to the root of the throat or the eye, or the palate, or the roots of the teeth, after becoming pus-filled and growing and turning into a fistula; and you treat it as we have said in divisions, but it does not improve; then it is necessary that you have .i. cautery according to the size of the fistula; after closing or sealing the fistula, keep your hand until the iron becomes hot at its point and at its base; and do this once or twice, after treating as we have said in treatments, until it is healed; and if it is healed thus, it is good; and if not, then you must find the location and remove the rotten bone, according to what you will find in its chapter.
dou movement des dens	the slight movement of the teeth
Quant les gencives sont mollifies par moistor et les dens muevent, et tu le cures per medicines et ceu ne vaut, adonc met le chief dou malaide en ton sain; aprés eschaufe le cautere dont li forme venra ci aprés en teil maniere que tu mettes une cainne sor le dent; et met dedens le cautere chaut hastanment, et tien tant ta main que li malaides sente la chalor venant a la racine dou dent; aprés lieve ta main et rencomence le cautere selonc ta volenteit; aprés emplisse li malaides sa bouche d’awe salee, et la teigne une houre et raiche fuers.	When the gums are softened by moisture and the teeth move, and you cure it with medicine but that does not work, then put the head of the patient in your lap; after heating the cautery so that its form will come here in this manner: you place a cane on the tooth; and put the hot cautery inside immediately, and hold your hand until the patient feels the heat coming to the root of the tooth; after removing your hand, repeat the cautery as desired; after filling the patient's mouth with salt water and holding it for an hour, rinse thoroughly.
Et en teil maniere li dens qui estoit movans si est confermez, et li gencive mollifie restrainte, et li moistors corrumpue sechie.	And in this manner, the teeth that are moving should be immobilized, and the gums softened, and the moisture corrupt dried.
de la dolor des dens	of the tooth pain
Quant dolor de dens vient por froidor, ou il i a froidor ou veir, et les cures de medicine ne valent, adonc i ait mestier de cautere selonc .ij. manieres: et cautere de burre et cautere de feu.	When tooth pain comes from cold or there is cold or fever, and the remedies of medicine are of no use, then it is necessary to use cauterization according to two methods: cauterization with butter and cauterization with fire.
Cautere de burre si est telz que tu preignes burre de vaiche, et le bout en une cuillier de fer ou d’arain; aprés pren coton et envolope sus la pointe d’une tente, et la moille en burre bulit, et met sus le dent dolant hastanment et tien tant qu’il soit refroidiez; et ensi fai sovent tant que sa vertus viegne a la racine de la dent, et se tu vues si moille laine et coton en burre froit, et met sus le dent doillant, et met sus .i. fer chaut tant que li feus viegne au chevement dou dent.	Cauterization with butter is as follows: you take butter from a cow, and the end in a iron or copper spoon; afterwards take cotton and wrap it around the tip of a tent, and wet it in boiled butter, and put it on the painful tooth quickly and hold until it gets cold; and do this frequently until its effect reaches the root of the tooth, and if you see that the cotton and linen are wet with cold butter, put it back on the tooth, and put hot iron on top until the heat comes to the tooth's apex.
Li cauteres ensamble feu si est telz que tu preignes uns cainne de fer ou d’arain, et soit grosse si que li feus ne viegne a la bouche dou malaide; aprés chaufe le cautere, de coi li forme venra ci aprés, et le met sus le dent et tien ta main tant que li cauteres soit refroidiez; fai ceu sovent, car li dolor sera ostee celui jor meisme ou l’endemain. Et covient que li malaides emplisse sa bouche de boin burre en l’empressement de cel cautere, et puis le raiche fuer; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	The fire cautery is made with a rod of iron or steel, large enough that the heat does not reach the patient's mouth; heat the cautioner, causing the shape to come afterwards, and place it on the tooth and hold your hand until the cautioner is cooled; do this often, as the pain will be alleviated the same day or the next. It is necessary that the patient fills his mouth with good butter in the hurry of this cautery, and then blow hard; this is the shape of the cautery.
Et fai cautere dou queil chief que tu voudras, et selonc ceu que tu as pooir; et c’est li forme de la caine:	And make a cautery on whichever place you wish, and according to what you are able; this is the form of the rod.
des scrophules	of scrofula (scrofulous diseases)
Quant les scrophules sont de fleume et de moistors froides, et ne sont obeissans a digestion par medicines, adonques eschaufe le cautere cheveit de coi ci aprés vient li forme, et ait ij. aovertures por les fumees a issir au cautere de l’autre partie; et met le cautere chaut sus l’apostume une fois, ou .ij. se mestier est, tant qu’il viegne au font de l’apostume; et se li apostume est petis si met cautere selonc la quantiteit de l’apostume, et le laisse ensi .iij. jors; et met sus coton moilliet em burre tant que li arsure soit ostee; aprés cure le leu d’oignemens et de tentes tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the scrofulas are of fever and cold moisture, and do not respond to medicines for digestion, then heat the cautery comb as described next, make two holes for smoke to exit from the other part; place the hot cautery on the abscess once, or twice if needed, until it reaches the base of the abscess; and if the abscess is small, apply cautery according to the size of the abscess, and leave it thus for three days; then put soft cotton soaked in butter on it until the pus is gone; afterwards, treat the area with ointments and plasters until it heals.
Quant les moistors vainquent sus les chenals dou pormon, et meismement quant ce vient de froide complexion, adonc covient que li malaides soit voidiez premiers par medicines solutives; aprés li fai cautere a la racine de la gorge, et te garde que tu ne venir mie jusc’a la gorge, et n’ardre dou keur mais c’un poc. Aprés li fai .i. autre cautere a la jointure dou col au chief de l’espinee, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» de coi nos avons la forme devant; et cure le leu si com nos avons devant dit tant qu’il soit sanez.	When cold moisture prevails over the intestinal channels, and especially when it comes from a cold complexion, then the patient should first be cleansed with soluble medicines; afterwards, make a cautery at the root of the throat, but do not go up to the throat and be careful not to burn it too much; afterwards, make one other cautery at the joint of the neck to the head of the spine, and use the cautery called "clavile" as we have described before; and treat the area until it heals as we have said earlier.
de la toust	Toast (noun)
Quant tous et maladie de pormon sont de moistors froides, et li malaides nen ait fievre ne sechor, et est li maladie anciaine, se li fai ij cauteres sus la forcele en leus vuis; et .i. autre cautere emmi le pis entre .ij. mameles; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» selonc la forme qui est devant dite.	When all and diseases of worm are from cold moistures, and the patients do not have fever nor heat, and it is an old disease, make two fire cauterizations on the shoulder blades; and one other cauterization between the breasts; and let the cauterization that is called "clavile" according to the shape mentioned before.
Et se tu vues, fai cautere en poignant a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins» de coi li forme est ci devant en la maladie des oreilles; et soient li poins jusc’a .xxx., ou enqui entor. Aprés cure le leu selonc ceu qui est devant dit, et soit li cauteres a .iij. rains selonc ceste forme:	And if you see, make a cauterization by piercing the entire cauterization that is called "poins" of this shape in the disease of ears; and let the piercings be up to 30, or less around. After curing the side as mentioned before, let the cauterizations be at four intervals according to this shape:
Et por ceu sont li cautere plus legier, por ceu que tu en fais .iij. a cop.	And because these cauteries are lighter, because you make four of them.
de la dislocation de l’ajutoire	of the dislocation of the shoulder
Quant li chiés de l’ajutoire est desaloiez par cause de moistor, et on le remet a leu, et il n’i puet demorer ains revient adés et desalue par petit movement qui avient, si com nos avons esproveit, adonques covient il que tu ramoinnes la dislocation premierement.	When the head of the shoulder is dislocated due to moisture, and it is reset but cannot stay in place, repeatedly dislocating with slight movement as we have experienced, then you must first reset the dislocation.
Aprés soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos et sus son costeit; aprés lieve le keur qui est dedens le titillite as dois de ta main senestre; et se li jointure est desaluee dedens, si eschaufe le cautere qui a .ij. ners douqueil ci est li forme:	After placing the patient on their back and on their side; after feeling the cavity within the chest with your left hand, if the joint is dislocated inside, heat up the cautery of the shape shown below:
et cauterize lou keur tant qu’il le perce jusc’a costeit, et venrait li fugure dou cautere ensamble .iiij. cauteres; et por ceu est faite cautere avec le cautere qui a .iij. ners, por coi li figure de cauterization sunt sis cauteres; et sont li nerf selonc la subtiliteit d’une tente et c’est li forme dou cautere qui a .iij. ners:	And cauterize the pancreas up to the costal margin, and the figure of the cautery will come together with four cauteries; and this is made with the cautery that has three nerves, because the figures of cauterization are four cauteries; and these nerves are according to the subtlety of a tendon and this is the shape of the cautery that has three nerves.
Et aucune fois est ajostez sus ce .i. nerf por coi il i a .viij. cauteres.	And sometimes it is joined above this one nerve, because there are eight cauteries.
Aprés met sus le cautere porrelz broiez avec seil; aprés fai reposer le malaide, et ne soit meus li membres par lonc tens tant qu’il soit bien confortez.	Afterwards put on the cautery that is broken with silk; afterwards let the patient rest, and do not move the limbs for a long time until he is well comforted.
Et s’il est desaloiez desus, liquelz chose avient poc, adonques fait cautere sus l’epaisse dou cautere clavile, ou mout de cauteres en poignant. Car li jointure est refermee, et est ostee li moistor et est sanez li malaides.	And if it is dislocated above (the shoulder), this happens rarely, then perform a cautery on the thick part of the cautery rod or many cauteries in pricking. For the joint is closed, and the moisture is removed and the patient becomes healthy.
dou cautere de pleuresin	for the treatment of pleurisy (inflammation of the lining of the lungs)
Li ancien dirent que on doit faire a pleuresin cauteres de racines d’aristologe, et en teil maniere: pren une racine d’aristologe longe, la plus grant que tu poras troveir, et soit seche, et soit ausi grosse et ausi longe comme tes dois; et la moille en oile, et l’emprens au feu, et cauterize .i. cautere entre la forcele et lou col, et .ij. petis cauteres un poc en dessendant en la partie qui est desoz la barbe; et .ij. cauteres entre la quinte coste et la sisime, en declinant derrier un poc; et .i. cautere emmi le pis, et .i. autre sus l’estomac, et .i. entre .ij. espaules, et .ij. as .ij. costez dou pis defuers le cautere qui est entre .ij. espaules; et ne presser mie ta main, ains fai apertement ausi com en odorant.	The ancients said that for pleurisy (inflammation of the lining of the lungs), one should make cauteries using roots of aristolochia (a type of plant), and in this way: take a long root of aristolochia, as large and long as your thumb; moisten it in oil, heat it over the fire, and perform a cautery. Make one large cautery between the chest and neck, and two small cauteries a little lower in the area under the beard; make two more cauteries between the fifth and sixth ribs, slanting downwards slightly; make one cautery on the bladder and another on the stomach, one between the shoulders, and two more on the sides of the abdomen, near the cautery that is between the shoulders; do not press your hand tightly, but make it open as when you are sniffing.
Et dirent aucun ancien que aucun home usent de cautere de feir semblant a .i. raseur, et l’eschaufent et le mettent entre les costes, tant qu’il vient a cel aposteme; et saut fuers li dolor, si com nos avons dit en l’aposteme dou foie. Mais en cestui ovraige est paour ou li malaides muert maintenant, ou fistule i vient qui ne puet estre sanee.	And they said that any ancient man uses a cautery like a razor, and heats it up and puts it between the ribs until it reaches the abscess; then the pain leaps away, as we have said in the abscess of the liver. But in this work, there is fear or the patient dies immediately, or a fistula comes that cannot be cured.
de la mice	And they said that any ancient man uses a pestle like a razor...
Quant tu cures la maladie de la mice de ceu que nos avons dit as divisions des cures, et il ne profite mie, adonques i afierent .iij. manieres de cautere que tuit sont boin.	When you treat the disease of the pestle as we have said in the divisions of treatments, and it doesn't help, then they suggest four ways of cautery that are all good.
Desquelz li une maniere si est que tu faices .iij. cauteres, ou .iiij., en lignant selonc la longor de la mice, selonc la figure dou cautere dou foie que nos avons dit devant; et n’apresser mie ta main a tout le cautere, et soit li malaides sovins sor son dos;	The first sentence to translate is: "From which manner it is that you make 3 or 4 cauteries, aligning them according to the length of the vein, according to the shape of the cautery for the liver that we have said before; and do not press your hand on the entire cautery, and let the patient be aware on his back."
et une autre maniere de cautere si est que tu eschaufe le cautere qui a .ij. ners, si com nos l’avons mostreit en la dislocation de l’espaule; et lieve le keur qui est endroit la mice, ou li coutes dou malaide vient devers senestre, et soit li elevations dont tu lieves le keur selonc la keur, selonc la longesce dou cors, et li cautere soient selonc la largesce dou cors.	And another manner of cautery is that you heat the cautery with two nerves, as we have shown in the dislocation of the shoulder; and carve the groove that is towards the vein, where the patient's artery comes from the left, and raise the elevations from the groove according to the groove, according to the length of the body, and the cautery should be according to the width of the body.
Aprés i boute les .ij. ners enflamez tant que li keurs soit perciez de l’autre part, et puis trai fuers le cautere, et ensi en i avra .iiij. Et se tu vues, si cauterize a tot le cautere a .iij. ners. Aprés le cure quant il a geteit porriture par lonc tens, et ce vaut mues que li autre des cures devant dites.	Then insert the two nerves and heat them until the grooves are pierced from the other side, and then pull the cautery through, thus there will be four. And if you see, if you cauterize with a single nerve, then cauterize the entire cautery at four nerves. After the cure, when it has discharged pus for a long time, it is better to use the other remedy mentioned before.
de ydropisie	From hydropisy
Cautere ne vaut a ydropique, fors c’a la maniere qui est apelee «asclytes». Quant tu la cures selonc les manieres que nos avons dit en divisions, et ta cure ne profite mie, adonques covient il que tu li faices .iiij. cauteres entor la boude, et .i. sus l’estomac, et un sus le foie, et .i. sus la mice, et .ij. derrier le dos sus l’espinee, et .i. endroit le pis; et soit li cauteres bien pres de l’espés dou keur.	The fire cautery is not effective for hydropsy, except in the manner called "asclytes". When you cure it according to the ways we have said in the divisions, and your treatment does not help, then you must make four cauterizations around the bladder, one on the stomach, one on the liver, one on the spleen, two behind the back near the spine, and one near the kidney; and let the cauteries be close to the swelling.
Aprés laisse le cautere aovert por giter porriture lonc tens, et ne lassier mie la cure dou malaide aprés le cautere; et sanation se hasterait, et seront ensamble les .ij. ententions avec l’aide de Deu.	After the cautery is opened to purge pus for a long time, do not abandon the treatment of the patient after the cautery; and healing will be hastened, and the two intentions (i.e., the patient's health and the cauterization) will come together with God's help.
Li forme dou cautere por le ventre soit li clavile que nos avons devant mostreit; et cil por le dos soit olivaire, selonc ceu qu’il est ci devant mis.	The shape for the belly cautery is like a key that we have shown before; and for the back it is olive-shaped, as mentioned earlier.
de l’enfleure des piez	of the swelling of the feet
Quant li piez sont enflez a celui qui est ydropique, et sont plain d’awe citrine, il covient que tu cauterizes sus le dos dou piet entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire; et lieve ta main avec le cautere sens torner. Et n’entrer mie trop em parfont, ensi sarrait fuers li awe citrine, et soit li cauteres selonc cest forme:	When the feet are swollen in a person who is edematous and full of yellow water, it is necessary that you cauterize on the back of the foot between the little finger and the ring finger; and lower your hand with the cautery without turning. And do not enter too deep, so as not to hurt the yellow water, and let the cautery be in this form:
Aprés fai sus .ij. jambes .ij. cauteres en chescune jambe a la pointe dou cutellaire; et soit li cauteres dou lonc, l’un desoz le genoil devant et l’autre defuers, enmi la jambe; et laisse les cauteres aovers longement sens curer, que li awe en isse; aprés le cure des autres cures que nos avons dit.	After making two incisions in each leg with the scalpel, place two cauteries at the tip of each incision; and let the cautery be long, one under the thigh in front and the other behind, within the leg; and leave the cauterized areas to heal, as needed; after healing all the other treatments mentioned.
de la menoison	From the dislocation... (Dislocation is the main topic of this sentence)
Quant solution de ventre vient de froidor et de moistor, tant que li vertus retentive et digestive qui est ou stomac et en l’intestine est afleboie, et ne puet estre curez par manieres de cures; et tu vois le malaide bien soffrant et de fort vertut, si fai .i. grant cautere sus l’estomac selonc ceu qu’il en a parleit ci devant ou cautere de l’estomac, au cautere circule; et .iiij. cauteres entor la boude subtilz a tout .i. cautere clavile subtil, et .ij. cauteres sus les hainches.	When the inflammation of the stomach results from cold and moisture, retaining and digestive qualities that are in the stomach and intestines are weakened, and cannot be cured by any means; and you see the patient suffering greatly and with strong pain, make one large cautery on the stomach as discussed earlier (cautery of the stomach), around the circumference; and four subtle cauteries around the navel, one thin cautery at the navel, and two cauteries on the flanks.
Et se tu vois les moistors habundans et le malaide soffrant, se li fai cautere sus le poignil, et .i. cautere sus chaicun yle, et .ij. petis cauteres sus l’estomac delez le grant, car li cure est profitans quant il i a bone aide.	And if you see excessive moisture and the patient suffering, apply a cautery on the joint, one cautery on each sore, and two small cauteries on the stomach in front of the larger one, for the cure is beneficial where there is good help.
de la cure des emorroydes	Of the cure for hemorrhoids
