Quant les emorroydes sont ou fondement, ou une ou plusors, et sont ancienes et sont de grosses humors froides et moistes corrumpues, et sont curees si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie, si fai cauteres: .iij. sus l’espine dou dos, celi qui est tout defuers desoz almecdate poc et poc en triangulant, et .i. cautere desoz la boude. ij. dois;	When the hemorrhoids are rooted or multiple and old, filled with thick cold and moist corrupted humor, and are treated as mentioned in divisions, it does not help if cauteries are performed: four on the spine of the back, one that is completely removed below the anus pointed triangularly, and one below the buttocks. Two cauteries should be done;
et se tu penses que ses estomac soit refroidiez, et li viande ne cuise, et on voit enfler la faice, adonques li faice on .i. grant cautere sus le stomac, si com il est devant dit, et .i. autre sus le foie, et i. autre sus la mice a tout le cautere clavile; et laisse le cautere overt lonc tens. Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	If you think that his stomach is chilled and the meat does not cook, and swelling is observed on his face, then a large cautery is applied to the stomach as previously stated, and another to the liver, and another to the spleen with all the cauteries being held together; leave the cauteries open for a long time. After healing the place where the cautery was applied until it is healed.
de la charnositeit qui est nommee «thelul»	of the sores called "thelul"
Quant tu copes althelul, si eschaufe le cautere qui semble .i. raseur, et puis le met tout embraseit sus cel althelul copeit; et i laisse tant ta main que li cauteres viegne a la naissance de la voine, de coi li sans cort; fai ceu une fois ou .ij., et s’il i a mout d’althelul, si cauterize chaicun si com nos avons dit; aprés les cure d’oignemens profitans tant qu’il soient sanez; et se tu cauterizes d’un cautere grant sus alchatim, si avra plus grant aide.	When you treat thelul, if the cautery seems like a razor, heat it and then place it all around the treated sore; leave your hand there so that the cautery reaches the base of the vein, so that it burns; do this once or twice, and if there is much thelul, cauterize each one as we have said; after these cure with healing ointments until they are healed; and if you cauterize a large cautery on the charcoal, it will have more aid.
de plaie mal curee	of an ill-healed wound
Quant li malaides ne puet soffrir tailleure ne overture, que nos raconterons en son leu, si vient teil maladie que ne puet estre sanee fuer que par cautere.	When the patient cannot endure incision or opening, as we will describe in its place, comes a disease that can only be cured by cautery.
Quant a aucun vient fistule, et est enveillie et giete porriture et moistors corrumpues, si la doies prover a tot une tente subtil, et garde que tu saiches a tot la tente combien elle a de parfont. Aprés eschaufe le cautere qui semble .i. raseur, et le boute en la fistule selonc la quantiteit que li tente i est entrée, et rencomence lou cautere tant que cil cors porris et corrumpus soient ars, une fois, ou .ij. ou .iij., selonc la quantiteit de som besoing; et te warde d’ardre lé nerf qui sunt enqui, et des grans voinnes. se li fistule vait au cors de la vesie et a l’intestine, si te warde de ces leus, et ne faire ceu fuers que en leu charnut, et pense qu’ele n’est mie persans; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez, et se li leus est saielez, et les matieres sont ostees lonc tens, adonc saiches que li leus est sanez entierement; et se les matieres ne sont ostees, saiche que li leus est troez, et corrumpus li os au font; et ensi com un de ces que nos dirons en son leu.	When a fistula comes and becomes swollen with putrid matter and corrupted moisture, one should investigate it thoroughly and be certain of the depth to which it has penetrated. After heating the cautery that appears as if it were a shaver, insert it into the fistula according to the thickness of the tissue that it has entered, and continue the cautery until the body becomes burnt and corrupted, once, or twice, or thrice, depending on the amount of tissue needing to be burned; beware of burning the nerves and large veins. If the fistula goes towards the bladder and intestine, be careful in this area, and do not perform this procedure outside of a charnel house, and believe that it is not sinful; after curing the area until it is healed, if the area becomes septic and matter has been removed for a long time, then know that the area is healed completely; if the matter has not been removed, know that the area is not healed, and burn the bone to make it heal. As we will describe in its place, one of these procedures.
de la maladie des reins	of the disease of the kidneys
Quant dolor de froit vient as rains, et de grosse ventositeit, et ne prent talant de femme, adonc covient il que tu li fais cautere sus les rains d’une part et d’autre au cautere clavile que nos avons devant dit; et se nos le cauterizons em mileu, si avra .iij. cauteres en ligne, et se feront plus grant aide.	When pain of the kidneys comes with cold and large wind, and does not take on the form of a woman, then you must perform cautery on the kidneys from both sides with a cautery iron as we have previously said; and if we perform cauterization in the middle (of the body), there will be four cauteries in a line, and it will provide more aid.
de la vessie	of the bladder
Quant li vessie est mole et foible de froit et de moistor, si que li malaides retient l’urine, adonc li fai cautere en la partie defuers sus la vessie, la ou encomencent li poil dou poignil, et .i. a destre et .i. a senestre, et soit chescuns cauteres si lons com li nous d’un poce; et li fais .i. cautere defuers le dos, ou .ij. se tu en as besoing; et soit li cauteres clavile selon la forme devant dite.	If the bladder is soft and weak due to cold and moisture, causing the patient to retain urine, then perform cauterization on the part outside the bladder, where the pubic hair starts, one on each side, and each cautery should be as long as the knuckle of your finger; and perform one cauterization behind the back, or two if necessary; and make sure the cauteries are shaped as previously described.
de la marris	of the marriage
Quant li marrix est froide et moiste, et ne laisse mie por ceu a concevoir, et les flors sont corrumpues et lor termines tarde; et quant elles vienent, si sent grant dolor: adonques covient il c’on li faice .iij. cauteres entor la boude, si com nos avons dit ou cautere de la vessie, et .ij. cauteres defuers le dos; et soit li cauteres clavile, si com nos avons dit.	When the marriage is cold and moist and does not allow conception, and the flowers are corrupted and their term is delayed; and when they come, it causes great pain: then it is necessary that you do four cauterizations around the womb, as we have said in the caution of the bladder, and two cauterizations behind the back; and let the cauterization be sharp, as we have said.
de la hainche	of the infection
Quant les moistors viscouses dessendent a la boiste de la hainche, et por ceste cause si se muet de son leu, et li signes est que li cuisse est plus longe que li autre quant on le mesure ensamble; et est trovez li leus dou departement vuis, si covient que tu cauterizes le malaide sus la boiste de la hainche a .i. cautere semblant au cercle, et seigne devant le leu entor la boiste si com elle torne, si que li boiste soit dedens le cercle; et si soit li cauteres telz com cil dont on a cauterizeit le stomac.	When viscous humors descend into the joint of the hip, and for this reason it becomes immobile from its place, the signs are that the thigh is longer than the other when measured together; and the limbs are found to be out of their socket, if you need to cauterize the patient over the joint of the hip with a circular cautery, facing in front of the joint around the socket so that the joint is within the circle; and if the cauterization is like those used for the stomach.
Et se cist cauteres ne t’est presens, se li fai .iij. cauteres de l’olivaire grans, et soit li cauteres ausi parfont com tous li keurs; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if this cauterization is not available to you, make four large olive-shaped cauteries and make them as sharp as all the others; and use it until it heals.
de la dolor de la hainche	of the pain in the hip
Quant dolor vient en la boiste de la hainche, et c’est de froidor et de moistor, et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en la division et li cure ne vaut, et li maladie est anciene: adonc covient il que tu purges le malaide des grosses humors de pilules fetides, ou autres pilules bones semblans.	When pain comes in the belly of the loin (lower back), and it is due to coldness and moisture; and the patient is treated for this as we have said in the division but the cure is not effective; and the disease is old: then you must purge the patient of the gross humors with fetid pills or other good-seeming pills.
Aprés li fai cautere; et li maniere dou cautere si est selonc .ij. manieres: c’est a savoir ensamble medicines ardans, et cautere de feu. Cautere de feu si est selonc mout de manieres, desquelz li uns est telz: que tu cauterize sus la boiste de la hainche .iij. cauteres triangulalz selonc ceste forme, et i fai bone profunditeit et grant, et ait entre chaicun cautere d’espaice la groissece d’un doi, et soit li cauteres olivaire; aucune fois fait on cautere en mileu sus lou chief de la hainche, por coi il en i a .iiij. selonc ceste forme:	After the fire cautery; and the method of the cautery is according to two methods: namely with burning substances, and the fire cautery. The fire cautery is according to many ways, one of which is as follows: you shall cauterize on the belly of the loin four triangular cauteries according to this form, and make good depth and width; and there should be space between each cautery the size of a dove; and the cauteries should be olive-shaped. Sometimes, the cautery is made in the middle of the lower back, so there are four according to this shape:
Et se tu vues, si le cauterize au cautere dou cercle que nos avons devant dit en la dislocation de la hainche; mais fai en teil maniere que li cercles conteigne toute la hainche, et tous li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if you see, if the cautery is made at the circular cautery that we have mentioned earlier in the dislocation of the loin; but do it in this way so that the circles encompass the entire loin, and all the spaces of the kidney are burned.
Et c’est li maniere c’on fait en sciatique, quant li dolor tient en la hainche, et ne parvient mie jusc’a la cuisse ne jusc’a la jambe. Et s’ele vient jusc’a la cuisse et la jambe, se li fai .ij. cauteres lai ou li malaides dit que li dolor li tient, et .i. cautere desus la cheville .iiij. dois, a la partie senestre un poc; et soit li cauteres cutellaire, et soit arse li espesseté dou keur; et se li malaides sent que li dolor s’estende jusc’a dois dou piet ou pres d’enqui, se le cauterize la ou il sent la dolor .iij. poins ou .iiij. au cautere qui est apelez «poins».	And this is the method that is done in sciatica, when the pain remains in the lower back and does not reach the thigh or the leg. If it reaches the thigh and the leg, two cauteries are applied where the patient says the pain lies, and one cautery above the ankle at a distance of 4 fingers from the left side; and whether the cautery is cutler's or arsenic is applied to the sore spot; and if the patient feels that the pain extends to the level of the foot or close by, the cauterization should be done where they feel the pain - three points or four at the cauterization point called "points."
Et se mestiers est, se li en fai plus; et se il seit que li dolor soit desoz le genoil vers la cuisse, se li fais cautere au cautere cutellaire ou circulaire, et te done bien garde en tous tes cauteres que tu n’i lassier mie tant le cautere que tu brules les ners et les grans arteres, et que tu ne faices au malaide plus grant nuisance et contraction.	If necessary, more are done; and if the pain is below the knee towards the thigh, a cautionery of cutler's or circular cautery is applied, and take good care in all your cauteries not to leave the cauter too long that you burn the nerves and large arteries, and do not make any greater harm and contraction to the patient.
Et je meisme ai veus plusors qui ont fait cautere sus la cheville dou piet, et li lasserent tant que li jambe fut toute enflee, et li piez ausi, et fut perciez et corrumpus toz li piez. Aprés une solution de ventre dont il ot la mort.	And I myself have seen more who applied caution on the ankle of the foot, and they left it too long that the leg was all swollen, and the feet as well, and they were pierced and corrupted through all the toes. After a belly solution in which they died.
Et se li dolors est en .ij. parties ensamble, fai cautere en l’une et en l’autre, selonc ceste maniere. // Et li saige dirent en la cautere de la hainche, de coi ci est li maniere, fai .i. tel fer et soit au chief ausi gros com uns nauvillon de dacte, ou un poc moins, et soit par entrechetres et soit des l’un entrechetres jusc’a l’autre d’espaice la quantiteit d’un nou de poce; et soient li entrechetres aovers de .ij. pars, et soient aussi comme noez, et i ait .i. mainche de fer bien fait; et c’est li forme:	And if the pain is in two places together, perform cautery on one and the other, following this manner. The wise shall say about the caution of the hunchback, as follows: make one nail of iron and be as thick as a finger of thumb or slightly smaller, and either between-the-cheeks or from one between-the-cheek to the other with a distance equal to the size of a nut of walnut; and let the between-the-cheeks be across two parts, and let them also be like nuts, and have one handle of iron well made; and this is its shape:
Et soit eschaufez tant qu’il soit toz rouges et giete senteles, et puis le mette on sus la boiste de la hainche malaide, et soit tornez sus lou sain costeit; et lou cauterize une fois .i. cautere reont et lou laisse .iij. jors; et puis fai emplaustre de burre, et laisse la plaie aoverte lonc tens; aprés la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	And scald until it is all red and blisters, then place it on the hunchback's patient's side, turning it towards the healthy side; and cauterize one time with the iron once and let it rest for four days; then apply a plaster of butter, leaving the wound open for a long time; afterwards cure with ointment until it heals.
Albucasim dit que nos usons poc de cest cautere por la paor de son regart, et se voions poc qui en usent; et toutevoie ceu est des boins cauteres, qui le puet soffrir, et lai ou il s’afiert.	Albucasim says that we use little of this cautery because of the fear of its gaze, and few who use it; however, this is one of the good cauteries, which can be borne by those who can endure it, and where it is applied.
de la dolor dou dos	From the pain of the back
Quant dolor vient au dos, ou par cheoir ou de percussion ou par trop grant evacuation, ou par semblans de matiere espandue froide, a nule de ces semblances ne vaut cauteres, fuer que a celi qui vient de infusion de froide matiere.	When the back pain comes from falling or striking, excessive bleeding, or similar causes of cold matter spreading, none of these cases are suitable for cauterization except to the one who is affected by the infusion of cold matter.
Il covient c’aprés ceu que li malaides est voidiez de pilules fetides ou d’autres semblans, que on li faice sus lou dos, lai ou li dolor tient, trois lignes signies d’enche, et en chescune ligne .v. cauteres ou plus selonc la vertut et la quantiteit que li malaides puet soffrir; et soit fait li cauteres selonc le cautere qui est apelez «poins»; et se tu vues, fai .iij. cauteres ou .iiij. au cautere clavile moien selonc ceste forme:	It is necessary that the patient be emptied of poisonous pills or similar substances, which are placed on the back where the pain is located, marked with three lines and in each line five cauteries or more according to their strength and quantity that the patient can endure; and the cautery should be made according to the cautery called "poins"; and if you see, make four cauteries or four using a medium-sized cauterizer in this form:
Maintes fois vient ceste maladie as petis enfans, et li signes de l’encomencement si est qu’il ont estroite alainne quant il se lievent, et paor; et tu trueves en la derriene espinee dou dos et en nous l’apparance qui vient sus les autres espinees.	Many times this disease comes to small children, and the signs of its beginning are that they have narrow anus when they strain, fearful; and you can find it in the lower spine of the back and in the appearance that appears above the other spines.
Quant tu vois ceu et tu le vues curer, si le cauterize au cautere de celcle selonc ceste forme.	When you see this and want to cure it, you should cauterize it with the cautery of that part according to this form.
Si que li cautere porpreigne chescune partie de l’espinee egaument. Et se tu vues, si cauterize entor l’espinee au cautere poignant .ij. lignes ou .iij., et soient li poins pres l’uns de l’autre. Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez selonc ceu que nos avons dit, et warde que tu n’amenistrer cautere en gilbositeit qui soit en spame de nerf.	The cautery should enlarge each part of the spine equally. If you see, then cauterize around the spine with a pointed cautery .2 lines or .3, and the points should be close to each other. After curing the area until it is healthy according to what has been said, beware not to apply the cautery in gilbositeit which is in nerve spasm.
de la dolor des jointes	of the pain of the joints
Quant dolor de jointes sunt de moistors que sont espandues a chaicun membre dou cors, et quant dolor vient em piez, que li mire apelent «podagre» proprement, et quant elle est de froide cause et cures de medicines ne la puent curer, si est curez par cauteres en teil maniere: fai li mout de cauteres entor la jointure dou piet, et soit li cauteres olivaire selonc ceste forme:	When pain in the joints is due to swellings that occur on every member of the body, and when pain comes in feet, which are called 'gout' properly, and when it is due to cold and medicines cannot cure it, then it is cured by cautery in this manner: make the patient lie down with a cautery around the joint of the foot, and let the cautery be olive-shaped according to this form:
Et s’il i a besoigne que tu poignes sus la faice dou piet, se li fai cautere a tot le cautere c’on claime «point». Et se les dolors viegnent jusc’a genous et as autres jointures, et ceu avient maintes fois, se li fai cautere sus chaicun genoil .iij. cauteres ou .iiij. de chescunne partie, a tout le cautere olivaire; et se tu as mestier de plus, si en fai plus, mais n’i tenir mie ta main fuers que tant que li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if it is necessary to pinch on the face of the foot, make a cautery all over the cautery called "point". And if the pains come up to the knees and other joints, and this happens many times, make a cautery on each knee four times or four on each side, with an olive-shaped cautery; and if you need more, do so, but not beyond that point where the edges of the burn are burned.
Et se les dolors dessendent jusc’a genoil et au dos, se li aministre le cautere que nos avons dit en son chapistre. Et se les dolors sunt as mains, si fai poins entor le foscile .ij. lignes; et s’il remaint point de dolor as dois, si fai poins sus chescune jointe et sus lou poil de la main; et se les dolors vienent jusc’as coutes ou jusc’as espaules, si cauterize chescune partie, et fai boin governement au malaide et penre medicines. Car se tu li fais boin governement et tu purges fleume, si sera saneis a l’aide de Deu.	1. And if the pains descend to the genitals and back, administer the fire cautery as we have said in its chapter.
de la routure dou syfac	The next sentence is: "de la routure dou syfac." Without additional context or comments, the translation of this sentence into English is: "Of the dislocation of the shoulder."
Quant routure vient en angres, et li bouelz dessendent as coions et c’est novelement, si covient que quant tu lou vues curer, qu’il ne menjuce mie celui jor; et qu’il use choses qui laichent lou ventre, si que li fiens dessende de son ventre; aprés le fai seoir sus son dos entre tes mains, et li comande qu’il teigne son alaine tant que li boueil soient repairiet, et les ramoinne a tes dois, et seigne d’enche desoz la routure sus l’os dou poignil, et a tout un signe que soit semblans a la moitiet d’un cercle a desus dou cors; puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When the dislocation of the shoulder occurs in anger, and the arms descend towards the chest and this is new, then when you see it to be treated, it should not eat anything that day; and use things which loosen the stomach, so that the farts decrease from the stomach; afterwards, make the patient sit on his back between your hands, and command him to hold his elbow as long as the dislocation remains, and reposition it at your fingertips, and press down firmly over the dislocation above the joint of the shoulder; and use a sign that is similar to half a circle above the chest; then heat the cautery in the shape shown here:
tant qu’il soit blans et qu’il giete senteles. Puis ramoine les bouels a lor leu; et li ministres teigne sa main sus qu’il ne retornent arrier; et oevre bien les cuisses au malaide, et met desoz lui .i. cussin et .i. serjant sus les cuisses, et .i. autre sus lou pis qui li teigne les mains; puis met le cautere sus lou signe a tout ta main, et lou tien droit et lou tien tant que tu ateignes l’os, et se tu ne l’ateins la premiere fois, si le rencomence encor une autre tant que tu viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde subtilment que li boueil ne saille quant tu fais lou cautere; que tu ne le brulasses; et que par ceu li malaides ne muere, ou autre malz.	Keep the hairs long and even while it is white and it exudes pus. Then move the shoulders back into place; and the attendant holds his hand above so that they do not return; and work well on the thighs of the patient, and put one cushion and one bandage on the thighs, and another on the affected part which holds the hands; then place the cautery on the mark all over your hand, hold it straight and keep it until you reach the bone, and if you do not reach it the first time, start again as long as you come to the bone; and be careful that the boil does not burst when you perform the cautery; that you do not burn it; and that through this the patient does not die, or other harm.
Et saiches que quant tu ne viens jusc’a l’os au cautere, tes ovraiges ne vaut rien. Et covient que li cauteres des enfans soit subtilz selonc la mesure d’ous, et des grans gens aussi grans selonc lor mesure; aprés .iij. jors cure lou leu dou cautere de burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’autres oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez, et gise li malaides .xl. jors sus son dos tant que li plaie soit bien soudee; et covient que ses norrissemens soit lassatis longement, si que li boueil ne saillent quant il se preigdra d’aler en chambres.	And know that if you do not come to the bone during cautery, your work is worth nothing. It is necessary that the cauteries for children be subtle according to their size, and those of larger people also large according to their measure; after four days cure the wound from the cautery with butter until the burn is healed; after that, cure with other ointments until it is healthy, and let the patient lie on his back for forty days until the wounds are well healed; and it is necessary that his dressings be left long, so that the boil does not burst when he is ready to leave the room.
Et aprés .xl. jors, quant il se voudra lever, se li amenistre une faixe bien faite, et la porse .xl. autres jors; et ait boin repos, qu’il se travaille poc et se warde de trop grant repletion de boivre et de mengier, et de trop haut braire; et quant il fait cest enseignement si est sanez entierement. Et je dirai ci aprés la cure de taillier en son chapistre.	And after forty days, when he wants to get up, bring him a well-made bandage and let it be for another forty days; let him have good rest, so that he does not work too much or strain himself, and avoid excessive drinking, eating, and shouting; and if he follows this teaching, he will heal completely. And I will say more about the surgery in its chapter afterward.
de la routure dou ventre	Of the hernia of the belly
Quant routures vienent en autres ventres et sont connisans, et tu vues qu’elles ne croissent plus, se li fai .j. cautere dou cautere reont selonc sa quantiteit, et soit ars li tiers dou keur; aprés le cure selonc ceu que nos avons dit; et aucun des anciens ont dit c’on le doit cauterizer au cautere a .iij. angles selonc ceste forme:	When hernias occur in other bellies and are recognized as not growing any more, do this. mais signe premier le leu d’enche et fai une ligne per la largesce desus la routure, et une autre defuers, et main ta main emmi a tout le cautere clavile. de dolor anciene en aucun membre	Of old pain in any limb
Quant dolor vient en aucun membre, ou de cheoir ou de ferir, et cele dolor tient lonc tens, et li cure de medicine n’i vaut, adonc covient qu’il soit cauterizeis au cautere qui est apelez «poins», et soit li cauteres selonc la longesce dou membre et la petitece et sa foibleteit et sa vertut et sa location de torcions et de sa dolor. s’il est sanez dou premier cautere, c’est bien; se ceu nom, recomence .i. autre cautere sus celui, car teilz costume est qu’il se doit muer au membre que li est prochiens, por coi il covient que tu faices les cauteres tant que li malaides soit saneis.	When pain comes in any member, whether from falling or being injured, and this pain lasts for a long time, and the medicine does not heal it, then it should be cauterized with the cautery called "poins", and the cauteries should be according to the length of the member, its size and weakness, and its virtue and location of twists and its pain. If it is healed from the first cauterization, that is good; if not, repeat one more cauterization on top of it, as this custom is that it must change in the nearby member, so you should perform the cauteries as long as the patient is not healed.
de meselerie	To mix medicines.
Li meseil sont aidiet aucune fois par cautere par grant aide, et meismement li maladie que vient de la putrefaction de fleume et de melancolie. Cant tu la vues cauterizer, pren warde se li maladie est au comencement, et s’ele est curee selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et ne dessent ne ne demoure, et tu doutes que li corruption ne porpreigne tout le malaide, adonques li fai .v. cauteres sus lou chief: .i. emmi le chief a nouf, et l’autre vers lou front a la fin des chevous; et .ij. sus les .ij. cornes, et .i. derrierre sus le haiterel; et i laise tant ta main que li cauteres viegne jusc’a l’os, et tant que les escorces en issent fors si que les vapors des grosses humors s’en puissent issir; et le cauterize sus la mice selonc ce qu’il est devant.	The remedies are sometimes helped by cautery with great aid, and especially those illnesses that come from the putrefaction of phlegm and melancholy. If you see it being cauterized, take care if the sickness is at the beginning, and if it is cured according to what we have said in the division, and neither bleeds nor remains, and you doubt that the corruption does not spread throughout the entire patient, then perform 5 cauteries on the head: one on the neck, and another towards the front at the end of the hair; two on the temples, and one behind the ear; and leave your hand so that the cautery reaches the bone, and so that the scabs come out from it, allowing the vapors of the gross humors to escape; and cauterize the private parts according to what is before.
Et se li meselerie est partout esparse; et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et .i. cautere en som lou neis, et .ij. cauteres sus l’espinee dou col, et .vj. cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos, et .i. grant sus la crupie et .i. autre delez, et .ij. sus les .ij. espaules; et .ij. sus les coutes, et .ij. sus les tendrons dou pis, et .i. sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains; et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler; et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l’os dou poignil, et .i. autre sus l’os de l’estomac, et .i. autre sus lou foie.	And if the disease is scattered everywhere; it will certainly perish, you must then burn it with the cauteries we have mentioned: one cautery on the neck, two cauteries on the spine of the neck, six cauteries on the spine of the back, one large one on the shin and another on the ankle, two on each shoulder; two on the hips, two on the tendons of the feet, one on each joint of the hands and feet, and on the hollows of the hands; be careful not to burn the nerves that are above the heels, you should not burn them; never apply a cautery on the bone of the thumb, and one other on the bone of the stomach, and one other on the liver.
Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, plus li fais d’aide, et mues li profite; et saiches que li malaides ne sent point de dolor au cautere si com li sain le sentent, por ce que li cors est ja toz corrumpus. Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers. Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis.	Know that the more you use cautery, the more help it provides and it benefits him; and know that the sick do not feel pain from the cautery as the healthy do, because the body is already completely corrupted. It is necessary that the cautery be large and small according to the members and joints, according to what you will find in manners of iron. After curing the wound with flour several times with honey and other remedies until it heals.
de enfleure	inflammation or swelling
Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n’est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre; et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l’espés dou keur; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez. Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l’issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure; et toutevoie ne s’en entremette nuls s’il n’est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors.	When a swelling appears in any member and is treated with medicines, oils, and plasters, but it is not healed, then you should perform cauterization on the limb according to its size and the smallness of the limb; and the cauterization may be a small incision in the thick part of the skin. Then you heal it with unguents until it is healed. Sometimes cauterization is done on the hand, foot, back, at the nerve issue that immobilizes the limb, and in such a case the swelling is removed; however, no one should interfere unless they are knowledgeable about members and the issues of moving nerves in the body.
de albaras	When a sore appears on any member and it is treated with medicines, ointments, and plasters, but it is not cured, then you should perform an incision (albaras) on the limb according to its size and the smallness of the limb; and the incision may be a small cut in the thick part of the skin. Then you heal it with ointments until it is cured. Sometimes an incision is done on the hand, foot, back, at the nerve issue that immobilizes the limb, and in such a case the sore is removed; however, no one should interfere unless they are knowledgeable about members and the issues of moving nerves in the body.
Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color; puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie; et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the disease called "albaras" becomes mature and the medicines do not work, then cauterize it with a deep cautery (according to the thickness of the skin), until the white spot is removed and its color changes; then heal it with flour and lentils mixed with rose oil and banana leaves, and ox blood and eagle blood, in equal parts; and mix everything together, tie it up in a cloth, and apply it to the place until it is cured.
li cure de chancre par cautere	The treatment of syphilis by cautery.
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble .i. cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.  Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre; et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois; et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	When syphilis begins and you wish to stop it, if you cauterize with the cautery that appears to be one circle around the syphilitic sore; and although the wise say that a cautery should also be applied in the middle of the syphilitic sore; yet I do not think this is good, because I fear that it will become ulcerated and corrupted, and I have seen it happen once before; and more proper is that it be cauterized with the "circular" cautery, as we have said in the discussion of cauteries.
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	The swelling that cannot measure (grow)
Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», et elle tarde de meurer ou por la superfluiteit qu’ele fait ou por l’eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c’est a dire trop vielz) et il a poc de sanc, ou por lou tens; et tu la vues haster de meurer: adonques le cauterize entor de mout de petis cauteres en poignant; aprés le laisse ensi. Car elle se hastera de meureir.	When someone has a disease called "adubelati", which is slow to heal or because of the excess it causes, or because of the age of the patient when they are decrepit (meaning too old), and have little blood, or because of the time; and you see it hastening to heal: then cauterize it with many small cauteries, pricking around it; afterwards leave it in this state. For it will hasten to heal.
Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	And if you see it being pierced with the entire cautery, heat the cautery in the form described here:
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis. Aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And place your hand in the middle of that disease called "adubelati" as long as the cautery pierces the core, and make sure the cauteries are such that the patient feels them outside in this manner so that the flow of the pus is even. Afterwards cure it until it heals perfectly.
li cure dou feu par fer	The fire cure by iron
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches. Se tu vois ceste maladie en leu qui puisse soffrir cautere ensamble feu, adonques eschaufe les cauteres clavile mout petit et grant, selonc ceu qu’il covient au leu ou li maladie est; aprés le cauterize de toutes pars tant que tu erraiche toute la corruption, et nen remaigne rien de li, que tout ceu qui est corrumpus ne soit osteit. Et puis le laisse .iij. jors, et met sus les leus cauterizez soffre broiet avec oile tant que les eschaudures dou feu soient ostees, et toute li corruption. Aprés lou cure d’oignemens engendrans char.  Et se tu vois aprés .iij. jors que chars saine ne naisse, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere sus ceu qui est demoreit des leus corrumpus. Et ceste mengeson est aucune fois esteit curee de medicine ague en leu de cautere de feu; mais toutevoie cautere de feu est de plus grant aide, et j’ai ja dit la cure de la medicine ague en la division: pren la quant tu en as mestier.	Another kind of disease is called "corrodens," and it is nothing but a rotting of the limb, for it eats away at the limbs just as fire burns dry wood. If you see this disease in a place where a fire cure can be applied, then heat the irons, both large and small, according to what is required in the place or location of the disease; after heating all parts until all corruption is reached and nothing remains of it, that everything corrupted is removed. And then leave it for three days, and apply soft cauterized ointment with oil as often as the burns from fire are healed, and all the corruption. After the healing of the wounds, generate char. And if after three days you see that healthy char does not grow, that's good; if not, repeat the cautery on the remaining corrupted parts. And this rotting is sometimes cured with ague medicine instead of fire cure; however, fire cure is of greater help, and I have already said the cure for ague in its division: take as much as you need.
des porrelz qui vienent as piez	swellings that come to the feet
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet. Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc .ij. manieres. C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude. Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe .i. cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges; aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou; et lou laisse ensi .iij. jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture; puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines. Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	Often, toes suffer from a disease called "clos" according to our understanding, which is a large swelling that hurts the foot. The cures for this disease are in two ways. One is fire cautery, and the other is hot water cautery. Fire cautery is when you heat one iron cautery like a feather of a raven, made of good iron so it can pierce the nail from all sides, and it should have fine margins; after that, place everything hot on the nail, turn your hand entirely around the nail until it comes to the base of the nail; then leave it for three days until it begins to discharge pus; then make a plaster of wild herbs crushed with oil, and leave the plaster on it all night; the nail will shrink and be uprooted from its roots. Then cure the area with soothing ointment until it heals.
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude; et est en teil maniere: pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues; et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine; et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre; puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines. Ensi fai un aprés autre, tant que tu esraiches toz ces qui sont au cors, puis les cure des oignemens qui engenrent char.	If they are converted on the outside of the body (meaning external wounds), and it often happens in hands and feet, you must provide hot water cautery; and it is done like this: take a cane made of iron or a raven feather, and place it on the nail and burn blisters (meaning boils); then place the cane so that it surrounds it completely, then put a little hot water, hold your hand firmly, and press your hand while turning so that the edge of the cane reaches the root of the nail, and let the hot water penetrate deeply to the root; allow the patient to bear the pain of the hot water for an hour; then leave it as it is, and it will uproot itself from all its roots. Do this again until you have heated all those on the body, then treat them with ointments that soothe.
li cure dou trembler	the trembling cures
Quant aucuns tremble de froidor de ners, ou de fievre quartaine ou d’autre, si covient que tu li faices .iiij. cauteres ou .iv. sus l’espinee dou dos, .i. cautere entre chescune espinee; et .i. cautere ou pez, et .i. sus l’estomac au cautere olivaire; si laissera lou trembler, et se hastera li santez de la maladie froide.	When someone shakes with cold or from quartan fever or something else, it is necessary that you make 4 or 5 fire cauterizations on the spine of the back, one between each spine; and 1 cauterization near the navel, and 1 on the stomach at the olive oil cauterization site; this will stop the shaking and hasten the recovery from the cold disease.
des pustules puans	pus-filled blisters (boils)
Aucune fois apperent par defuers le cors bathes, ou pustules puans, que vienent de grosses matieres corrumpues. si covient au premier quant eles apperent que on faice cautere sus chescun chief de la pustule: un cautere subtil de fust de mirte, de coi li pointe soit emprise au feu, ou de racine de aristologe longe, ou au cautere lenticulaire. Et aucune fois les cauterize on au comencement quant il aperent, selonc ceste maniere, et il ne puent croistre des enqui en avant, mais est desrompue li superfluitez dont il vienent, et sont sanez; mais il covient que ceu soit fait aprés l’evacuation de sanc.	Sometimes the body appears to be bathed with boils, which come from corrupted matter. It is necessary, at first when they appear, that cautery be made over each head of the boil: a subtle cautery from myrtle stick, so that it can grasp fire, or from long root of aristolochia, or cauterize with lenticular cautery. Sometimes they are cauterized from the beginning when they appear in this manner, and they cannot grow further, but the superfluous matter which comes from them is discharged, and they become healthy; however, it is necessary that this be done after the evacuation of blood.
quant li artere est copee	When the artery is cut
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses; et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.	Often there are great outflows of blood from the artery that is cut in the wound or at the abscess incision, or during cauterization of the limb, and similar things; it is a very serious matter to cause bleeding.
Et toutevoie quant ceu avient a aucun, si te haste de mettre ton doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne, et l’estrain mout tant que li sans soit apaisiez desoz ton doi, et que goute n’en isse plus; puis met au feu les cauteres olivaire plusors petis et grans tant qu’il soient tuit rouge; puis empren .i., ou grant ou petit selonc la plaie et lou leu en coi li artere est route, et met le cautere sus cele voine ou tu tiens ton doi, et tien le cautere tant sus que li sans soit restainchiez.	Moreover, whenever this happens to anyone, you should quickly put your finger on the wound vein and press it very hard until the blood is stopped from flowing; then take olive oil cauteries, both small and large, until they are all red; then take one (either large or small according to the size of the wound and where the artery is located), and place the cautery on that vein where your finger is placed, and hold it there until the blood stops flowing.
Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement .i. autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	And if the vein suddenly jumps when you hold your finger on it and the cauteries go out, take quickly another of the cauteries that are in the fire.
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez; et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide; et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des .iiij. manieres que nos avons dit: ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc; et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	And do not stop doing this one after the other until the artery is closed; and beware not to burn the nerve that is exposed, and let no other harm come to the patient; know that when the artery dries up, it cannot be well kept closed when the artery is large, unless it is by one of the four ways we have said: either by cauterization, or by extraction when it has not been treated, or by strong binding with thread, or by medicines applied that can keep blood from flowing; and let it be tied and tightened accordingly.
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	Whoever applies a narrow binding tightly with cloth or places hot things on it, or similar things, if it does not help, it does not profit.
Et se ce avient a aucun et il n’ait mie mire ne medicine present, si doit mettre son doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne si com nos avons dit, et bien estrendre tant qu’il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne; et ne remuer lou doit, mais lou moille d’awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez; et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines.	And if this happens to anyone and he does not have medicine present, he should put his index finger on the wound of the vein as we have said, and stretch it out well until it is closed above the wound and the vein; and it must not be moved, but the wound should be cooled with cold water often so that the artery becomes frozen, thickened, and closed; and make inquiries about cauteries and medicines ahead.
Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	Here begins the second book of the treatments for wounds
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres; et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	We have told you in the first chapter all kinds of diseases where it is necessary to use fire cautery or burning medicine, and their causes and instruments and forms of cauteries; I have placed that chapter in its entirety up to the feet, and I will go into this chapter through the same path because it is easier to understand what you are looking for.
Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.	And so, as I begin this, it is necessary, dear child, that you learn that in this chapter there is more danger and fear than in the first of the cauteries, and because of that, it requires greater caution.
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses; ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	For in the work of this chapter, there is often the evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in the treatment of wounds, and in the extraction of arrows, and in cutting into stones, and similar things; where there is doubt and fear, and many die.
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie. Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures. si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice; et de ces doit on avoir paor.	And I warn you not to undertake folly. For many kinds of people come into treatment. Some of them arrive with such illness that they die quickly due to the frenzy they find in their disease, and from the greatness of its malice; and fear is deserved from these.
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit: «atendez, je sui garis»; et li maladie est despitouse. Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los; et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie; et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	And from these there are those who give you counsel and say: "Wait, I am cured"; but the illness is deceitful. It should not be that you consent to those who come to you who have this manner, but put more trust in your honor than in your desire, and do not rashly but wisely from those of whom you are certain, and from which you can take and lose; and use prediction and indication in the treatment of your patients so that health may be converted; and this will help you to acquire good reputation, and glory, and memory of praise.
Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement et droiture, et se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration de sa main, amen.	My dear son, may Our Lords grant you good understanding and righteousness, and if you wish to aspire to the holy inspiration of His hand, Amen.
Or je vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.	I have organized this chapter in sections, following the sequence of the cauteries that I previously described to you from head to feet, because you will find these easier to understand which ones you may need.
dou chief plein d’aigue	full head with water (meaning swollen)
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant; et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	Know that this disease often comes to children during birth, and when the vagina contracts too strongly around the child's head; and sometimes it comes from causes that are not known.
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors; et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	And I have never seen this disease in adults, except for children; and all that I have seen, death hastens; and because of this it seems to me that I should abandon the work in some treatments.
Et je vis .i. enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir; et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os; et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large; et soit ausi longe com .ij. nous, tant que li mostor corre; et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	And I have seen a child whose shoulders were swollen with water, and his head grew larger every day until he could no longer support it; and the moisture was so great that death was believed to have occurred, and this moisture is collected beneath the bone and between the cartilage and the bone; and if the moisture is between the cartilage and the bone, and the abscesses are small, then you should make a large incision in the head, extending as far as two fingers, and follow the shape of the spatula:
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai .ij. fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	If the moisture is deeper and the abscess is larger, you should make two incisions in a cross-like manner, according to this form:
Et se li moistor est desoz l’os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t’est mie reponut: si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief .iij. fendures selonc ceste maniere:	And if the moisture is under the bone, and you see the joints of the head opening on each side, and the hollow gap jumps when you press it with your hand inside, and it does not respond; then you must cut the head open in three places as follows:
Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers. Aprés estraint les fendures de drapelz et de poudres, et i met vin et oile, et laisse ensi jusc’a cinquieme jor; puis le deslie, et cure la plaie par tentes et par oignemens, et laisse estraindre le chief egaument, et done mengier au malaide viande seche de poc de moistor tant que li membre soit confortez et sanez.	After the incision, remove all the moisture outside. Then bind up the wounds with linen and powders, and put vinegar and oil on it, and let it be as such for five days; then unbind, and treat the wound with poultices and ointments, and keep the head stretched out until it heals well, and give dry meat of the moisture to the patient so that the member is comforted and becomes healthy.
Et une autre maniere d’incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l’aposteme, et li assemblé de l’aigue; car aucune fois est elle devant; aucune fois derrier; aucune fois en destre; et aucune fois en senestre.	And another way of incision is that you look where the abscess swelling is greatest, and the opening of the wound; for sometimes it is in front, sometimes behind, sometimes on the right, and sometimes on the left.
Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l’emplissement de l’aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir; et warde que tu ne coper l’artere; et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides muere dou decorrement de sanc et de l’evacuation de moistor.	Therefore, open the abscess or wound and drain the pus, and do as you can with it; but avoid covering the artery; and let some blood flow, so that the patient may die from bleeding and evacuation of moisture in a proper manner.
de reume	Repeat the procedure.
Quant il avient a aucun une maladie qui est apelee «catarre» as eulz ou au pis, et li maladie est anciainne, et li cure de medicine ne profite mie, adonques li derraine cure si est li cauteres avec ceu c’on li copera les .ij. arteres.	When there is any disease called "catarrh" among the eyes or at its worst, and the disease is old, and the medicine's cure does not help, then the last resort is the cautery, by which two arteries will be burned.
Il covient donques, cant tu les vues coper, que li malaides faice rere son chief; aprés li frotte lou leu d’un drapel aspre tant que les arteres aperent, puis estraingne li malaides son col a tout .i. drapel; puis regarde ou li voine bait, et li leus de l’une et de l’autre sont aprés les oreilles, et poc sont reponues; puis signe les leus d’enche, puis cope l’une et l’autre d’un spatumile agut de .ij. pars. tant que li taille veigne jusc’a l’os, et ceu soit par lou large dou chief.	Therefore, when you cover their eyes, the patient must lie down on their back; then rub the area with a rough cloth until the arteries become visible, then grasp the patient's neck with one rough cloth; then look for where the veins meet, and the joints of both sides are behind the ears, and the shoulders are returned to their original position; then mark the places of reattachment, then pierce one and the other with a sharp spatula of two parts. This should cut until the tip reaches the bone, and this should be at the base of the neck.
Et se tu vues, boute le spatumile desoz l’artere et la cope au desus, en taillant ausi com .ij. dois au traver.	And when you pierce, push the spatula under the artery and strike above it, cutting as deep as two fingers.
Et quant li voinne est copee, si saut li sans en haut continuelment fuers.	When the vein is struck, it should jump up repeatedly out of place.
Et se li artere n’apert au sentir, si covient que tu mesures la quantiteit de l’espaice de .iij. dois, puis seigne d’enche et fent jusc’a l’os; et ceu qu’il covient dou sanc mettre fuers si est .vj. c/, et par aventure un poc plus ou moins. selonc ce que li malaides puet soffrir, et la repletion de l’artere; puis regarde la plaie: s’il remaint sus l’os point dou syphac, si le cope que apostemes chaus n’i veigne, puis estrain la plaie et lie, et la cure d’oignement tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And if the artery does not open on its own, it is necessary that you measure the space of three fingers, then incise and cut up to the bone; and the quantity of blood that must be let out is about 5 cubic centimeters, and by chance a little more or less, according to what the patient can endure, and the swelling of the artery; then examine the wound: if it remains above the bone without spreading, then the pus from an abscess does not come, then hold the wound closed and bind, and apply ointment until the wound is healed.
de emigrainne	And in moving (the dislocated limb), if it cannot be returned to its place without pain, then it must be moved gently with a warm cloth or a small hot iron, and then immobilized with bandages so that it can rest until the swelling subsides.
Quant emigrainne anciaine vient, et catarre agut, por les moistors des larmes et les chalors en temples et sode anciene forsenee et semblans choses, et il est medicinez par manieres de cures de medicine et tout ceu ne li profite mie, si estraions les arteres des temples et lou cauterizons, si com nos avons conteit.	When an old dislocation comes and acute catarrh occurs, due to moisture from tears and heat in the temples and other similar conditions, and it is treated by various means of medicines but does not improve, then we should open the arteries of the temples and cauterize them as previously mentioned.
Et li maniere de l’estraction d’elles si est que li malaides faice rere les poilz de ses temples, et entende a l’artere qui apert en la temple, car elle apert bien par son batement, et est poc reponue fuers que en aucuns homes qui sont trop froit; et s’elle est reponue, si estraigne son col li malaides d’aucuns drapelz, puis frote le leu d’aucun aspre drap, et arose le leu d’aigue chaude tant que li artere apere manifestement; puis pren le spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	And the manner of extraction of these [things] is that the patient should shave their temples, and pay attention to the artery which opens in the temple, for it opens well by beating, and is not easily responded to except in some cold individuals; and if it is responded, the patient should tighten their neck with some cloths, then rub the area with a harsh cloth, and warm the area with hot water until the artery becomes apparent; then take the spatumile of which this form is:
puis escorche le cuir legierement tant que tu veignes a l’artere, puis la trai en haut as pinceures, et la depart bien des toiles que sont desoz li de chescune partie; et se li artere est subtilz, si la torne a la pointe de l’uncine, puis la cope de celle partie selonc la quantiteit des .ij. chiés. Car s’elle n’est copee, si ne saut mie li sans dou tout en tout.	Then lightly scrape the skin to see the artery, then pull it up towards the prongs and carefully separate the cloths on both sides; and if the artery is thin, turn it at the tip of the scissors, then press that part according to the size of the two heads. For if it is not pressed, it will not open by itself entirely.
Et trai dou sanc des .vj. c/, jusc’a .iij.; et se li artere est grans, si covient que tu la lies en .ij. leus d’un fil double fort de soie, que porriture n’i veigne devant le soudement de la plaie, et veigne decorremens de sanc; puis cope la superfluiteit qui est entre les .ij. liiens en celle houre meisme, et puis, se tu vues, si lou cauterize dou cautere cutellaire jusc’a l’os tant que li chiés soient copez; et c’est li muedre oevre, se li malaides n’a fievre et il est de chaude complexion.	And draw the blood from 5 cubits, up to 4; and if the artery is large, you must tie it with two strong silk threads, so that pus does not come out before the wound closes, and there is a flow of blood; then cut off the excess between the two ligatures in that same hour itself, and if you see, you cauterize the cautery cutter up to the bone until the heads are separated; and this is the muddling work, if the patient does not have a fever and they are of a hot complexion.
Car li cauteres est aide por finir les moistors: por ceu est il de plus grant aide as moistors.	For the cautery is aid in healing moisters: therefore it is of greatest aid to moisters.
Ou il covient por l’estraction des arteres que om emplisse lou leu de viel coton et mette on sus tentes bien faites; et quant on les desliera, si soit curez de medicines seches que font naistre char, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se sans cort de l’artere tant dis com tu i oevres, si te haste dou coper par cautere, ou tu emple lou leu de vitriole et l’estrain a ta main que li sans soit estainchiez; et se tu n’as ceu present, si met sor le leu ton doit tant que li sans soit congelez, et arose le leu d’aigue froide tant que li sans cesse, et soit estraint si com il covient; et ceu qui est muedre et plus legier en l’estraction de l’artere est que tu cauterizes la voinne de cest cautere trenchant de .ij. pars, mais li trenchant soient bien espés por warder plus longement lor chalor.	For the extraction of arteries, it is necessary that one fill the area with old cotton and place good bandages over it; and when they are to be cut open, if it is cured with dry medicines that cause heat, and bandages, until it heals; and if without a tourniquet from the artery as you operate, hurry to cover it with cautery or use vitriol on your hand so that the area does not bleed; and if this is not present, place your finger over the area until it congeals, and rub the area with cold water until it stops bleeding, and bind it as necessary; and that which is softened and lighter in the extraction of the artery, you should cauterize the vein from this sharp cautery cutting two parts, but the cuts should be thick to keep its heat longer.
Car quant li estrumens est trop tenves, si tient moins sa chalor.	For when the strings are too thin, it holds less its heat.
Et doit avoir entre les .ij. coutelz .i. doit de gros d’espaice, et puis quant tu as signiet d’enche les .ij. leus, et tu mes lou fer ardant sus tant qu’il viegne jusc’a l’os, et cope la voinne en .ij. leus; et soient esloigniet entre les .ij. chiés car il n’est mie soudez de cest cautere dou tout en tout; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And it should have between the 2 incisions, one deep and wide apart, and then when you have signed the incision of 2 places, and heat the iron hot above until it reaches the bone, and cut through the vein in 2 places; and they must be separated between the 2 heads because it is not bonded all over with this cautery; and this is the form of the cautery:
des larmes	And the tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont dessendans des voinnes que sont sus lou test dou chief de fuer, et il ne profite mie cure de medicine c’on i faice, et tu vois la faice dou malaide enrougir, et sent ou front ambulation si com de fremis; et sui oil sont tenve et moiste si que li poil des papieres sont cheut, et sont eschaufees les papieres, et escorchies de l’ardor des larmes, si ait mestier de ceste cure.	When the tears of the eyes are flowing from veins located on the forehead above the head, and it does not benefit from any medicine that is applied, and you see the patient writhing in pain as if with fever; and when they are thin and moist to the point that hair falls out like paper, and the skin around the eye area is burnt and scorched by the tears, this requires this kind of treatment.
Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai .iij. fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front; et soit l’une des fendures ausi com .ij. doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres .ij. as .ij. costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as .ij. costez par desus les papieres; et aloigne ta main de la continuation des .ij. mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de .iij. dois au traver joins;	And they called the ancients "cure contuse", and you shall do this to the patient who has this disease: shave his head from the front, then make three cuts or the same length on the forehead according to the length of the forehead; one cut should be like two fingers below the eyebrows going straight down until the nose, and the other two should be in the temples above the eyebrows, and avoid cutting the arteries that are in the temples above the eyebrows; keep your hand away from the connection of the jaws, and each wound shall have the size of three fingers together.
et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de .ij. pars de coi ci est li forme:	and take a piece of sponge and dampen it with linen to squeeze the blood, then insert the sharp spatula of two parts in this shape:
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision; et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les .ij. fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	from the incision that is at the temple up to the second incision; and scrape all the cartilage that is between the two cuts along the entire bone, then continue from the middle incision up to the other second one, and then pull out this spatula.
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	Push the instrument called "cultellaire" into the first opening. It is very sharp on one side and soft, not sharp, on the other side, and it is shaped like this:
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure. Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer; et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris; puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne; et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then cut the vessels that descend from the eye to the hairs, until the incision is continuous up to the opening of the wound, and then make another incision on the other side; and then drain the blood equally, and press the area for the blood taken; then put a piece of old cotton in each opening, and place damp linen soaked in vinegar, oil, and asafoetida over it, and ensure that no pus comes out; on the third day, remove the suture, and apply great heat from mustard plaster, then the treatment with ointment of basilicon with rose oil, and other treatments for wounds until it is healed.
dou reume des eulz	The root of the hairs
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees; et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue; adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	When anyone comes with an acute catarrh, you often see the eyes swell and become small, blur vision, burn paper, hair falls out, and a headache ensues at great pain; and the patient coughs; then recognize these signs that such materials and this catarrh do not come from anywhere but from many veins, and the remedy for the cure is in it, if it is this.
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large. i. poc. Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os; et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier; et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les .ij. levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin; puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut; quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	And command the patient to recline their head, then make a large cut on the back of the head, and another deep one. Then start from the incision of the left temple to the right temple, and let the incision reach the bone; and keep your hand away from the nerves of the temples that move when eating; and when the bone is exposed, suck out all the blood with a sponge, and then apply cotton between the two edges of the cut and bandage it with linen; then place damp linen cloths on it and guard against hot abscess; when the bone is removed, you must rub the bone until char begins to grow, then treat with things that encourage char growth.
En teil maniere: pren .ij. parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine .iiij. parties, et en fai emplaustre; et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	In this way: take two parts of wheat flour and four parts of colophony, and make a poultice with it; then administer it to the wounds to encourage char growth everywhere.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	Of the stoppage of the ears
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des .iiij. choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	Anything that falls into the ears is one of the four things: grains, beasts, stones or similar items such as iron; or seeds, peas, beans; or something flowing like water and similar substances.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel. Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction; et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine; et estent l’oreille au desus. Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	If a stone or other foreign object falls into the ear and does not fit properly in the ear, or it becomes swollen in the ear, place the ear in the sun. If you can see the stone, apply a few drops of violet oil or camphor oil, then administer extraction; and make the patient sneeze with ginger, and plug the nostrils when the sneezing comes, and put pieces of cloth or wool around the ear; and hold it upwards. Many times pus is produced by this cure; and if it does not produce pus, use fine tweezers for extraction as follows:
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin; se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure; et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne; puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit; et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor; puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	If it jumps out at the hinges, that's good; if not, introduce extraction with a subtle hook of small thickness; and if it doesn't jump out by this means, make a thread of wax and push the head of the thread or earplug strongly, stop the area around the thread with melted wax so that the air can't enter with the thread; then pull firmly, for many times it comes out as we have said; and if it doesn't come out in this way, take some glue and catch the animals, and put any suitable instrument on top of it; and place a piece of cotton around it; then press the glue on the stone or something else, and pull firmly.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme; et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant; et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche; et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it doesn't jump out from all the things we have said, then hurry to cut the ear when abscess pus comes and spasms; and the method of cutting is that you first anesthetize the patient with a head anesthetic, draw blood according to the measure of its potency, then make the patient sit between your hands and turn the ear upwards, and make a small cut in the root of the ear where the fat or skin depends; let the cut be like a crescent moon until you reach the bone, then extract it with all your might, and suck it quickly into your mouth; and heal it until it is healed.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction; et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre .i. spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	And if it is grains that have entered and swell, apply extraction; and if it cannot be extracted, apply a thin, fine spatula in this form:
et amenistre incision de celui grain. Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces; puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	And make an incision in that grain. However, do not do so if you think the grain is moist due to moisture from the ear, until you have made many pieces; then extract it using fine tweezers and a sucker, as we have said, to ensure the extraction is aligned.
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton. Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est. s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin. se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu; et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille; et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer; et se tu vues, si prent .i. jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars; puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	Then the patient should use ear drops of strong condysum and stuff the ear with old cotton. The patient must lie on the same side where the water has fallen. If it jumps out because of this, that is good. If not, take many small and light pieces of straw, heat them slightly in the fire; then have the patient put one end of the straw into his ear and hold the other end with a pair of tweezers from the other side, and press another piece of straw onto the straw in the ear; continue pressing the straw against the straw in the ear until the water jumps out completely, and when you see it jump out, take one thread, insert one end into the ear, and burn the other end with fire as much as the thread is burned; then repeat this process with more threads until the water has all come out, as we have said earlier.
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division; mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures; et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	In the removal of the beast (insect), if it is small, like fleas and similar creatures, treat it as we have said earlier; but if it is large enough to feel, then use extraction with tweezers; and it is easier to remove what is in the ear with lighter tools.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil: s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	In the extraction of worms in the ear, when you treat it as we have said in the division and where to administer distillations, if it does not improve, you must observe the ear in sunlight; if any worms open, remove them with subtle tweezers, if no worms appear, take a string of this shape:
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus. Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine; fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent. Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere; et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations; et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	Make it narrow at the bottom and wide at the top. Push the most subtle part of the string into the ear according to the severity of the patient's pain, then pull the entire string; do this repeatedly until all the worms come out.
