If they don't emerge, stop up the string with cotton as I said earlier; if no worms protrude as we have mentioned, administer distillations that the ancients have tested in the treatment of worms, and you will find them where to administer distillations or treat distillations; and if you distill your oils and medicines into the ear with this device as shown, you will find it here:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a .i. petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller; et por presser dedens la distillation a .i. estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren .i. raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton; puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille; puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille; et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations .i. poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille; et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	And let it be of silver or brass narrow at the bottom with one small opening and wider on top for distillation; and to press within the distillation, use a well-made device made of brass; if you see, take a scraper and wrap cotton around the tip; then pour your oil or liquid and whatever medicine you wish into the string, and place it in the ear. Then push the scraper with all the cotton inside to press the medicine and distill the oils or liquids from the ear. The patient will smell it inside, and let the distillation be one heated pot as when it is distilled in the ear; but make sure it's not too cold, for the medicine will not be as effective.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	Of the stoppage of ears
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient .i. poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	No child is born without any perforation in the ears; and this same thing happens to adults due to ear injury or pus coming from within the ear, and this perforation sometimes occurs completely inside the ear if it cannot be seen; and sometimes there is only a small hole perforated and it can be easily seen.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	Therefore, if the perforation is not visible, it is difficult to treat in various positions, and in this case you must place the sick person's ear in the sun and look inside. If you see the opus (pus) appearing, then open the perforation with this spatula shaped as follows:
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille; se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	And it should be cauterized and incised in front and behind completely, so that it does not touch the ear; if the opening is of cartilage or bone of the ear, hold it with fine tweezers and lightly crush it until all the cartilage is crushed.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren .i. raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille. Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille; puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	If the opening is at the front of the ear, take a fine and sharp razor and heat it slightly over the fire, then place it in the cartilage of the ear. If you feel the opening from which the patient feels pain in the ear, make a small incision, but be careful not to injure the nerves of the ear; then put a bandage of appropriate size into the ear and moisten it with Egyptian ointment.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet; et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Do this every day until the wound heals, or take a bandage and moisten it with rose water and powdered vitriol broken; if you see the ear swell, then it is necessary to pull out the bandage and insert another bandage moistened with cerote made of rose oil and beeswax until the swelling disappears; then treat it until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	And when bleeding comes, dip a sponge and cloth in cold water, put it on the ear, and use other treatments that stop the bleeding which are either to treat distillations.
de la char des papieres	of the charcoal from paper (this likely refers to a substance used for healing or treating wounds)
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	This althelul that comes from paper leaves when they are moist and dry should be stretched with tweezers and forceps, then scraped with a spatula at its roots; then place it on the wound covered in vitriol (a type of acid).
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues; et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines; et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	And if no incision is made, the subtle lancet cautery should be used on the cauterized spot, and it is beneficial to cauterize after the incision; and many times they heal, since nothing remains from their roots; and when they are cauterized by fire, those roots are burned and do not return.
de la gresle	Of the hailstorm
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope. se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	Many times hail-like things come in papers that appear similar in shape and hardness, and because of this, the disease is called "grandine," which is a thick collection of moisture on the paper above and below; the remedy is as follows: Take care if the hailstorm becomes muted from one side or the other, and it is an easy thing to know; then make an incision on both sides, then peel off each part lightly, take it with the tweezers and squeeze. If you cannot cover it without piercing the paper a little, do not worry the patient; and if the tear is large, gather it in stitches, and cure it until it is healed; and if it is small, do not apply force because the oilmen restore it soon and cause pain.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	And if the grains (small particles) are descending within the ear towards the upper part, turn the paper and hold the grains with tweezers, and press it from both sides; and if the paper is moved by the incision, it doesn't matter; and when the grain is pressed, apply salty oil to it, and heal the wound of the one who suffers pain until the patient is healthy.
de la graisse des eulz	from the fat of the eyes (eyelids)
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil. Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	Exinach is a fat rendered in paper-like cloths, and this happens more often with children than with adults, and it causes them great pain, and they come down with catarrh at mornings, and cannot bear the light of the sun because their eyes are watery; and therefore they lie on their faces immediately, and sleep on top of it, and their paper is damp under their eyelids covered by the exinach that opens in oil. And when you press the place with your fingers and feel the exinach between them.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain; et puis pren .i. drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li; et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle; puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne; et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach; et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	And the method of the work is that the patient places their head on a pillow; and then takes one linen cloth, and prepares a tent in the shape of a circle according to the quantity that contains exirnach from each part, then puts it below; and presses with your hands on both sides, so that exirnach is assembled inside the circle; then they make an incision in the middle of the moisture with a sharp spatumile, but not too large than the wound one makes to open a vein; and cut the skin completely until you see the exirnach; and in many positions, exirnach comes out from the incision, according to the shape of a piece of white fat.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars; et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	Then stretch out a piece of folded cloth between your hands and turn your hand to both sides until it is spread; and be careful not to injure in the incision, that you do not go too deep with the spatumile, that you do not cut it open.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere; puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	If the exirnach does not open at the beginning of the incision, then slightly raise the incision to make it appear; then stretch out as we have said, then wet cloths with oil and water, and place them on the wound, and hold down bandages.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree. Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez. Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if such men break the seal and put it over to corrupt that moisture which has remained. Then cure it until it is healed. If it comes to an abscess hot, then heal it with poultices soothing until it is healed.
des poilz des papieres	the hairs of paper
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc .iiij. manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	When hairs grow from paper other than nature, and are nurtured, they harm the eyes and bring about ways of diseases such as common tears and albugine, until it is a cause of destruction of the eyes; and there are four methods of cure: either by cautery together with fire, or by medicine according to what is before in this chapter on cautery, and it is done either by incision and stitching or by caustics, according to what I will say.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre; s’elle est convertie, c’est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout .i. fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai .i. fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit; puis estrai .i. fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	It is necessary that you place the patient's head on your side, then turn the paper with the oil on your left hand; if it has been converted, it is good; if not, insert an awl through one of the holes; and it should be pierced through the edge of the paper where the hairs grow from those hairs, and pull one filament across the entire paper, then shave the paper; then make a hole in the part beneath the paper, below the hairs, completely filling the spatula, from the large rim to the small; then pull out one filament, and put a small tent of cotton and linen on top of the paper under where the figure is drawn, as the thorn of the myrtle; and it is necessary that the figure is according to the quantity which you wish to raise the paper that has been designated for all.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les .ij. lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit; et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des .ij. angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute; puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout .i. fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les .ij. sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce; et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a .iij. jors ou .iiij.; puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor;	And if it is necessary to apply a large quantity of the paper according to the softness of the paper; then make a hole in the entire spatula along the two lines that you have drawn, and start from the large rim to the small; and let one of the slits be near the natural hairs in the thickness of a root, then insert the awl into one of the corners of the keyhole, then scrape it all; then sew together the two lips with a needle at one filament of fine linen, and squeeze out the blood, and make the superfluous filaments adhere to the two scissors with anything sticky, if you wish to do this; and if not, do not care about it, then leave the sewing and the filaments for 2-4 days; then treat the wound without sewing with drying and constricting substances, because the paper revives at the edge of the wound and gathers it, but the sewing is rotten (as the ancients say), and this is laborious work without fear.
et si a une autre maniere: et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a .iij. oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	And if in another way: and it is that you draw the paper of a figure as the thorn of myrtle, as we have mentioned, at four openings spaced according to the form shown here:
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	Then bind that which is above the small forces equally according to the form that is here:
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait .i. fil, et la boute emmi la figure; et boute .i. autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment; puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans;	And if you have no power to hold the pincers and the things are not even, take a needle with one thread, and put it in place according to the figure; and put another thread of the large armhole, and the second thread of the small, and assemble the threads equally between your hands; then lift your hand equally, and lift the entire skin over what you have marked, as we have said, then sew the two lips of the wound together by stitching, and let it heal until it is healed; and if an abscess comes to your incision, soothe it with ointment and similar calming balms.
et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit: si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision; mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	And sometimes the hair of the papyrus is transformed: if you need to use what we have said about incision; but sewing in one and the other is more artificial.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai .ij. caines par art, et .ij. liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as .ij. chiés de .ij. pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les .ij. cainnes des .ij. parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	The treatment for dogs is as follows: First, fold the paper and place it inside as I have said, then make two cords of equal length and width similar to that of the paper and the diameter of a spatula; take the heads of two parts where you hold the strings; next, assemble one and the other subtly on top of the paper with oil, and bind the two cords from the two parts; leave it like this for some days, and the skin that is bound will die, rot, and fall off, leaving a wound.
S’il tarde, si le cope aunes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des .ij. cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	If it takes a long time or if you need to force it, then treat it until it is healed; and when the wound is closed and no more hair can be found; this is the form of the two cords that you will make according to the figure and quantity of length and width:
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute .i. fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse .i. autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a .i. ou .ij. ou .iij. ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	the work (ovraiges) is such that you take a fine needle and insert one silk thread of the same size; then assemble the cords (chiés) and align them carefully, and the length of the threads should be about one palm; then arrange another fine silk thread briefly, attach the head of the thread, put the patient's head in your hand; expose it to sunlight so that the work is done under clear conditions, as this work is subtle and small; next, insert the needle into all the hair (chasse) along the root of the hair (ajosteit), and pierce it through the paper quickly until you pull out the natural hair; then draw out the hair up to the head of the thread, and attach that hair to the thread, if there is one or two or three or more hairs; then draw your hand until the hairs come out completely from the paper along with the natural hair.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil; adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus; et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne .i. poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	And if the arrow has been expelled but hairs do not come out with it, draw out the arrow to the end you have ordered, until the arrow comes out from the wound and you see it through the oil vision; then draw out the arrow and the hairs, and let the oil close for 2 or 3 days, until the hair grows in its place and the skin forms over it; if the hairs are small, let one long hair of natural origin accompany it, and let it grow along with the one you left, until it is elongated and then remove it.
de la porriture de l’oil	The decay of oil
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de .ij. manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.  Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	When this disease called "alecrati" or decay comes in the oil, it happens in two ways: one natural and the other unnatural. It occurs suddenly from a wound, an injury, or a burn, and similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent. Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere; mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	And the method of work in it is that you cut the joint, separate the ligaments from it, put tent-like strips of flax inside, and let it heal until it is healed; and it should not be used in its treatment with things that dry and restrict. For if you do this, the disease will be worse than the first one; but the work of softening things, such as fenugreek, and the juice of water or oil and flax seeds cooked, and immediately cool down some oil, and wrap a tent around it, and cure with these.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant; et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	And the treasure of your cure is that you do not let it heal in its original form; and this treatment which we have said is not helpful unless addressing the disease in this way so that it does not return to its original form.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	of the fat coming in the oil
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens. Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans; et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait .i. fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en .ij. chiés de la char; puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a .i. spatumile large.	This sickness that is below is truly called "axacrati," and it is both natural and accidental. The accidental part comes from wounds, cuts, burns, and similar things; the way of treatment in it is that you take a needle with one double thread, and pierce it through the flesh, entering from the left tear duct to the right, so that the threads come out in two cheeks of the flesh; then the flesh is raised above the whole needle, and it is covered with a large spatula.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin; se ceu non, si pren .i. raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent .ij. fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere; et soient li chiés des .ij. fendures des .ij. angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «.j. griesche»; puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les .ij. parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne; puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the shape of the paper comes back as it should be, that is good; if not, take a rasp and place it in the wound, turn the paper, and make two wounds where the skin is inside the paper; and let the corners of the two wounds be at the angles of the incision that you made, and let it form an angle so that when they are assembled, the shape will be like the letter that has no "greek y," then remove that flesh, according to the thickness that its edges are curved underneath, from where the paper is; then join the two separated parts, and sew them with a thread of linen; then treat as we have said for the medicines softening, and tenting, until it heals.
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant; puis desevre entre les .ij. leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit; et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil; et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	And if the sickness comes from a wound or stitching or cauterization, it is necessary that you make a shallow cut below the hair on the paper, as described before; then separate between the two leathers of a tent, as I said; and the work should be done according to the shape of the disease, for it is very diverse in form, and wise masters adapt devices with all possible skill to bring the figure back to its natural form; and patients themselves, according to what is necessary for work and instruments in various positions.
dou soudement de la papiere	The swollen pain of paper (literal translation)
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut; et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil; et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil; et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere; puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef; et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	When such swelling occurs in the hand of a man as described above, where the paper is swollen with white oil and cannot move or perform its natural functions, it is necessary then to cut the point of a razor under the paper and lift it upwards; keep it between pliers until you find that which protrudes at the spatula-like part (subtle spatula), which should not be too sharp nor too deep, so that the patient does not suffer from a too sharp spatula causing injury to the oil; make your incision, from which you scrape the assembled matter, gently, so that the paper returns to its natural form; and heal the entire assembled matter, sometimes making the oil sour and adding sweet warm collyrium; then put a linen tent between the paper and the oil, and place damp wool over the oil abundantly with egg; after three days, use the collyrium and other healing substances until it is healed.
de l’ungle de l’oil	The nail of the oil (literal translation)
Saiches que li ungle est selonc .ij. manieres: elle est nervouse et semblans a .i. dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om; et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	Know that the nail has two types: one is nerve-like and resembles hard wax, and another which is not nerve-like but resembles frozen white moisture; when it is touched by iron and cooked with tweezers, it cannot be removed; and both seem to start towards the large root, and grow little by little until they cover the entire view and light and the movement of the oil.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz; et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus; puis pren une aguille, et i met .i. poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et .i. fil fort; et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement; et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit; puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	And the method of incision is that the patient places his head on your healthy hand, then you pull out the nails; and tear off the paper with your hand, then take tweezers to remove the nail, and hold it above; then take a needle, and put a horse hair or ox hair, or strong thread on it, and double the tip of the needle slightly and poke it into the nail, and pierce it all through with the needle, tie the nail with the thread and hold it above, and scrape off all the hair from the side of the nail that follows the cuticle and the silk to the hair up to the head, then chip away the remaining in the root of the big toe with a small chisel and fine tools, and leave the natural flesh or big toe as usual; and sometimes the nails are set on the incision only, and along the fillet, as we have said; then scrape off all the soft tissue from where this shape is formed:
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie; et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	And ensure that the soft tissue does not touch the skin and tear it, and that the cuticle is not pierced; and after incision, drop a little bit of crushed oil in the wound, and let the oil of collyrium made from litargirius remain until the next day; then treat whatever is necessary until it is healed.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines; et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	And if the nail is not nerveous and you cannot insert the needle, and the uncines cannot enter, many times this appearance of the nail is cured with medicines; and they grow as I have told in the division, and if you see it covered, it works the oil of the patient, and take the spatumile lightly pointed according to this form:
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor; puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	Then gently lift the nail and if you see it does not thin out or reduce in size, apply pressure to it. Then distill from your mouth into the oil of collyrium made from litargyre and red collyrium and pulverized, and anoint the oil until the next day; then repeat the procedure as before until it is completely removed.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If nothing is contrary to it in the oil (as with an abscess), then lait (milk) should be applied and the abscess should be treated hot until it is healed, then continue the procedure as before until it is healed.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne; puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	And if the appearance of the flesh near the armpit harms in oil greatly, suspend it at the neck, and cut a part but not too much, so that tears do not come; then distill in the oil collyrium which is made from litarge.
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	of the flesh which grows above the eyeball
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste; et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force; puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tune bleces l’oil a l’ovraige; et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre;	The eyelids of some men sometimes grow red flesh, and cover the eyeball and press upon the paper and turn it outward, and seem like a rosebud from a balustrade; and the remedy for this is that the patient should place his head in the bowl, then open the eyelids, and remove all the red flesh to the appropriate uncinations (eyebrow areas), and hold it with force; then cut off the first layer of the red flesh, and continue cutting towards the razor until the end, but be careful not to wound the oil during the procedure; and make the incision with a spatula as mentioned in the treatment for the nail and the small bones around the nail, as described by the form after this chapter.
et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut; et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut; puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	And when the incision is completed and all the flesh is cut, apply the oil of seil crushed or you distill red collyrium and similar corrosive medicines, and put cotton soaked with egg white on top to ensure proper healing; and if anything remains, and the wound becomes cold, and you doubt whether it is properly healed, leave the oil and heal the wound with things that calm inflammation; then return to your work until it is sound, and do this whenever a wound is treated in this way with oil by this means.
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil; et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer; et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	Nevertheless, you must reduce the treatment of each oil by natural means; and in case of accidental work with iron, do not put your hand into any of these works until you see that this limb can bear that work.
des voines des eulz	of veins of the eyes
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors. Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel; adonques le coil en teil maniere: comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	The first red veins which are covered above the eye, and it reveals its work and weakens the oil every day. Therefore, it is necessary for you to first examine whether the oil, where the red vein is, is healthy or if there is any other disease except the red vein; then instruct the patient to put his head in your hand, then press those veins all along their length according to one's wisdom, and let the pressure be subtle double according to this form:
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en .i. cors selonc ceste forme:	And there should be two degrees of pressure in one fold according to this form:
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil; et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes; et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	Then press those veins subtly, and squeeze out the blood hour by hour until you see the veins moving away from the oil; and make sure not to prick the oil with the tips of the lancets, and perform this procedure at noon before the sun, and be very warm in your work so that you do not spoil the veins; and when you have completed this, if it distills green and red oils, it will correct those who are affected by the sebel.
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme des forces:	And if you cannot bind all of it in that hour, apply a plaster on oil of calming things to the pain of the eyes, and leave it for some days until the pain is alleviated and assured of healing, then resume as before according to this method until it is healed; and this is the form of forces.
de la fistule de l’oil	of the fistula of oil
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule: quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	The sore called "arissati" fistula: when you cure it by cautery and burning medicine as I have previously said, and it is not healed, there is a trick in it that you should cut open the abscess where it must rot, and drain all the moisture that is in it, until the bone is exposed.
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme; et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a .i. chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	And when the bone is exposed, and you will see corruption and blackness; if it needs to be scraped with all the tools mentioned here, it is called a "rough head," and should be scraped circularly once with a tool shaped like a chisel and pointed like a limer.
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese; et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	And place the level over the bone corruption, then turn it between your hands and press your hand slightly so that you feel that the corruption is removed; do this once, then restore the level of healing balms.
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi xl. jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez; se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme: et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent .i. foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a .iij. angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	If the joint is sutured and char comes out, and the bone of the bow is sutured and remains so for 40 days without reverting or becoming abscessed, and no evil accident occurs (knowing that it is healthy); if this does not happen, there is no other remedy but to return the fistula to the point of the navel according to this form: you must expose the bone a second time with iron, and with healing medicines, and when it is exposed, take one awl according to this form, and make the head of the awl at four angles, and let the shaft be attenuated up to the tip as you see here.
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil .i. poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif; si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	Then put it on the dislocated bone of the elbow, and move your hand away from the oil (ointment). Then turn the whole instrument all the way until it penetrates the bone and the patient feels it if they hold their hand on the affected area; and then restore the joint with dry medicines as I have shown you, and when the flesh grows and hardens, the matter goes to the affected area; it is easier for the patient.
de l’issue de l’oil	of the dislocation
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide; puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil .i. liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz; et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en .iiij., et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier; puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir; puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout; puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin; se ce non; si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the eyes are fully open in all places and do not move at all, there is no need to bind it (the patient); then clean it, then put on poultices or hot irons for healing, then apply oil made from acacia and aloe and incense and saracocolla, and hold the oil, and anoint it with bandages and cloths; and the manner of the cloths is that you take soft cloths, fold each one in four, and put one on top of another according to the size that the eyes require; then bind them with a strong bandage, and repeat the poultices for healing without injuring it; then remove the poultices and leave the oil held tight day and night, and if the liniment becomes soft, you must bind it tightly; then remove the linen after the day and night, and if you see the eyes heal, that is good; if not, repeat the anointing and the cloths and the liniment until it heals.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	the bursting of a water bladder
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com .i. grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir; adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait .i. fil double des la partie dou larmier; et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition; puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef; et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee; et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	When rupture occurs in the water bladder, it bursts and paper-like matter comes out like a grain of resin, and is very frightening to see; then if you cover it, the treatment is such that you push an awl into the root of the affected part all the way up to its top, then push another awl or double-filed needle from the edge of the bladder area; and make it pierce through, leaving the first awl in place according to its position; then bind the end of the double filament with a piece of linen and tighten, then remove the awl and put moistened flax oil on it; and leave it until the filaments stick with the bladder, then treat the oil with healing substances until the wound is healed; and sometimes the wound is kept closed by the bladder on each side of a circular piece of cloth, until it is healed.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost; puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the eyes seem to be large in appearance, pierce them with a thin spatula that comes from oil and cure the moisture and pus, then insert some immediately; then remove it when healed.
de la bowe de l’oil	Of the bone of the oil
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus .i. siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de .ij. pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit. si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee .i. poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	This disease called "alcunnati" is not caused by anything other than the bone in the oil assembly resembling an ulcer and it is not an ulcer; its appearance during surgery looks like a seated patient. Then you should take hold of his head with both hands, make him move so that you see the bone come up to your eyes. Then it should be fixed, and let the light shine through and let the patient see things as he usually does. If it does not discharge below, know that it is an ulcer, and if the discharge from the bone is not properly arranged as we have said. Place the seated patient in your hands, then take the thin spatula and place it under the corneal sheet and the crown, along the continuous junction with the corneal sheet and the crown, until the bone protrudes. When it is issued, it will distill into hot oil mixed with honey or ulcer-healing herbs boiled together with honey, and then it should be treated with another remedy until it heals.
des aigues de l’oil	of the waters in the oil
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit. Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre. se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	We have the appearance of the artery in division, and that which is required to pierce; proceed according to health. You must make the patient sit between your hands crossed, away from light due to the sun, and hold the oil clean and press it very firmly; then place the paper of the oil on your left hand if the eyes are on the left, or on your right hand if they are on the right; then take with your right hand, if the eyes are on the left, the instrument called "almagda", or your left hand, if they are on the right; then place the point of the instrument near the corona through the thickness of a nail in that part of the oil where the minor tear is, then push the instrument called "almagda" firmly, and hold your hand as long as it pierces the oil, and feel that almagda comes to the empty place; and it must be that the measure of the path of almagda should be at the full depth of the measure of the space from the pupil to the end of the nose; and this is the corona of the oil; then you will see the bone in that paper due to the clarity of the corneous cloth, and then place the instrument up to where the artery is, then press it down a path after another. If the artery is still there, the patient will see before him and the instrument in his oil.
Aprés repose .i. petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc; et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens. Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.  Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	After a short rest, and if the artery rises again in the second way, apply the force with the instrument, and when it is fully inserted and does not rise anymore, gently turn almagda around your thumb; then place another small amount of gemmed oil on it, and squeeze out this oil from within. Then put damp cloth or moistened linen soaked in rose oil and abundant egg yolk, and bind with the clean oil. We, and those of our time, put on top a layer of crushed matter with an abundance of egg yolk.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if almagda cannot enter the oil due to its hardness because some people have too hard eyes, then it is necessary that you take the instrument called "alberit", of which this is the shape:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai .i. leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide .i. dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en .j. leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	Therefore, pierce the conjunctive only, and do not go too deep, but make one shallow incision, then apply alum, as we have said; and when the work is complete, prepare a draught for the patient, in which he sleeps on his back in a dark room; be attentive to all movements, and give light foods, and let him not move his head neither to the right nor to the left, and tie him as necessary until the third day; then untie him in the same dark room, test his vision, and let him see some things, and then rebind him for seven days; do not perform this, however, during the time of the cure or immediately after the incision, but you should alleviate it, because the pain increases quickly.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice .i. orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse. Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	If an abscess comes, you should untie the oil before the seventh day and direct it towards that which soothes abscesses; and when it is soothed, then you should untie the eye and put on it one eyelet to cover for any length of time, and stay in that dark room. Then slowly leave the house a little at a time, and turn to his case; and know that no disciple should interfere in this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	And one came to us who was from Iria, who told us that in his land they pierce alum, so that the pain subsides, but I have never seen anyone do it in our land, nor have I ever read about it in old books; and perhaps this is a new thing.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	And these are the resemblances of the forms of amalgam, because those who do not recognize them will see them; and they are properly of arsenic:
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en .iij. angles ague.	And the heads of these are of the same subtlety, and the bases at four angles intersect:
de la char sor le neis	of the skin over the nose
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color. En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; puis cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	There are never born or nasal skin growths that appear different, of which there are some that resemble scorpions with many legs; and if it has a swollen char of such color, and a soft char of good color. In the case of these chars that are soft, but not swollen, you must make the patient sit between your hands in the sun; open his nostrils, and pour the onion juice over those growths, and pull them out; then hold what can be supported with a spatula thin and sharp from one side, until you know that the char is completely removed.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout .i. des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	And if any thing remains that cannot be covered, you shall open it all with subtle and light instruments, so that there is nothing left; and if there is no abscess, or the abscess is closed, help as needed; and if the abscesses are malicious, hurry and cauterize them until the pus is drained and all the charred matter is removed, then pour in oil, water, or wine.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, acoi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes .i. fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice .i. doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil. Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu .iij. jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	If the opening does not work, and moisture comes up to the palace (meaning head), know that it is healthy; and if moisture does not pierce as needed, know that there is charred matter in the bone above, which the instruments do not come to cut: then you shall take a large linen thread, about two fingers' width apart; and insert the threads into the patient's nostrils up to their power, and pull out smelling it until pus comes from the nose into the mouth; and many times children in school do this, and it is easy for those who wish to do so; then hold one head coming from the nose with one hand, and the other head coming from the mouth with the other hand, and know each other's turn as we are the ones holding the threads. Do this until you know that the threads have rotten the char; then pull out the thread, let the blood flow, and moisten the thread in Egyptian ointment, and put it back into the nose as before; do this for four days or more, until the ointment corrodes everything remaining of the char; and then put a reed of plaster in the nose for some days until it is healed, and if there is need for drying medicines, use them; and this is the shape of the instrument to purge the head, as one distills oils and medicines in the nose.
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait .i. mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And it shall be made of silver or tin, resembling a lamp with a handle, like a cane, and guide it so; and if you see, make a closed cane, and the instrument shall be full to purge the head; and have one handle on the head to hold when heating the oil or any liquid.
de la char sor le neis	About the skin near the nose
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	Many times a disease called "telul" arises near the nose, which grows and becomes large when seen; therefore, it is necessary to treat it at the beginning and completely excise it, then apply heat or burning medicine to it; if it is delayed until it becomes large, take care if it is hard, dark in color, insensitive: do not touch it with iron because it is a swollen abscess, for when it is touched once, it brings great harm to the patient; and if the abscess has soft contact and is not discolored, you can completely cover it, the patient must be warned and treated with dry remedies and binding substances.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	when the nose is cut and sutured
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes. Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les .ij. levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Know that when a solution of continuation comes to one of these cartilages, it is of little use, unless in some men. Therefore, if such a situation occurs in anyone, check if the wound is fresh with all its blood; and then bring the two lips together into a stitch, then treat it until it heals; and if the lips have already separated from both sides, you must scrape all the parts of them until they heal, then bring the two lips together into a stitch, tighten it, and sprinkle powdered dragon's blood powder on top, and incense pulverized; and place some plaster of strong or other plaster over the powders, and leave it until it dries, then treat it with ointment until it heals.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The method of stitching is that you gather the solution: either with needles, as I have told you in the abdomen stitching; or with thread, as I have informed you.
des apostemes des levres	of abscesses of lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	To the hands of men happens an abscess hard within the lips, resembling grains of various sizes, both small and large; then you must turn the lips, and cut on each side, and take it with the forceps and crush it in every part; then apply the leeches after the incision of vitriol powder, until the wound is cauterized; and then cleanse the wound with ashes, and cure the wound with dry things until it heals.
de la char des gencives	From the jawbone
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Many times an abscess arises on the jawbone that the ancients called "albulus"; then you must hold it with the forceps and crush it at its root, and let the pus flow out; then apply vitriol powder or other powders restrictive and drying to the wound; if that abscess returns after the incision, and repeatedly occurs, crush it again and cauterize it; it will not return after cauterization; these are the shapes of the instruments for covering (it).
des sordens	From the sores
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	Sometimes, sores are gathered at the head of the teeth, inside the mouth between the gums, rough and harsh scales that are ugly; and sometimes the teeth are black and yellowish and curved, until corruption comes to the gum, and the teeth stink; you must make the patient sit between your hands, with his head in your lap, and remove the sores or scales that are visible, as long as nothing remains; and in the same way do for the blackness and greenness, and yellowish and other spots, until they are removed; and if you remove what is there at the first reason, it is good; if not, start again on the second or third day and let him have everything removed; and know that the teeth require different types of instruments to be cleaned, according to what the worker demonstrates, because the tool used to clean the teeth has other forms than that used between the teeth; and these forms and others should be prepared for you.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	You should wait as long as possible when extracting a tooth for its pain, because it must not be done immediately; because this is a high substance up to which there is no excuse for shaving.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant. Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	Then, when the patient is constrained to extract a tooth, it is necessary that you are certain about which one to pull. Many times the pain deceives the patient, and believes it is a good tooth, and pulls out the bad one; however, the pain does not go away until the bad one is removed, as we have seen in the past; and when you are certain about which tooth to pull, you must scorch around the tooth with a strong spatula to protect the gums from all sides; then grasp it with your fingers or delicate pliers at the very root, and gently rock it back and forth until it is well loosened, then firmly hold the pliers; and keep the patient's chin in your saint (or hand) between your knees, and hold it still so that it does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier. Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	After pulling the tooth properly without breaking it, if it does not come out, take one of these instruments and gently push it in from each side, and move it as you have done before. And if the tooth is pierced and eaten away, it is necessary to fill it with cloth, where the rotten parts are; then carefully pull it out with pliers so that it does not break while being pulled; and work very carefully around the gum to remove the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere. Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	And be careful not to break it and leave a part behind, causing the patient greater pain from the root. Be careful that you do not act like ignorant lords who sometimes break the cart by their haste and recklessness, and do not bring about what we have mentioned; but they sometimes bring about disease through the roots that remain or the cart that is broken, as we have often seen; and when the tooth is pulled out, wash the area with wine or oil and salt; and if bleeding occurs, which often happens, use vitriol powder; and if it does not work, cauterize.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The forms of the instruments, with which one mutes (silences) the teeth first, should be of long points and thick handles, so that they do not double when you extract the tooth; and these are their shapes:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	They should be of thick handles so that they do not bend when pulling (extracting), and they should be of good iron and toothed for holding (clamping).
de la racine des dens	of the root of the teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre .i. jor ou ij., tant que li leus soit amolis, puis i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	When the root remains drawn out, you must put on it soft cotton wool in butter for 1 day or 2, until the wound heals, then insert the tongs called "algefri", which resemble the beak of a tweezers; and inside them should be made like a chisel and that is its shape:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	If the roots do not want to come out with these tongs, you must uncover all the flesh around the root, and use the instrument called "althali", which is known as a plaster, in this shape:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And it should be thick and large so that it does not break, and if the root jumps out through them, that is good; if not, help yourself with all the instruments, from which the forms come afterwards:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait .ij. rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if one helps himself with this instrument which has two prongs, here is its shape:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other iron pincers which are in front of the teeth, and of this instrument that resembles large tongs, whose shape is as follows:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	Let this instrument be made such that it cannot break, and know that many iron pincers are needed; and also other instruments, which are not counted here; and the wise masters find their own instrument by themselves according to what their work and the illness requires, for there are such diseases where the ancient did not teach an instrument due to diversity among them; and if it breaks a chariot or any other bone, where it could have helped, then let him seek the instruments that he needs, as I have told you, and help with movements, whose shape is as follows:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And let them be large and firm to hold the bone so that it does not slip, but can be held and removed; and then restore the joint with the appropriate medicines, and if there is pus in the bone, which is small, use this instrument to clean it all:
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a .i. petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When teeth appear not according to natural form and the shape is ugly, especially in girls, if you know that the tooth has not yet grown after the dent, and it is not properly aligned, and cannot be filed or trimmed: remove it; and if it is near the gum with the tooth, take this instrument with the shape of a small beak, and made of sharp iron on the end:
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And the sharp-pointed instrument is used for many hours due to the hardness of the tooth, and because you do not move the others, and if it appears that it can be filed, file it with a flat file shaped like this:
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	And so it is like the lime with which they make needles; and in the lime, the tooth little by little wears down gently, so that it does not move until it wears away completely; then the flat surface is smoothed out with any file, and if the dent is too sharp and pierces the tongue, it is necessary to smooth the sharpness until it is even, so that it does not pierce the tongue or corrupt the speech.
quant li dent lochent	when the teeth are loose
