Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les .ij. dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a .i. ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper. Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des .ij. dens sains, et des .ij. meus, si com tu vois:	When the teeth become loose, either from percussion or falling out, and the patient cannot chew food without it falling out, and you treat them with tightening medicines, it is not effective; rather, they should be tightened with a gold thread. Silver threads become green and moldy, but gold does not change. The thread should be neither too thick nor too thin, according to the space between the teeth. If you want to align the teeth, take the thread and double it between two healthy teeth, then place the loose teeth in between the healthy ones, whether there is one or more, until you reach the healthy tooth on the other side. Then, continue covering up as far as you started, and hold your hand delicately and skillfully, so that they do not move. Your knot should be at the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape. Then, take the loose teeth with tweezers, assemble them, and place them back between the healthy teeth, ensuring they do not pierce the tongue. Leave them in this position for as long as possible, and if they slip or the thread breaks, tighten it with another thread; if it lasts and serves for a while, it is the form of the tooth and the alignment of the two healthy teeth and the loose teeth, as you see:
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when the tooth falls out, if one puts it back in its place, freshly, as we have said; and let no one interfere who is not wise and patient, and sometimes a bone fragment of an animal's tooth is shaped to fit, and one places it at the site where it is missing, and holds it in place as we have said, and lets it stay for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	To cover the ligament of the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder. Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	Sometimes there arises under the tongue or nearby, a ligament that is not naturally present; or by accident due to a sealed wound. The work involves opening the mouth of the patient and holding his head straight, then lifting the tongue. Next, you should separate the nerve-like ligament widely enough for the tongue to be dislocated from its place, and if it is tough or hard, and caused by a sudden wound, push in the uncinate bone and tie it off widely. Make sure the cut is not too deep, as there is an artery underneath. Once you have done that, lift the swollen area with rose water and a soft cloth, then put a linen tent under the tongue. The patient should bite on it each night to prevent it from healing. If there is discharge of blood, apply vitriol powder; if the wound breaks open, cauterize it with the slow-burning cautery (which is good for this). Then treat it with another remedy until it heals.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the swelling appears dark or hard to the sight of the sick person, do not touch it because it is a cancer; and if it is declining towards decay, and there is moisture, throw onion juice over it, and pierce it with a thin spatula from both sides; and if it resists your work, place powdered vitriol above it until it becomes dry; then remove the lees and the pus, and treat it with other remedies until it heals.
des apostemes de la gorge	for abscesses in the throat
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les .ij. amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer. Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez. Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	Sometimes there come into the throat boils called "godath", and they are properly called the two almonds. When you treat them as we have said in the division, and they do not heal, be careful: if it is a hard abscess of small size and dark color, do not touch it with iron. And if it is red and the root is thick, do not touch it with iron for fear of bleeding; but let it remain until it softens, and then you will cut it open, or it will burst by itself; and if it is white in color and the root is thin, prepare the instrument to cover it, but first check that the abscess is calm and pacified. Then have the patient sit before the sun, and his cheeks should be in your hand, and he opens his mouth and you take the servant between his hands, and press the tongue under the entire instrument, as follows; and it should be made of silver or thin brass like a knife:
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	Can you press the tongue with this instrument and observe the abscess? If so, take the awl and poke it into the abscess and draw it up above as much as possible; do not bring anything from the linen with it, then strike it with the instrument in the shape of a cross or a forceps; even though the head is bent, and one part is against another, and they are sharp, they are made of iron or bone.
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this instrument at hand, strike it with pliers, in the shape of which is a cross or forceps.
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les .ij. amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les .ij. amandres igament.	And it should be cut through on one side and named on the other; and when you have struck one of the abscesses, strike the other in the same way, and after the incision gargarize (cleanse) the patient with hot, sharp, and acidic material, and if bleeding occurs, gargarize the patient again or use scorched pomegranate rind or myrtle leaves, and similar things until the blood is stopped; then cure it until it heals; and at times other abscesses than the two will appear in the throat, strike them in the same way as the two equally.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir .i. aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi .i. jor ou .ij. Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis .ij. rains par les .ij. pertuis dou neis. Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un .i. oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	I will treat a woman with an abscess inside her throat, meaning a small abscess; it had already been very tightly closed the entire throat, so that the woman could not breathe through the blocked passage, and could neither eat nor drink, and would have died within a day or two. The abscess was so large that it had filled two hollow spaces through the neck. I made a hole immediately, and pierced once, then pulled it out, and took out a large piece of pus; then I sewed up the other opening in the throat, and opened her mouth and pressed her tongue; afterward, I pierced the abscess again, cut off a part of it, and only a little blood came out; and thus the passage was unblocked from the woman's throat, and she began to drink water and then wine, and did not stop cutting away at the abscess for a long time; the abscess grew back again, filled up the space that I had seen, until it became very large; then I tricked it and cauterized it inside her throat: thus the growth stopped; and I left those parts alone, and may God do what he will with them afterwards.
de l’uve	a woman with an abscess
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve». Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li. Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide. Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a .i. des .ij. estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des .ij. amandres. Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des .ij. amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee. Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor. Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague. Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	1. When the anus retreats into the urethra and is long, it is called "perpendicular"; and if it is swollen and round, it is called "urethra". When it is treated as we have said in the division, and the treatment does not improve, and you see that the large abscesses are subsiding, and it is subtle, you must cut it; and the one that is rounded and not long; and it is red or of a dark color or black, you must avoid cutting into it. For there is great danger for the patient. Therefore, when you see it, according to the method that I have said, of its shape and length, you should make the patient sit before the sun, and press his tongue with the instrument that we have mentioned earlier in this treatise; then pierce the anus, draw it out, and cut it at .i. to .ij. places that I have mentioned in the incision of the two wounds. And you must not cut beyond the natural boundary; for if you do so, it will cause pain and words. After the incision, use what we have said in the incision of the two wounds, and treat it until it is healed. And if the patient fears to be cut, you must use an instrument for cauterization to alleviate his fear. The method of cauterization is sharp and hot. And it is that the patient puts his head in your hand, and then presses his tongue with the instrument that we have mentioned or chapter of caution, and hold it with hot coals, so that it is not too thick nor too clear; and use the handle of this instrument, which has this form:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés .iiij. jors ou .v. Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And have a hair or some medicine, like the handle of a spoon, and place the instrument with all the medicine on the anus; and let the patient lie on his side so that saliva and mucus flow from his mouth into the medicine, so that it does not enter the throat and the bladder; then hold your hand over the entire medicine and press it on the anus, for the amount of half an hour, until you see it swell and the bites of the medicine are alleviated; and if you see, take cotton and wrap it around some instrument, and moisten the cotton in the medicine, and stick the instrument with all the cotton into the sheath above, so that the cotton adheres to the anus; and do this often, until the cauterization is perfect, then let it dry, and wait for 4 or 5 days. And if you need to start the cauterization of the medicine again, start it again, and after the cauterization, suck out the pus around the anus, with a cotton swab dipped in butter, and clean what is around the medicine; and wash it with cold water, and treat it with gargarisms until it is healed.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en .i. pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait .i. estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This cure is more effective than incision, not just cautery; if it is treated by fumigation in this manner, take camphor and hyssop and origanum and rue and chamomile and wormwood and similar herbs, gather them all or some of these in one pot, and put it all inside, and let it boil; the pot should be well sealed with strong clay, and within the pot have one hollow instrument like this:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut. Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	And it should be of silver or brass, and the one end should be inserted into the mouth of the patient as long as the vapors rise to the eye through the tube until the eye is deadened; afterwards repeat often, until the eye dries up, and make sure not to do this at the beginning of the abscess's hot stage, because many things may happen; and do not do it if there is no hollow instrument present. If this instrument is not available, take a tube and place an eggshell crack within the patient's mouth so that the patient's mouth does not get too hot; for the eggshell will not let the vapor weigh on the mouth, and it is good cure combined with health.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou .i. morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge .i. fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren .i. estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Many times it is necessary to insert into the throat a bone or fish spine, or any other object; therefore you must pull out what you can see, and press the tongue against the instrument until you see movement in the object; and if it does not open up and remains lodged in the throat, you must make the patient vomit before the meat is cooked in the stomach; by chance, this may expel the object through vomiting. Or the patient swallows a piece of sponge, or a piece of wool, or a root of lettuce, or one morsel of dry bread. Tie a thread to the sponge, and then swallow it. When it reaches the place, it will adhere, and you will pull it out; and if it does not come out as we have said, take one plunger in this shape:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	And let the instrument be curved at the top so it can more easily enter the throat, and lift the head high; watch that you do not touch the epiglottis, for it should not come loose or push the bone inside; it is better that the patient pushes the instrument, because they are able to move or the thing is already moved; if it goes down, or you pull it out all the way to the instrument equally, until it comes out.
de la sansue de la gorge	From the throat incision
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit. Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout .i. petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu. Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine .i. fer chaut, et fai ce sovent. Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor. puis pren plein .i. voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	Sometimes medicine is used on the throat, as I said in the division, by means of medicines; and when this does not help, then look at the throat of the patient in the sun, afterwards press the tongue with the instrument I told you about. If you see the throat, cut it open with a small knife or thin pliers that are suitable for this purpose. If this is not effective, take a hair-covered string, and put it into the throat of the patient, then push or turn a heated iron on the end of the string frequently. And anoint the patient with cold water all day. Then take a full glass of cold water, open the mouth, and pour it into the mouth without swallowing, and move it around with your hand often; and as soon as the throat feels the water, it will vomit.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier. Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes .i. pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	And if it does not fall as we have said, then subdue the patient with asefetide in the instrument that I have mentioned for fumigation of the eye; do this many times, for it will be stubborn. The method of fumigation is that you take one pot or one containing charcoal, and cover the opening of the instrument with a perforated cloth; then pour your fumigation into it, and have the patient hold the head of the cane in their mouth, and close the mouth so that no smoke escapes, but comes only as far as the nose; and the nose will now be affected, and if it does not fall, repeat the fumigation many times; let the patient endure thirst, and eat salty and acidic foods, and drink nothing of water; and then it will be necessary for it to come out under this governance.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	The form of the instrument with which one treats the nose, is, when it can be seen, resembling crooked pliers for entering the throat; and having the shape of a syringe, and having an asperity of lime, so that what it takes, it cannot release; here is the form:
li chapistres des apostemes	The chapter of abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en .ij. manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor. Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors. car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	According to the memory that comes afterwards in this book from one and another, many resemble abscesses, and they are diverse in perforation and cutting; and it is in two ways, of which one is like itself and depending on whether it holds moisture. And the second way is by the organs or parts where it is located. For abscesses of the head are different from those of the foundation, and abscesses of the charnut lews are different from those that come in jointures; and each one should have its own judgement in the work.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures. Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre. Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	If one has abscesses, it should not be perforated until the bowel is ripe according to its accomplishment; and if there are those that require perforation when they are hardened, but do not die according to their accomplishment, such as abscesses that come from jointures. For when an abscess comes from jointures, and it is left until it is surrounded by pus, perhaps the ligament and nerve of the jointure become corrupted, which causes contraction in that member. Or the abscess is from the principal member, and if you delay perforation too long until it is ripe, it will harm the principal member; or it is from the foundation, if it is perforated before it is ripe; and it should not be perforated without accomplishment of digestion except for those that are from the foundation, which should not burst out and become long inside, and a fistula should form; and it will not heal in a great term.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	And you should know the sign of the perforation of an abscess that is healed according to completion; and this is when pain is eased, and the departure of fever, and the diminishing of pain and redness, and the settling and narrowing of the head of the abscess, and other signs; and you should make it sit where the perforation is more dependent on the abscess, and where it has opened out; and let the perforation be along the length of the body, and if the abscesses are at the hands or feet, or in joints and nerves and arteries, and in all equal places or where there is no opening.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre. Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit. Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui. Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.  Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com .i. drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en .iij. angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	In those that close, according to the affected limb. And when abscesses are in fleshy areas, it is best to leave the perforation until it is confirmed in complete digestion, as we have said. For if you pierce it before this, the body will drain out from it, and it will be filled with much pus; and possibly harden the lips and deeply penetrate it. And for any abscess that are pierced according to the width of the body, according to what the limb requires. And you should bring forth small abscesses, small punctures; and in large abscesses, large punctures, and many slits according to the likeness of the size of the abscess; and if it is necessary to cover such abscesses, you should sew them; when they have become as thin as cloth, and are softened, it is necessary to do as with babies: and if there are those that are cut into four angles, and if there are those from which one covers like the myrtle leaf, as abscesses in joints; and if there are those where one makes a round incision, and other similar incisions and coverings.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites. Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois. Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Those without a head, such as a superficial abscess, it is necessary that you pierce it completely; and when the abscesses are large, and they have gathered much pus, and you pierce it, do not drain all the pus in that hour, but drain some part of it; then stop up the abscess until the next day, then drain nothing crookedly; do this many times gradually, until the pus disappears. This is especially necessary if the patient is weak, or a woman carrying a child, or small children, or elderly people in decline. For the pus sometimes jumps out with the drainage, which may cause the death of the patient, and you will not be at fault. Therefore, avoid this chapter with great caution, and when you have pierced your abscess, clean the wound, and check if the wound from the abscess is small; and if it is a deep wound, bring in strips of linen or old cotton; and if it is a large abscess, and there is much draining, it is necessary that you stick in a strip in each one so that they meet; and if you have sewn part of the skin in the abscess, and covered it around, it is necessary that you fill it with old cotton or woolen cloth without moisture, and bind until the third day; then unbind, and cure with ointment until it heals.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille .i. drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.  Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if bleeding occurs during your work, bring cold water and apply it, along with a wet cloth, and place it on the wound repeatedly. If the bleeding persists, provide treatment and care, and use the powders I have mentioned in this book, and if it is winter, or the wounds or abscesses are very nervous, you must put hot tents and moistened cloths over them; and if it is summer, and the limbs are fleshy, you must put moistened cloths over them with cold water and oil, or cold water and cold oil, as we have said; and then drain the abscess and the pus and treat it, as necessary, until it is healed.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	This also needs to be known universally in the treatment of abscesses: I have already told you how to proceed before the treatment of abscesses, and here is the chapter.
des soros	on ne devra estre en grant doutance a estre en grant paor de mourir; et se il n'est pas bien curez, li malaides moront.
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances. Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire. Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout .i. estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient. Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc. Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit. Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez. Et se li apostemes tient .i. nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés. Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	1. For small abscesses that come on the head are handled in our practice, similar to grapes or blisters from a linseed; there are also those with moisture like pimples, and some are hard and stone-like at the base without any doubt that the artery does not oppose it. And the operations of the neck should be proven with all instruments called "entromissoire", from which the following form comes, what it contains. For if it contains moisture, it is to be done above the long one. And when the moisture is drained, scrape skin without leaving any remaining hair, for it returns immediately when left; then immerse cotton in Egyptian ointment, if present; if not, in water and oil, and apply the wound, and leave until the next day; those who are delayed by night will heal. And on the second day, repeat the cotton as before, and on the third, until you know it does not stay by night; then cure the wound with ointment as appropriate, until it is healed. And if the abscess contains one hard nut, squeeze it along this form, with long force; throw your nails into it, scrape it from all sides, and apply all your care to draw out the pus or where it lies; and if the artery opposes you, do as I told you before. And do the same for a hard abscess, and treat and heal as I told you.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc. Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut .i. apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere. En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	And the incision on a hard abscess and the one with moisture is lighter because they have little blood. And if any of these abscesses or head has no moisture, and of these I treated an abscess or head of an old woman; I found the abscess as hard as a stone axe, rough and white, could not be broken; and if one had cut it with a knife, it would have made the same wound as a stone. In other abscesses coming on the head, unless those which come on the heads of children and at the roots of the ears, they should be opened always for the best, to let pus out; and they are to be treated as appropriate.
des scrophules	of scrofulas
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre. Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes. Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit. en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les .ij. levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	Sometimes this abscess appears at the neck, under the chin, and in the groin, and sometimes it occurs elsewhere on the body, and they are large and joined together. And each scrofula is located within its own side, as the notch and the abscess of the neck, as we have said; and the appearances of these scrofulas are various. Some contain moisture, and some are malignant and do not want to obey health. Therefore, when you see a good disposition for treatment, and it resembles the color of the body, and is silent from all sides and not irritated at the nerves of the neck or the artery or the duct, and is not inflamed; if necessary, you must cut through the top, and peel off each part, and place the two edges of the knife on the incisions, as we have said in the abscess of the neck; and pull it out slowly, and be sure not to cut the nerve or the vein, and do not use a probe or lancing that might injure the hand, and look not too far ahead, so you do not injure what should not be.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir. Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde. Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	And if you cut the vein or artery and it does not allow closure, put vitriol powder in the wound, or some powders that stop bleeding, and hold the wound closed; and leave it until the abscess is appeased and the wound softened and begins to drain. And when the blood is clotted, return to your work, as you complete it; then observe your indications if there remain small scrofulas at the root of the scrofula, cut them and wash them. If the scrofula has a large vein at its root, do not cut the scrofula at its root, but tie it with a strong double thread and allow it to hang down without harm; then use old cotton dipped in Egyptian ointment and heal the wound.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les .ij. levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule. si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit. Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you have excised the entire scrofula, you must gather the two lips of the wound and stitch them now, as there is no need for superfluity due to the largeness of the scrofula. You must understand how to cover the root of it and draw pus, and then stitch as we have said. Those scrofulas that hold superfluity, pierce where there is a hole; and pierce it as the one mentioned above, depending on it, then introduce tents with ointment and similar things, so that it corrupts what remains from corruption; and when the wound is well cleaned, cure it with ointment enchanter char until it heals.
de squinance	When there is no movement of the afflicted member due to a dislocation or fracture, tie a bandage around it tightly so that it remains motionless and the pain decreases; but if there is swelling, put a warm poultice on it.
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The ancients spoke and wrote about the measurement of the throat; but I have never seen it done in our land, and this is their written word.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en .ij. amandres.	For those who have squinchy throat, the slit in the throat called "epiglote" should be opened; and no help can be given by those, because all veins and the opening of the mouth or throat or two glands are at those who have an abscess hot in the mouth, or in the throat or in the two glands.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the illness is in the channel of the mouth, it is necessary to cover the epiglotte to avoid the danger of strangulation that comes from the constriction.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz .iij. cercles ou .iiij. une petite fendure dou travers, entre les .ij. cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige;	Therefore, when we want to split the epiglotte, it is necessary that we split it under 4 circles or 3 small slits across, between the 2 circles or by the amount of the split at the tip, not in the cartilage.
et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	And when the neck is tender at the incision of the epiglottis where there is no flesh, and the vessels are long from it.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit;	And if the master is afraid, then it is necessary that you extend the skin of the throat to its entire length, then cut open the neck until you reach the trachea; and squeeze out the vessels of blood, if you see anything, and then sew up the opening, as we have said.
et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix;	And it is demonstrated by the incision of the trachea that a bone has broken through the place which is broken, and by the lack of voice.
et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	And leave the wound open for a while.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the hour has passed where there is doubt of strangulation, bring the two lips of the wound together gently, and press it all around the cartilage; then administer medications that produce heat, until it heals.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Al-Zahrawi says that it should not be done until the throat is completely stopped up, and the patient has been judged dead, and the soul has departed.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort;	Then tie the epiglottis because the patient cannot breathe, and they breathe through the wound, and thus it is guarded from death.
et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en .iij. jors ou en .iiij.	And for this reason, the ancients commanded to leave the wound open until the malignancy of the disease has passed, and it has passed in 3 days or 4.
Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee;	And then they commanded to stitch up the wound and heal, until it was healed.
et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	And I will tell you what I saw.
Je vis que une damoisele prist .i. coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon;	I saw that a maiden took one knife and stuck it in her throat, cutting part of the windpipe;
et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	And I was called to cure him, and I found him as dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I found the wound and saw the blood flowing from it, and I knew that it had not opened nor conducted anything except the throat, and the veins were flowing through the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee;	I quickly closed the wound and healed it until it was healed;
et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition;	And it did not happen to the lady except that her voice became red [swollen or hoarse], and afterwards she returned to her condition.
por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	Therefore I say that in the case of the epiglottis, have no fear.
de la grosse gorge	of the thick throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes;	This abscess is called "gullet hernia," and is a large one with a yellow color, and is much in women.
et est selonc .ij. manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	And it is according to two ways: natural and accidental; where the natural has no artifice.
Et li accidens est selonc .ij. manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere;	The accident is according to two ways, one of which resembles fatness and the other resembles an abscess that comes from us through arteries;
et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire:	and it should have fear, and no force should be done except in that which is small, and the proof and search should be made in every intrusion:
se tu le trueves ausi com .i. nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point;	If you find it as hard as a knuckle, and it cannot move in any direction, strike it as one strikes the nose, and pull it entirely off if there is anything attached to it.
et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And bind it well, and heal it as necessary, until it heals perfectly.
des nous	of the nose
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances;	Many ways of ours are, which I will say all their similarities;
et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	and it is necessary that I say the entire difference that exists between a dislocation and a fracture.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	I say that dislocation is heat and fever lasting until the swelling has passed, and then the pain subsides; afterwards, the fever and the heat subside.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient .i. syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros;	With a fracture there is no heat or fever or pain, and it contains one swelling, which is its own sack and is the same as the body's color, and begins like a blister, and becomes large;
et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	And they are of two types, either fatty or moist, and many-colored as I said in the classification.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	When you come to treat the newt, it is necessary that you examine and test first all the instrument called "entromissoire," according to its form or the chapter that follows.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme;	The method of the inquiry of the abscesses for us is that you take or more moist place than you find within the abscess and turn your fingers little by little, until you feel that the instrument has pierced the core, then according to the size of the abscess;
puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	Then straighten the joint (or dislocation), and take care not to let it jump out again.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes;	If the moisture turns black (or is infected), as I have said for other abscesses;
et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout;	And if after straightening the joint (or dislocation) there is still moisture, know that it is fatty; then make a cross-shaped incision over it and take hold of the edges with the pincers and carefully remove the skin from both sides, and pull out the garment or cloth that covers it so you can remove it cleanly with the thread.
et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	And if you cannot draw it out whole, then draw it out in pieces so that nothing remains.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois;	If there is anything remaining, it comes back to us many times;
et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez;	If a small amount remains and does not trouble you, apply some corrosive powders to the wound, hold the wound closed, place soothing hot things on it, and treat it with other remedies until it is healed.
et se li nous est grans, si cout les .ij. levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	And if the wound is large, make two lips of it, and treat the one that bleeds.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	And if the wound swells against you or another thing happens and you are forced to use vitriol powder, leave it for two or three days until the wound heals over, allowing the boil to drain; then cover what remains of the wound with oil.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de .iij. manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a .iij. quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et .i. qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de .iij. manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule;	Here are the forms of the instruments for opening, and they come in four types: large, medium, and small; and there are four squares called "albaret", and one that is called "breb", and there are three types for encircling abscesses with fistulas.
et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule;	And are also like the needles with which they sew witches, and are made of silver, or iron, or citron rind, and yellow ones are worth more, and those blackened are more experienced for surrounding the swellings of a fistula;
et sont de .iij. manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	And are of three kinds: large, medium, and small, according to the size of the wounds.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont .ij. corbeures de .iij. manieres ausi;	The shapes of the wounds are much alike, as you can see here: large, medium, and small; and some wounds have two swellings of four kinds;
et si a oncines qui ont .iij. corbeures, et sont ausi de .iij. manieres; et si a oncines qui ont .ij. corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de .iij. manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	And if one has hunchbacks who have three bends and are of four types; and if one has hunchbacks who have two bends, or humpbacks of a single bend and they are also of four types; all of these are necessary in their place.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf;	The tips of these [humpbacks] are sharp, and there is no need to cut them from any other side except where the vein or nerve is not to be severed.
et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes;	And these incisions [made for treating an abscess] are tied up with lacerations so that the patient does not tear them open during the treatment of abscesses.
et sont de .iij. manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois;	And there are three types: large, small, and medium, as you see;
et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus;	And it should not be used except in charnu (charred) flesh, such as legs, arms, breasts, and similar areas.
et aucune fois fait on .i. autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	And sometimes another small instrument similar to fistula scissors is made in this shape, to drain blood; \[...\]
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	And set it [the dislocated joint] in its place that heals with the covering of veins, and the arteries, and sometimes it returns according to this great form:
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme;	Sometimes the breasts of some men swell when they begin to decay, so much that they resemble a woman's breasts;
et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne b. jusques a .g.:	and remain ugly and swollen, and whoever wishes to cure them, must do so according to this form of the following line b.j. to .g.:
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee;	then scrape the fat off, apply medicine soothing to the wound, then gather the two lips of the wound together for suturing, and heal it until it is healed.
et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en .ij. costelz desus, par .ij. semblans fendures;	And if the breast sinks downwards and is flattened due to its large size, as it often happens with women, then make two cuts on top of it, through two similar openings.
de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.;	so that one is held to the other at the end of each one, so that the larger line contains the smaller one according to this shape, from this line b to the line g;
puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les .ij. levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then peel off the skin between the two lips, remove the fat, and introduce the aforementioned suturing and powders, as well as whatever is necessary for the cure, until it heals.
et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif;	And if the patient is not healthy or the incision is not completely made because the patient does not want to rest, or due to the flow of blood, then you must fill the wound with cotton soaked in corrosive ointment.
et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	And leave it until it digests the remaining flesh and fat, then heal it when it is drained.
des apostemes des asselles	abscesses of the buttocks
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	These abscesses that come under the buttocks are handled as cases of hard scrofula with ribs (or sides), and if they contain moisture within them.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Therefore, those containing moisture should be cut along this shape from line b to line g:
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the entire cavity in the abscess is emptied, use old cotton to fill the wound, and leave it until the next day, then remove all the cotton, and heal with ointment as necessary until it heals.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the abscess resembles scrofula, perform it as we have said in cutting out scrofulas, and if the wound becomes a cavity, apply caution as we have said before.
de la routure de l’artere	Of the rupture of the artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme;	When the artery is torn and the skin is sealed over it, there are often abscesses, and the same happens with an open vein and abscess;
et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont;	and if one knows this about it [the artery], then the abscesses will be long-lasting;
et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens .i. estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans;	And when you feel it with your hands, if it feels dislocated; and if it is due to the vein, it should be reasonably displaced in appearance;
et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	It is foolish to cover this abscess, especially when it is under the bones and near angles or neck and in many other places, and it is very large.
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc;	Therefore, the iron cure must be avoided, and so should it be for those with head problems, and in those swollen with an artery, they must be punctured through the skin lengthwise;
puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte;	then cut open the wound along one edge, and carefully separate the artery from the membranes, until it is exposed.
puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en .ij. leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des .ij. arteres qui sont en temples;	Then insert an awl under it and make it pierce through to the other side, and hold the artery with a double thread for two inches, as I have shown you in the extraction of the two arteries that are in the temples.
puis point le leu qui est entre les .ij. liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme;	Then insert a probe between the two ligaments until it reaches the abscess and separate the abscess.
puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient;	Then apply the cure that soaks a beech-wood bowl until the ligament is swollen.
puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then treat him with salve until he is healed.
et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir,	and if the abscess is large, you must apply the salve to the entire skin surrounding it.
puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait .i. fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit;	then insert the needle underneath the skin you are holding with your hand, and make it pierce through, and have one doubled thread ready so that you can pull it from the other side.
puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de .ij. pars as .ij. chiés dou fil;	then tie the abscess, as I told you, or sew it with one of the two halves of the thread between the two shoulders.
et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout .i. fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en .iiij. leus;	And if you doubt that the thread has passed through, press another needle underneath the abscess at the incision of the first needle, and hold the threads in four inches;
puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez;	then press the abscess so that the excess comes out, then cut off the pus and leave what is tied;
puis met sus .i. drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	then put on a damp cloth soaked in wine and oil, then treat it with liniments and poultices until it heals.
des apostemes des ners	From the abscesses of the limbs
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	As abscesses come in arteries and veins, they come in nerves when injured, or from too much work, and similar things.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est .i. grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor;	This often happens in the shoulders and knees and in all limbs with joints, which is severe abscesses, and its color resembles the body's color, and it occurs in multiple forms of pain.
et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur;	And when it is pressed firmly, the patient feels pain, but it is not throughout the body, but under the skin.
et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer: par aventure i vanroit contraction;	And it should be immobilized from all sides, neither going forward nor backward, neither above nor below, and one who is in the joints should not be covered by iron: perhaps it would cause contraction.
et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	And if it is on the head or forehead, flatten the skin with a spatula.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine;	If the abscesses are small, hold them with forceps and strike at its root.
et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is large, suspend it on a hook, peel it off, then drill and stitch the wound closed, and let it heal until it heals.
des grosses boces pendans	Large boils hanging
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros; et en i a de petis et de mout grans;	Sometimes it happens in bellies and nowhere else, and it is a disease called "fungus" because of its resemblance to mushrooms, and it has subtle roots and large heads; there are some small ones and very large ones.
et je vis .i. home qui en avoit .ij. ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	And I saw one man who had two bellies that were more like mushrooms than anything else, and there was no difference between them, they were white, and had a thin root, and were split open, and moisture flowed out of them continually.
Je les copai et trovai en l’un .xviij. onces pesant, et en l’autre .vj. З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine;	I found and weighed eighteen ounces in one, and five pounds in the other. The incisions show that if you look at the patient, they are moist, and the color of the artery is pale and moist with a subtle root;
si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu. Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer;	if the wound is deep and wide, and in your presence the fire cautery is needed. For there are often excessive bleeding during slicing, and if it overwhelms you, hasten to use the cautery;
et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent .i. fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse .ij. jors;	and if you see the patient trembling and afraid of the incision with iron, take a good-made thread, tie it around the artery as we have said, and leave it for two days;
et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail; et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet,	and then hold it (the affected part), and do not stop applying pressure on the bandage until it feels the pain, and the joint starts to work; and if the roots are large, then be careful when pushing at the same time due to the abdomen, but you can easily push half of it.
puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne; puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	Then cauterize so that it does not return; then treat the wound, and ensure that you do not press on the tumor which is of a dark color and poor sensation and liquid discharge.
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	For it is an abscess hardened, and I will come to the treatment of this scrofula later.
quant li boude ist fuer	When the thigh (or leg) is injured
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit;	If the wound or cut on the thigh (or leg) is caused by cautery of an injury or incision, and it is above the belly and in some of the thighs, as happens in other routes, or from blood that cuts from veins or arteries according to what is beforehand, or from windiness;
et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	If it is by the route of cautery and by the exit from the bowel, then the appearance of the abscess is similar to the color of the body, and it is a light thing without pain, and open with various issues.
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	And if it is due to the bursting of an intestine, then it is more diverse. When pressure is applied to it with the hands and it collapses, then returns, and in some cases if it is sutured, and greatly swells at the entrance of the wound, and due to heavy work.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie; et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit;	And if it is due to moisture, it is an easy matter, and it opens easily when you press it with your hand, do not force it; and if it is blood, it opens with these signs: the abscesses are large and hard, and are pierced according to a certain amount.
et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	If it is due to windiness, it is suitable for touching. The signs to look for are whether the appearance is due to blood from an artery or vein, or windiness.
Si covient que tu laisses la cure. Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	It is necessary that you allow the healing to take place. For there is doubt and fear, as I told you in the chapter on abscesses, regarding the artery and the vein.
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude;	And if the appearance is due to the intestine or the abscess, you should command the patient to strain his anus, and stretch it out straight, then apply heat all around the abscess;
puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains,	then you command him to lie quietly between your hands,
puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile,	Then go around the joint that you have signed with all the splint.
puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine;	Then spread half of the abscess on top to the entire great spoon.
puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz;	Then bind it with a strong thread or a strong silk cord tightly and let the patient hold it closed.
puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine;	Then open half of the abscess spread over the cord, and push your index finger inside and search for the intestine.
se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre;	If you find it tied up with a cord, untie it, and push the intestines out of the abdomen through the incision.
et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit;	And if you find the bowel, take hold of it at its thickest part, and squeeze out the excess.
et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren .ij. aguilles, et i boute .ij. fors filz, et boute les .ij. aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier;	And if the artery or vein becomes contracted, go around it, then return to your work and take two needles, and insert two fine threads, and insert the needles around what you have made in a cross shape that you make perforated.
puis estrain l’aposteme en .iiij. leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi;	Then press the abscess four fingers above the needles, and if you see, remove the needles, and leave it for as long as possible, and let the dead flesh rot away by itself.
ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit;	or you strike when it is softened and breaks, then you treat what is necessary, and cover the wound as we have said.
et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	draw out the blood or moisture that you find, then treat the wound of what is necessary, and bind it up.
dou chancre	the boil
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	We have said in the division the likeness of scab, and how to treat it with medicines, and how to avoid iron cure; and we say that the scab originates in marriage, and great caution should be taken in its treatment, and the ancients said that when scabs are in a place where it can be shaved like a scab that is on the mamelas, and in the thigh, and in similar places, and it should all be removed when it is at the beginning; and when it is large and old, it is not good to approach it, for I never knew anyone to heal it; no one ever healed it before me.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire; puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide .i. boin leu por faire l’ovraige; puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier; et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the work, when it is in a place where it can be removed as we have said, is that you purge the patient once with black bile; then make him purge if he has evident repletion, then shave the patient.i. one good piece of skin to do the work; then shave the scab or abscess, and the hair of all parts, and the bone of all parts leaving nothing remaining; and let the blood flow freely, and press well the place with your hand or any thing, and if the discharge of blood makes you opposite to the incision of the artery or vein, cauterize it until the wound is stopped from bleeding; then cure it with other means until it is healed.
de ydropisie	dropsy (medical condition)
