Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer: si est eclites soulement; et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces .ij. semblances: c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose; donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses; si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance; et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer:	We have said in the division that the similarities of edema are like idropisie; and in what manner the assembly of water is made, and the signs of each likeness, and the cure which is done with medicines, and that which is cured by iron: it is only eclites exposed; and no iron should be used in these two likenesses: namely tympanites and yposarche, for it is a deadly thing; therefore when you treat this likeness of edema called "eclites" with medicines, and the cure does not improve, look to see if the patient is weak or has other disease besides edema, such as an inflamed abdomen and similar things; do not use iron, for there is doubt; and if you see the patient of strong virtue, and he has no other disease except edema alone, and he is neither too young nor too old, then you should work in this way:
lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme: Et soit trenchans de .ij. pars. a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier;	Place the patient right on your lap, and the assistant presses the abdomen from below to bring the water to the lowest part of the bladder, then take the pointed spatula as shown in this form: And it should be sharp at two ends. But it should not be so deep that it reaches the intestine when inserted, and it should not pierce or bruise it:
puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines: si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude .iij. dois droit desoz sus lou poignil; et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude .iij. dois; et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu;	then look to see if the edema is attached towards the intestines: if it is, you must make an incision below the bladder two fingers' breadth straight across from the handle; and if the edema is due to liver disease, the incision should be on the left side of the bladder two fingers; and if it is due to a blockage, it should be on the right, and the patient should not lie over the incision so that the superfluidities do not run to that weak place.
puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor; puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme: Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz .i. petit pertus; et ou costeit d’une part, .iij. pertus; et .ij. d’autre part, et .i. d’autre; et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	Then pierce the entire skin with the instrument, and push it, and place your hand all over the spatula between the skin and the gristle as much as the size of a nail or in which it fits; then pierce the gristle until the spatula comes to the joint which is the joint of the thumb, then pull it out, and put this instrument here that you see: It resembles a thin silver chain, and is made of bronze or light iron, and has a small hole on one side. On three sides, there are four holes; on two sides, two; and on one side, one; and the head is shaped like a feather, and this is the shape of the incision that scribes carve a feather:
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument; vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort;	At the top (of the thumb), there is the nerve. So when the instrument comes to the joint, then you hold it up now on the instrument; then empty either half or a third part of it, because if you see more than necessary in that hour, by chance the patient might die from resolution of their spirit due to the weapon, or they fall down unconscious, or approach death.
mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz; puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere; puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit;	but empty according to its strength and according to the patient's condition and pulse; then pull the instrument and hold the joint, and it is now held for the cautery that stops the holes on the gristle, of which I have spoken earlier. You pierce in this manner; then you use the instrument again the next day if you see the patient suffering from it, and draw out a small amount of the joint liquid:
fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue. Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre; et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	Do this every day and avoid overeating until it recovers but has a little water. And if you doubt the patient, and leave much water, cure it with burial or hot sand, and by sweating or bathing and in the sun, and anoint it with wine; and cure it with drying medicines until it is healthy, and cauterize the stomach, liver, and spleen after the extraction of water, as I said before.
de l’estopement de la verge	Stopping the penis
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu. Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout .i. spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme: puis met ou pertus .i. clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi .iij. jors ou iiij. et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet; et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	There are never born children who do not have foreskin on their penis, or the foreskin is small, or it is not in its place. If this happens immediately, puncture a very thin spatula according to this form: then put a thin piece of cloth under the foreskin and hold it in place for 2 to 4 days until the child wants to urinate, at which point the cloth should be removed, and urination allowed; and by chance, it is not necessary to do so because the urine that comes out does not close the opening.
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera. Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut; et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	If the bladder of one who has a small stone is treated with a plug of lead as previously mentioned, it will expand. Those who do not have a stone in its place are weakened, because no one is born who has the stone at the head of the penis; therefore, they cannot urinate before lifting their penis up; and they cannot enjoy sex because the matter cannot reach the marris (the opening of the urethra), and it is a harmful disease.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient; et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	The manner of work is that the patient lies on his back, with the head of the penis and the buttocks positioned as the end of a feather, so that the stone can fall into the bladder where it should be; and beware of bleeding that often occurs, and if it happens, stop the bleeding from the wound and cure the wound until it is healed.
des pustules de la verge	boils on the penis
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide; et en i a malignes et non malignes; si covient que tu les preignes a .i. oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien; puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	"Many times this albathe appears in the penis, and it is an ugly appearance of the flesh; among them are malignant and non-malignant. You must take them one by one with a .i. oncine subtil (probably referring to tweezers), and crush and clean them all. Then put cotton soaked in Egyptian ointment on it, and treat it with diafinicon ointment until it heals."
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere. Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier; et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer. Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion; si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	"If the albathe is malignant, of a putrid color and spreading, it requires cauterization. After you crush it, if the albathe is within the penis and has both internal and external parts, first remove the albathe that is inside. Once removed, treat the outside. Because when treating them together, there is no assurance that the parts of the penis will not be pierced, causing blackness and corruption in its length and breadth; it is necessary to remove all that is black and corrupted. Then lie it on a plaster made of honey and flour, which is made from the peel of pomegranate rind and other substances, then treat it with other medicines until it heals."
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme: Li cauteres si aide as .ij. dispositions ensamble: c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption; et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi; et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a .i. estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars;	"If there is bleeding, apply the lunar cauterization as follows: The cautery should be in two forms together: for bleeding and corruption. If the parts of the penis are corrupted and retreat, it is necessary that you lead or make a canal from the penis and make the patient urinate. When the hairs reach the head of the penis (which happens to those who have not been circumcised), or it happens due to an injury or abscess, then you must shave it with one instrument having teeth, until the ligaments are released, and free the parts of the penis from all sides;
et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a .i. spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil; puis dessevre belement entre .ij., et i met .i. subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	And if it is a difficult matter to discuss this, you should make an incision with a lancet about one span from the tip of the vein and skin; then press carefully between two fingers, and put a thin linen cloth soaked in cold water on it immediately, so that it does not swell up again.
de la circoncision	of circumcision
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	Circumcision is not the same as other wounds; however, when we perform this work of our own free will and specifically for infants, it is necessary that we make the best and most straightforward work to save them.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say that the ancients did not speak of the circumcision of their children, for they did not practice it in their law, and we have only what we have acquired by experience.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor .i. dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule; si fuioit li keurs car il i a .ij. toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	I wanted the largest part of masters and surgeons who performed circumcision around one day, and with forces, and in all cases, a newborn; however, the foreskin was too thick, and perhaps it healed over the top and delayed healing below.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre; et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	If it is covered again, the pain is doubled, and at the healing of the member's tip, it is not assured; and in the trimming of the nail, perhaps the iron slips, ruins the work, and many times it heals so that there is no need for trimming, and I have seen this.
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	Of the amputation that is made to all the limb of thread I found the goodness of the experiment, for the forces cut equally well above as below.
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en .i. tout soul tens; mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir; et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues;	For when you press your hand, it cuts equally all the time; but that the thread be well stretched around the skin; and in the first work, it is that you make the child think, if he understands, that you do not tie the thread around him except for attaching it to the rod only, and then let him play in all the ways that you can.
puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens; puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens; puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz .i. poc a .i. autre liien; et la tien as .ij. dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les .ij. liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge;	Then place him straight between your hands and position the forces between your hands or under your feet so that the infant does not see them, nor any of the tools; then press your hand against the rod and blow or cough, and pull it up until the joints of the rod are in; then clean it well of the filth that has accumulated there, then tie the wound signet with a double thread, then tie a thread under one piece to another thread; and hold it at the second knot to the thumb and index finger, and cut between the two threads, then remove the core quickly and pull the head of the rod.
puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres; et met poudre sus et sus la poudre .i. drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then let the blood coagulate drop by drop, for it is clotted; and sprinkle powder on top and over the powder put a cloth dampened with a mixture of cooked egg white tempered with rose water, mixed with fresh rose oil; leave it on until the next day, and treat it with another remedy until it heals.
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste: li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	The form of the strength for healing is as follows: the two cheeks should be tender and thin, and the cheeks should be equal in size to a hand.
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision; donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme; et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	The error in healing is when the intestines are cut during incision; therefore, it must be extended to the fingernail, so that the wound is made deeper; and it should be cut evenly, and if you cannot hold it with your fingernail, use pliers, and then cut it.
Et s’il trespassent .iij. jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement; si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	And if they pass more than three days, and that which is below the vein becomes swollen, leave it until the abscess subsides, and gently lance it; cut if you can move it, but avoid the part of the vein; this will not harm it.
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point; cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then heal the limb with things under swollen wounds using the powders that we have said or mentioned treating, and if you cut too deeply it will go up, but do not worry; heal it as we have said until it is healed.
dou retenement de l’urine	retention of urine
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division;	The retention of urine is due to a stone, or congealed blood, or a swelling, or frozen water, or similar things, as we have said in the division.
et se li urine n’est desliie, et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz; et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet; et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e;	and if the urine is not released, and you see that it is retained by a stone in the bladder or urethra, then you must make the patient lean on his knees; put the feet on the back, extend the abdomen from above the lower back, and hold the patient as firmly as possible; and then apply pressure to the bladder area above the stone to expel it.
et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme: et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil; et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	and if it does not come out as we have said, and the patient feels great pain, then you should administer extraction with all the equipment called "syringe", whose form is: it should be made of thin, light silver tube, like a bird's quill; and the cavity should be one and a half palm lengths, and thin at the tip.
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren .i. fil double, et lie au chief .i. poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue; et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus .i. siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede;	And the method for the discharge of urine is that you take one double thread, tie one end to the head with a piece of linen or cotton, and push the head through the syringe with the thread inside; and fill the excess of the linen up to the head of the syringe, then oil or butter the syringe and put egg white on the bladder and penis moistened with oil and olive oil and cold water; and make the patient sit on one seat, and rub the bladder and penis with oiled and olive oil and cold water.
puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude; puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors; puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine;	Then gently insert the syringe into the penis until it reaches the root of the penis, then double the penis over towards the scrotum; then push the syringe forward up to the bladder, and make the patient feel as if he is urinating until he fills the empty thing, and this is not done according to this order unless because the guide through which it goes is twisted; then the thread is tied to all the linen piece by piece, and the urine follows the linen, then remove the linen, and correct the urine.
et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	And the doctor should repeat the syringe process until the bladder is empty and the patients are relieved.
des maladies de la vessie	Diseases of the bladder
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When scorchings or blood comes into the bladder, or pus is collected there and you see it distill liquids and medicines, use all the instrument called "clepsydre" and this is its form:
Elle est close, et si a .iij. pertus: .ij. d’une part, et .i. d’autre, si com tu vois; et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est;	It is closed with three openings: two on one side and one on the other, as you see; and the upper part should be shaped so that the medicine can flow freely from the opening, stopping the water if possible, and adding more when needed;
et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens; si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens; si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira;	And when you see that your medicines are thrown into the bladder, put the head of the cucurbit in the moisture, and draw out slowly what is inside; if you draw out the moisture from the cucurbit, then push the drawing forcefully in again; the moisture will enter the cucurbit and will come to the bladder immediately, so that the patient will feel it.
et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie: si est ci:	This is the form of a subtle enema, which is used to cleanse the bladder. Here it is:
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut; et desoz a .i. sein ou li liiens chiet; puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les .ij. seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe .i. poc celle moistor sus le feu; puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie;	And it is made of silver or lead and has the head raised above one hand or a loop; under this a linen cloth is placed; then take a sheep bladder and put in the moisture that you intend to use for cleansing the bladder. Then tie the moistened bladder between two hands with a strong double thread, and heat one end of the bladder on fire. Then insert the head of the enema into the penis, then hold your hand above the bladder so that all the moisture goes towards the bladder until the patient feels the moisture has reached the bladder.
et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai .i. cercle, et le perce rondement entor; puis boute .i. fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble .i. dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument; et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	And if you do not have the bladder, take a piece of parchment, and make one circle, and pierce it roundly around; then insert a strong thread into these holes, then assemble the circle like one does a syringe, and put inside it oil, moisture, and water, and tie it in the instrument; do as you have done with the bladder, press it with your hand until the moisture reaches the bladder.
de la piere	From the stone
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	We have said in the division the ways of stone, and extraction with medicines; and I have said the difference between the stone implanted in the rain, and all the signs, and in what stone one must work in size; and in the bladder, and in the penis; and I will tell you openly and briefly.
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont .iiij. ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	I say that the stone in the bladder often occurs more frequently in children, and this is a sign that the water jump from the bladder resembling water in its subtlety; it opens a passageway, increases the pain of the patient greatly, pierces it many times, and then binds it; and much of these jumps cause foundation; and the healing of children is light until they reach the age of 4, but it is very difficult in the elderly, and it is at the middle age for those who are between youth and old age; and the cure is easier for those who have large stones, than for those who have small ones.
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines. Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	And when we come to the treatment, it is first necessary to purify the patient with an enema, to draw out all the filth that is in the intestines. For it often blocks the search for the stone.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut; puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval; puis la quier et la touche ded ens;	Then take the patient by the feet, bend and move them downwards, so that the stone descends to the bottom of the bladder, and sinks upwards sometimes with the help of gravity; then make him sit between your prepared hands, and his hands should be below his hips, so that the bladder is completely inclined downwards; then search for it and touch it with your hand.
se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere. Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis; et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie; puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	If you feel the stone in the body, hurry up to cut it above the stone. And if it does not fall down by itself, moisten your left index finger, if the patient is weak or old, or use oil, if the patient is a young man; and push it into its foundation, search for the stone, when you feel it with your finger, push it to the neck of the bladder; then press on your finger, and push it out where you see fit to cut.
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille; puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	Instruct the servant to press the bladder with his hand, and command him to extend his right hand upwards, and with his left hand remove the skin that is below the testicles in the part where the cutting is done; then push the spatula covering it, as it is its shape:
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre; et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans;	And make an incision between the scrotum and the foundation, not on the midline but along the left side of the scrotum; and let it be straight above the stone, and your fingers should be at its base or foundation, and let the cut be wide externally and narrow internally according to the size of the stone, not too large:
par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail; et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges: si est griés a issir; et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	By chance, if the foundation presses it must jump without effort; and know that there is a stone or an angle, edge: it is curved to come out; and if it is soft like a plum and round, whose opening is easy.
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant; et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe; ou tu boute desoz li .i. estrument subtil corbé au chief; et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge .i. poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole;	Then make the cut larger if it has angles and margins; and if it does not jump, then you must strain upward with pliers that are like a limer at the head to force the stone to stay in place; or you can push an instrument subtle and curved at the head beneath it. And if you cannot maneuver it so, widen .1 inch with a chisel, and if it is not cut, strain it with vitriol.
et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors. Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie. Car .ij. choses avienent au malaide: ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder; mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces;	And if there are more than one stone, then push the largest one at the bladder neck first, then hit it, then pull it, and the smaller ones after if there are more. And if it is very large, it must be, and make a larger wound. For two things happen to the patient: either he dies, or urine comes immediately through where the joints cannot be sealed; but nonetheless, try to extract, or break apart with pliers, as much as you can pull it in pieces.
et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus .i. drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut; puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	And when you have completed your work, smear the wound with incense and aloe and dragon's blood, hold it closed, and place a damp linen cloth in oil and wine on it, or in olive oil and rose water and cold water, to cool the abscess; then raise the patient's head on his neck, and do not remove the bandage until the third day.
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When you remove it (the dressing), wash the wound well with oil and water, then apply a healing ointment of diaphinicon and basilicon until it heals.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine: boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit;	If an abscess or erosion comes in the wound and congelation of blood forms in the bladder and urine is retained in this manner: without delay put your finger in the wound, and draw out the blood, for if it remains, the bladder will corrode and perforate.
puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez; et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les .ij. cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	Then clean the wound of pus and of any dirt and linen, and assist in every possible way that you can while it heals; and it is necessary that you bind the thighs together for her, and apply the medicine on the wound.
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir; si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure. Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	And if the stone is small and it is led by the rod and driven in, and urine cannot pass; heal it as I tell you now, cut it many times, or excuse yourself from the cutting by this cure. I have already proved it thus.
Pren .i. foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a .iij. angles fichiees en .i. tison:	Take one iron fork of this form and sharpened at four angles with one tine:
puis pren .i. fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie; puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere; et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part; si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge. Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides;	Then take a thread and tie it around the shaft of the stone, so that it cannot come back into the bladder; then gently push the awl into the shaft, until it reaches the stone; and turn the awl slowly towards your hand in the stone bit by bit, until you can pierce the stone from the other side; if urine comes soon, press your hand on that which remains inside the shaft of the stone within the bladder. If it is soon broken, it will jump out with the urine, and the patient will be healed.
et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie .i. fil desoz la piere et .i. autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les .ij. liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if you cannot do this for any reason that prevents it, tie a thread around the stone and another one above, then push the shaft towards the stone between the two threads, pull it out, untie the thread, and clean up the congealed blood in the wound; and treat it until it is healed.
de la piere des femmes	of the stone from women
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por .iij. choses: l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	It often happens that a stone is embedded in women, and if it ever occurs, it is a serious matter, and it is forbidden for four reasons: one is that perhaps the woman is a virgin; and the second is because it cannot be found a woman who knows well how to uncover herself, especially when she is chaste.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains; et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a.	The third reason is that perhaps it cannot be found a woman skilled in this art of hands; and the fourth reason is that the stone in the woman's body is deeper than the stone in a man's, therefore it requires a more profound incision, and great fear arises from this.
Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier .i. caste mire subtil; et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere;	And if you must proceed with this, then you should take a skilled midwife, and if one cannot be found easily, do not hesitate to use a chaste and subtle maiden; and present a wise woman of life of women, or a woman who knows a part of the art, and command her to perform what you command regarding the incision of the stone.
et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge: adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere; et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	And pay close attention to whether the woman is a virgin; then you must insert your finger or foundation and search for the stone; and if you find it, you should press it beneath your finger, and advise her to bear down with her hand on the bladder formed.
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse; puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie; et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite;	If you find it, you should make her push it little by little from the bladder entrance to beneath, until it reaches the root of the thigh; then strike upon the stone at the root of the thigh against the mons pubis, where it is moved, and feel the stone in that place; do not move your finger above or below the stone, and cut it with a small cut.
puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont: c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains. si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	Then push the right hand into the thigh, if you feel the stone, open the wound so that the stone can come out, and know that there are many types of stones: small or large, smooth or rough, long or round, and those with grooves. Know their appearances to recognize them.
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre;	And if the bone protrudes, set vitriol in powder on it and hold for an hour until the bone is cauterized; then return to your work, until the stone is fully expelled, and have instruments as I told you for the extraction of the stone for men to assist you in your work.
et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide; puis cure la plaie.	If the bone protrudes, and it is an artery that has been cut, put powder on the wound and bind with strips and bandages, do not resume work, leave the stone and do not draw it out for fear of killing the patient; then care for the wound.
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	And when the heat of the blood is appeased and the wound heals over, then return to your work until the stone is expelled.
de hernie carnouse	of a flesh hernia

de hernie carnouse	Of a fleshy hernia
En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	In this remedy I have never seen anyone dare to cure by iron.
Et li ancien dirent qu’ele est faite si com li ramice qui est ensamble la vis, en teil maniere que tu lie les vasselz, aprés la taille sus ous legierement au desoz;	And the ancients say that it is made like a remedy that consists of vinegar, in such a manner that you bind the vessels, after cutting them lightly below;
puis cope em mi, et cure l’aposteme de ceu qui oevre, tant que li vasselz chient; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then put it in the middle and heal the abscess of those who are affected by it, until the vessels bleed; and heal it as we have said before, until it is healed.
Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus; et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres;	At times rot comes in the groin, as we have said, and opens the joints; and no internal organs are sent to the anus, and if any are, it is little, and repair them every hour;
et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent;	Moreover, if it remains too long in this place, the wound or syphac grows, as long as internal organs are expelled.
et ceu avient par l’estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert;	This happens due to the spreading of syphilis which is in the groin, as we have said, because it spreads, then the joints are softened and opened.
et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit; et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere:	And if the treatment is by cautery, as previously stated; sometimes it is cured by iron in this manner:
et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de .iij. dois;	The patient lies supine on his back between your hands, then strike the swollen place along the length according to the size of three fingers;
et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que l’ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac;	Then extract the pus that is underneath the skin, then take the iron and place it on the visible part of the abscess;
et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les .ij. leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre;	And press at the lower part of the abdomen, then count the two levels appearing near the navel, and count both;
puis estrai le chief dou rait, et ne coper point dou syfac ne n’estendre l’uef n’autre chose, si com je t’ai fait savoir en la cure de la ramice des intestines;	then extract the navel, and do not cover or extend the siphon or any other thing, as I have told you in the treatment of the ramie of the intestines;
puis le cure par la cure des plaies. Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	then treat it with the treatment for wounds. And when you cover the threads, if the wound heals and the wound is healed;
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	The siphon is constricted, and has no appearance in the wound, and the cauteries are made in this place, and closer to salvation.
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	of the softening of the skin on the buttocks
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir; et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil; puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a .iij. costures ou .iiij. fermement; puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	Many times the skin of the buttocks becomes soft in some men, because the charms within are softened and there is a visible liquid; and it is necessary when one sees it to cure, that you make the patient lie on his back, and strike the softened skin on the natural skin; then bring together the two lips to a stitch, and if you see, sew first the superfluous skin softened to 3 or 4 firm stitches; then strike between the stitches, and the wound as with other wounds, until it is healed, and let the thread seep through.
dou chastrement	The punishment for a crime in this time period was severe and often involved physical pain or torture. In the case of a serious offense, a person might be subjected to various methods of corporal punishment such as flogging, branding, mutilation, or even execution by burning at the stake. Here is the first sentence to translate:
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; et n’est necessaires fuer que por .ij. manieres: dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes. Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc .ij. manieres: ou par atraction, ou par fendure.  En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant; puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.  Du chastrement de taille: covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a .i. cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez; et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz; et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure; puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	1. Know that castrations are mentioned in our law, and I would rather not speak of them in this book; and it is necessary only for two reasons: the first is that a person should respond when asked about castration and its cure; and the second, because we often need castration of certain animals to help us, such as goats, sheep, pigs, and other animals. I say therefore that castrations are done in two ways: either by attraction or by cutting. In the one that we do by attraction, we make the animal sit on hot water until its genitals become soft; then we seize them with our hand, holding them until they are restored and you no longer feel them.
des hermofrodites	Hermaphrodites
Hermofrodie est selonc .ij. manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les .ij. coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.  Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et .ij. coions.  Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies; en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	Hermaphrodites are of two kinds in men: the first kind has both openings as a woman, with hair and sometimes urinates through them. The second kind is in women, who have something above the penis like a spear and two openings. The treatment for men and women is to cut around the genitals, and cure them like other wounds; however, in the second kind of man whose urine leaks through the skin of the genitals, there is no cure.
de la tentigene	The evacuation (of blood) occurs from the incision of the artery, (and) from the abscess, (and) in the treatment of wounds, (and) in the extraction of arrows, (and) in cutting into stones, and similar things; where there is doubt and fear, many die.
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir; et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure. Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee». Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	The tentigene is a wart situated on a natural part, which becomes too ugly to look at; some women have one as large as a hand, and it is a disease. You must dye the superfluous growth of the tentigene with your hand or onions, and strike it lightly; do not go too deep, so that bleeding does not occur, then treat it with another cure until it heals; and at another wart that grows from the mouth of a woman, and applies, and possibly jumps off, and is similar to a cow's udder, and for this reason they called it the "disease of the cow" by the ancients. You must strike it as we have said with the tentigene, and treat it until it heals.
de erratique	In some cases, a patient may develop an unusual growth or lump that appears suddenly, moves around on its own, and is often painful. This condition was known as "erratique" in Old French. It could be caused by internal injuries or diseases and required careful observation and treatment to prevent worsening of the condition.
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile. Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait. S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as .ij. leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi: met tes .ij. dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes; puis estent les .ij. leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens; puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder. Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte. Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope; et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef; puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder; et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec; puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.  Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez. Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	1. The nature of a woman is not discerned or small; it may be inherent or accidental due to illness that comes about; it may be due to adultery, subtle semen from the penis, or thick semen in the vagina, and it occurs either during sexual intercourse, in the thighs, or elsewhere; they should avoid conception, pregnancy, and flowers growing; and the knowledge of this is by looking at the woman's face. If the discharge appears near the hands or the genitals, then place your two index fingers together, and have the woman lie on her back with her legs spread open; then form the semen, when it becomes ripe, cover it with linen and oil-soaked cloth, and have the woman rest daily so that it does not stick. And if the semen is subtle and close to the two leves (testicles), hurry and do as follows: place your two index fingers together, and the woman should be on her back, her legs spread open; then form the semen, when it becomes ripe, cover it with linen and oil-soaked cloth, and have the woman rest daily so that it does not stick. And if the semen is hard and thick, you must cut it with a spatula resembling a mirto leaf. If the discharge is of blood, suspend it on an onion and cut; have medicines to stop bleeding, such as acacia, dragon's blood, incense, mixed with many eggs; then bring a wide cloth bandage, so that the wound does not stick; and in this way let it heal for a long time, and bring a dry linen tent; then cure other ailments until it is healed. And when in marriage there comes discharge of blood, it should be covered as described above, except if it is an inflammation that has been treated with cautery. For the inflammation that has been treated with cautery in the vagina, one should not touch to heal.
des emorroides	Hemorrhoids.
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation. Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer. Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer. Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai .i. emplaustre sus son dos. Et se il estainche, c’est boin. Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.  Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a .i. chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	1. "Emorroydes are openings of veins which without care are usually not noticed, and when emorroidles become old, they swell; and as I have said in the division [of this work], their resemblance and signs, and I will say here those that receive treatment. I say that emorroides and the swelling, when they are fully formed inside the body, cannot be felt by touch, unless cured with iron. Those which are at the mouth of the body can be felt, and these can be treated. Therefore, you should put the woman in a cold house, then stretch the swelling with pliers at its roots, then sprinkle powdered medicines that stop bleeding, such as acacia, dragon's blood, and incense, etc.; then place her feet exposed for an hour, then immerse it in cold water; and if there is any blood flow, make her sit in a decoction of sumac, apple bark, wild madder root, and similar things, and then take barley flour, mix it with honey and oil, and make one poultice to apply on her back. If it bleeds, that's good. If not, make her wear hot water bottles on her back and under the breasts without piercing them; then take linen, wet it in juice of plantain or marshmallow with old wine, and apply hot linen at the site. And when the abscess subsides, treat the site with ointment until it heals; and that which is called 'albathir' is red, and resembles a small rough stone, and it should be covered as I have said for the swelling; and then treat it until it heals."
des apostemes de la marris	openings or abscesses of the anus
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division. Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.  Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus .i. siege, et ait .ij. petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument. Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés .ij. jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.  Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	There are many types of abscess that may occur in the anus, such as canker sores and hot abscesses, herpes, fistulas, hemorrhoids, and other diseases I have mentioned previously. Therefore, I will explain here the treatment for a hot abscess in the anus, which is not one of those that are filled with pus. And if you want to know the procedure for iron-making, check if the abscess is acute at its onset, and full of heat and fever, and turns red when touched. Then do not hurry to puncture it, but let it mature until the pain subsides; then make the patient sit on one seat, or two small seats so that he can lean, support his back with his hands, and spread his legs apart; his knees should be bent and tied firmly with a strong rope; then apply the instrument used to open the anus, as follows: When you bring this instrument, ensure that it does not enter too deeply into the anus, and does not cause pain or bleeding to the patient. If the instrument is larger, cover the depth of the anus with fabric so that the instrument does not hurt; and place the mouthpiece on top, and mark the instrument. And when the abscess opens, and it becomes soft in your hand, cover it with a sponge soaked in rose oil or green dry oil; place the sponge inside the wound towards the depth of the anus, and place fabric over the anus and over the handle clean cloth moistened with vinegar or cooked long-rooted herbs such as aristolochia. After two days, apply ointment to it until it heals; sometimes the anus and the wound are cleaned with water and honey, then vinegar or long-rooted herbs are cooked, and then return to the ointment. And if the wound heals back into the anus, be careful not to burn with iron, but treat it as we have said previously.
de l’enfantement	Of childbirth
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment. Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	It is necessary for the midwife to first recognize the natural figure of childbirth and its signs when she sees the woman in labor and desires to urinate; then hasten the birth of the child; know that this childbirth is according to the natural figure, and it issues from below the head, and the second one comes with it; and when you see these signs, gently press the woman's abdomen so that the child comes quickly; for when it descends onto its head, the second one follows with it, and the husband cleans himself of his waste through good cleansing; and this which comes otherwise does not come naturally. For sometimes it comes on its feet, or the body or the head, or the hands, or on the belly or the backside, and it is turned by chance onto its neck, and in other bad figures; it is necessary for the midwife to be wise and clever in these things, and to beware of error and deception, and I will show you all the figures as to how one should assist.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	If the child comes onto its head naturally, and the woman gives birth with great effort, and the strength of her virtue is weak, make her sit on a saddle, or women hold her; anoint her nature with oil or fenugreek that has been cooked, then the midwife puts the small spatula between her hands in the shape:
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.Et se les .ij. mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus .i. siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	And cut the second bone, and strike its nail so that the moistures which are within come forth; and press the woman's belly until the child descends, and if it does not descend, then you must clisterize the woman with muscillaige of fenugreek with oil of sisament; then make her take and vomit from condysi, and hold her mouth and nose for an hour: thus the child will come forth.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piez	The issue of the child from its feet
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut;	When the child comes out from its feet, you must push it upwards;
et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz;	and then turn it gently here and there, until it is equal.
puis preigne .i. des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	Then take one piece and stretch it gently here and there.
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi;	If it can jump up to the knees, when commanded to seize, and makes it vomit from disgust;
si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	If it jumps up, may God will it.
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if it is not as we have said, turn it little by little until it is according to the natural shape.
Car adonques ist il legierement.	Then it is gently turned little by little.
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons dit, si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en .i. mortier;	And if it does not come as we have said, take musk-root juice of height, oil of sage, and melted resin, and grind everything in one mortar;
et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement,	And apply the ointment made of woman's nature upon it.
puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz;	Then make her sit in a cold bath until below the ribs;
et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai .i. coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre;	and when she has been softened, make one collar of myrrh, place it beneath her, and leave it for an hour;
puis la fai seoir sus .i. siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	then make her sit on a chair, then make her cough and hold her mouth and nose, and press gently on the belly, for the infant will soon come out now.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	Of the birth of the child on its thighs
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc;	When the infant comes in this way, place the birthing forceps hand by hand.
puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor .i. lit;	then rest on its neck, and let the feet hang down, and lie it on one bed.
et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval;	fold its hands hand by hand, and then take hold of the hands above, and push the hips down, until it is aligned below.
et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains;	And if the child does not jump, take its feet and bend it forward, then bend it upward, then place your hands;
et ewe l’enfant poc et poc; et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	and order the woman to catch the child as it comes forth.
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	from the delivery of the child that comes out with one hand wide open
I covient engignier a ramener la main:	it is necessary to find a way to bring back the hand;
s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler;	If it cannot be returned [to its place], then lift up the woman and walk away.
s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus .i. lit, et li deboute les jambes forment;	If she cannot walk, then make her lie down on a bed and spread out her legs.
puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit;	Then administer the mustard plaster as I have told you;
et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus .i. siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main;	And if it does not give birth [to the dislocation], make her sit on a chair or seat, then study how to reset the hand.
et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer.	And cause it to give birth according to its natural shape, and make her vomit, and command her to hold on until the child comes out.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	Hold the baby's head by its neck, and spread your hands, and turn your face towards the mother's back.
I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement;	You must hold the baby's foot gently, then twist it slowly, and pull it out lightly.
et quant il est igalz, si met sus la nature muscillaige de altee et oile, si com nos avons dit, puis li comande qu’elle se mueve poc et poc;	And when it is equal [the joint], put above it a strong mustard plaster made with high altitude and oil, as we have said, then command that it moves little by little.
et quant tu avras ce fait, si la fai seoir sus .i. siege, et li comande k’elle se preigne; et la fai esternuer.	And when you have done this, make her sit on a chair and command her to take hold of it; then make her vomit.
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	in the same way, treat the second [injury].
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie;	When this kind of inflammation comes on in this manner to any other [part of the body], press it with your nail until the moisture is voided.
et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes;	And if the infant lies on its face and neck, press down on the belly, so that it is not held back, and the infant dies.
puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois:	Then push the child inwards, as much as you need to, and command the woman to take care of herself once.
adonques si istra legierement.	gently draw it out.
de l’issue des gemelz	of twin births
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent .iij. ou .iiij.; et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	Know that twins are born often, and sometimes three or four; and this is not strange, and it happens frequently.
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom;	Twin births are rare and do not survive very often.
je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude;	I know that they are multiplied, and the sperm that conceives them is linked to filth.
et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	And sometimes it returns to its natural state as a sow gives birth, as we have said.
Et s’il issent griement, si la cure si com nos avons dit, et soit li baile subtilz, et faice tost et legierement ceu qu’elle fait;	And if it emerges violently, as we have said, and the bailiff is skilled, and do quickly and gently what she does.
et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut.	and do as is appropriate to save life.
de plusors enfans	of many children.
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris .i. ou .ij. ou .iij. ou .iiij. ou .v. ou .vj. ou .vij., ou plusors jusc’a .xv., et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious,	At times they are formed in the womb: one, two, three, four, five, six, seven, or more up to fifteen; and all of them are fully formed like a child by the measurement of the wise glorious one.
et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient;	It is necessary that the bailiff knows this, for sometimes similar things happen.
si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	follow as it is required.
de l’enfant mort	Of a dead child
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains;	When you cure the woman of the dead or unborn child, as I said in the division, and it does not come forth, and you are forced to work with your hands;
si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort;	you must know if the woman is of pure virtue, and has no accident or fear of death;
si covient que li femme soit sovinee sus son dos, et soit ses chiés enclins aval, et les jambes levees;	The woman must lie on her back, with her head inclined downwards, and her legs raised.
et li ministre la teigne de .ij. pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant;	And the minister should shave the woman's head in two parts, or tie her down to the bed so that she is not treated in childbirth.
puis frotez la bouche de la marris d’oiles moistes avec muscillaige de altee et de fenugrec et semence de lin, puis oigne li baile ses mains de ces oiles et de ces muscillaiges;	Then rub the wife's mouth with moist oils mixed with myrrh and musk, and anoint her husband's hands with these oils and these myrrhs.
puis les boute en la marris legierement, puis quiere .i. leu ou elle boute les oncines que soient covenaubles a ceu,	Then push it gently into the socket, then search for one that fits, which is suitable.
et pren warde se li enfes est apparilliez qu’il dessende sus son chief;	and take care if the bones are broken on top of their head.
si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez,	if you pierce the joint with a needle or its neck or mouth or throat or under the chin or in the armpit or near the sides.
et se li dessendemens est sus piez, se li fiche ou poignil et as costes moienes;	And if the dislocation is on the feet, push or pierce it and bring the bones together in the middle;
et covient qu’il teigne l’oncine a sa main destre, et mette la corbeure entre ses dois de la senestre main, et li boute a tout sa main legierement, et fiche l’oncine en aucun de ces leus que nos avons dit, tant qu’il viegne a la chose vuide;	Then it is necessary to stretch the skin around it with the right hand, and place the curved instrument between the two of the left hand, and push gently with the whole hand, and pierce the skin in any one of the places we have mentioned, until it reaches an empty state;
et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	and this is the shape of the instrument:
puis fiche encontre .i. autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz;	Then insert [a needle or awl] opposite another one, or the third if needed, so that the extractions are equal;
et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	and then move it equally from one side to the other, so that they [the extractions] move out, and sharpen the awls so they hold, as shown in the following form:
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie;	If there remains a part, press some oil onto the blades of your fingers and apply them to that part, and pull the other part.
et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	And if it remains not at all, place this splint or higher up the limb, and do so until it goes completely away.
Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement,	When one hand is in front of the other, and cannot be returned due to strain.
si covient que tu envoloupes sus .i. drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote;	you should wrap it with one cloth, until it goes completely.
puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as .ij. piés.	Then press on the joint of the sole or at the heel, and you must do this with the other hand, and with two feet.
Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee,	And if the child's thigh is large and swollen at the outlet or has a hard head assembled.
si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue;	If you must insert the pointed spatula between your fingers, and press and extract the sharp one (arrow/stone).
ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui;	or you grind it with the instrument called "almidach", from which the form comes with the instruments or chapter that follows this.
et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment;	And do the same with infants naturally born with large heads;
et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles,	Then draw out the bones with forceps;
et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer;	And if the head leaps out and is pulled by force, it must be cut open to let out the moisture that is causing the problem.
et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues;	If it cannot come out, break it into smaller pieces where you can.
et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.	And if it [the patient] is swollen in the belly or beneath the ribs, then you must pierce it until the moisture flows.
