Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os,	Then I hurried up and cut into one of the wounds until I discovered a part of the bone,
et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens;	And I found it corrupt and pierced, and the corruption came up to the bone within;
je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai;	I seemed to see the bone as corrupt, and I thought there was no other corruption except that which I left;
et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder;	and I began to dress the wound with medicinal salves for a long time, but it could not heal;
et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant,	and then I dressed it again and discovered the bone as before,
et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu;	I found continuous corruption in the bone, I cured it, and then I extracted it, and I considered how to set it;
mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole,	but I could not manage to hold a palm's breadth of the bone, and I pulled it apart with all its marrow;
puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment,	then I restored it with medicine; and it became healed and set quickly,
et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir,	And it is not necessary to start the work again except due to the weakness of the patient who could not endure.
et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	and due to the fear of death that I had for him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement,	For there was often bleeding, but he recovered completely.
et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	And a hard cyst grew on the bone and he had a good disposition without any harm or side effects, neither in the air nor in coming.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere:	And if the bone is broken anywhere in the body, it must be set thus:
pren .i. liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert,	Take one splint and hold it at the open end of the broken bone,
et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut;	and command anyone to extend it upward;
et met .i. autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os,	and place another larger splint of linen over the flesh that is torn from the bone,
et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz,	And you draw out the corrupt flesh beneath the skin of the head,
et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char;	and uncover the flesh on the spot where you wish to be, that it does not burn the flesh;
et met .i. tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue;	and place a splint or a flat piece of wood under the bone to protect the rotten flesh;
et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	and it must be as much as one can see and feel the corruption, and also again.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie,	And if the bone is corrupt but does not open, and the corruption is in the middle or a part of it,
si descuevre la char toute; puis met .i. tison desoz,	un iron rod beneath it; then press.
et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption .i. poc, si com nos avons dit;	and press the cloth from one part of the corruption to another, and let the iron rod be as long as the length of the corruption, as we have said;
et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part;	if the corruption is in the joint, then strike the dislocated joint and hold the bone that contains it from the other side;
et se li corruptions est en la continuation des .ij. jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper;	And if corruption is in the continuation of the two joints, there is no other remedy than covering [it].
et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose,	and if corruption is at the tip of the hand or the foot, it is a very grave matter.
mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert;	but nevertheless, you must inquire about this corruption, how it has opened up.
et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire;	And purify it in all ways as you can, but let the vein or nerve not hinder you.
et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous,	And know that the incision and stitches for covering these bones are many, according to the position of the bone and the appearance of them.
et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce;	and their thickness, their fineness, their largeness and smallness, and their hardness;
et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument;	and for this reason, the tool must be adapted to each type of work;
et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art,	And know that the work will show you the instrument needed, according to the knowledge of this art.
et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies;	and the testimony of the ways of diseases;
si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	if you think about the instrument needed according to what is necessary.
dou feu	with fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer;	The shoulder may dislocate either from within or from outside.
et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie,	and when you have administered this corrosive treatment by means of medicine, it does not benefit at all.
si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient,	it is necessary to cover that limb up to the level where the corrosion occurs,
si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre;	if the patient becomes weakened by death or by the greater wickedness of the limb's defect;
et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu,	And the signs are that the limb turns black, as if it were burned by fire.
et porrist aprés la noiror, puis va celle corrosions de membre em membre,	And then comes the spreading of darkness, then follows the corruption of member to member.
et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper,	It takes all over the body; if you hurry to cover it.
et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans,	If it is from the sting of some poisonous animals, such as sea scorpions, vipers and similar.
se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	If the corruption is at the head of the tooth, strike it, but give it no space to come up to the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras;	And if it comes up to the wrist, strike it at the joint so that the corruption does not reach the arm;
et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors,	and if it reaches the arm, strike at the neck; and if it passes the neck, that is death.
et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut;	And no remedy is of any use but the amount of its potency;
et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe;	And thus one does when the corruption comes or the foot: if it comes in the first joint, then strike after the next joint;
et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet;	If it comes at the foot, then strike the entire foot;
et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil;	If it reaches the leg, then strike at the knee joint;
et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort;	If it rises above the knee, there is no other remedy for the patient but death;
et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz,	And the method for covering or dressing the limb is such that you bind it above and below,
et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont,	Extend one minister to the lower ligament and another minister to the upper ligament,
et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les .ij. liiens a .i. spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers;	And you separate the cartilage that is between the two ligaments by about one span wide, so that the bone is exposed;
puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part .i. drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain,	Then cover or dress it (the limb), and put on each side a linen cloth, so that the dressing does not touch healthy tissue,
et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	And the patient comes with another injury and abscesses growing.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment,	And bleeding comes when you work on it, so cauterize the wound quickly,
ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie,	or you put some restricting powders on it; then return to your medicine until it is completed,
puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then bind the limb with a suitable ligature, and let it heal until it is healed.
et je te conterai k’il avint a .i. home en som piet:	and I will tell you what happened to a man in the foot:
il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu,	a man had a blackness that resembled burnt by fire,
et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet;	the corruption began first in his toe of the foot, spreading through it all;
et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez;	And when the wounds see corruption, he pierces them with copper [instruments] and they become healthy;
et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi,	For a long time after the corruption returns or comes back with the hand, it came to me,
et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions;	And I put him on things that stimulated recovery after the body's cleansing, but the corruption could not stop;
et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere;	And you command me to cut off his hand, and I don't wish, unless I have hope of repelling the matter.
et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist,	and doubted also if by cutting his hand, it would not cause death.
car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre,	for the man's strength was weak; and he despaired completely, and returned to his land.
et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez;	if he were struck with a sword to cut off his hand, and he would be healthy.
et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	And I have not considered this except for when other options are needed, if it is necessary.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe;	An abscess occurs in the shin bone, and remains for such a long time that it causes a great swelling of the leg.
et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz;	Then they run and pierce through, causing the leg to jump, and the bones remain visible, as if a knight's.
et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com .i. drapelz deliiez,	And the skin that is above is also as thin as a linen cloth torn.
et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain»,	and it will not run up to the bone nor to the nerve, and such a disease is called "putrid".
et n’est mie apelee «fistule»;	and it is not called "fistula".
mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»;	but if it is so long that it comes all the way to the bone in depth, it is called "fistula".
et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz;	And the cook should be such that you wrap it completely, and equally when it is subtle, as a cloth.
et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	and not to become corrupt.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont,	And if you suspect that the meat will rot and the corruption is not complete,
et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi:	And the skin is thick with fat, if you cure it with a plaster like this:
regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor,	look to see if the breasts are large and swollen, and if they smell foul,
adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite:	then use this Egyptian plaster made in this way:
prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en .i. vassel au feu,	take asafetida, oil, and litharge, equally, and cook them together in one pot on the fire,
tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel;	As long as the medicine is red and thickens like honey;
et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel,	and then take from this according to your need, and make it into water and honey.
et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus;	and anoint the breast, and bind the wound;
et laisse la medicine ens par .ij. houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant;	and leave the medicine inside for two hours, then take it out straining;
fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor;	Make this procedure as many times as necessary, until the breast is drained; and remove the pus.
et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres,	and occasionally cleanse with water of ashes.
quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus,	when this medicine is not present, and you take vine ash and pour water over it,
puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez;	Then bleed and apply poultice until you know that the breast is well healed;
et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres,	and if the patient cannot endure it, do not use the Egyptian medicine or water with ashes,
si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet;	if the poultice is with water and honey or it has a little bit of crushed litharge;
ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver,	or you may apply poultice with honey and sweet wine, which has the property of purifying and washing.
et li vins fait aerdre le sain;	And the wine makes the blood congeal
et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez,	and when you have done this, and you are sure that the breast is well cleansed,
si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li,	if the enemas given causes the flesh to be produced in him,
et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin;	And you take a plaster of definite size, and make it with rose oil and wine.
ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens;	and you anoint it with some medications and unguents, whose properties or treating the unguents I have mentioned.
et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer,	if the wound on the breast is small, and the cloth plaster cannot enter,
si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein,	If a wound from a small iron is opened, place an Egyptian bandage on it.
ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez;	or Basilicon ointment, as long as it is opened wide;
et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement .i. leu ou li clistere puisse entrer,	and if the wound is too large, leave it at least one league or the size that can be reached by a clyster.
et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	and if the hernia that throws out the belly is above, lower it or even more below.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char;	For when the bone is fully set, do not let any cartilage grow on it.
et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues,	and if you cannot cover the wound beneath as you see fit,
si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est,	arrange it in such a way that the bone is set at its lowest point.
car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char	for when the bone is fully set, do not let any cartilage grow on it.
et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues,	And if you cannot cover the chest beneath as you see,
si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe;	Then proceed in this manner: let the intestines move gently downward and do not leave anything of the intestines.
et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sein,	and take consolidating medicines to place on the chest,
et estent sus .i. drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sein;	and stretch a linen cloth over the entire chest;
puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein .i. poc plus large dou premier,	Then press with force on the breast, i.e., slightly larger than the first [pressure point].
pues estent oignement souef sus .i. autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus,	then anoint gently on top of it, i.e., another cloth according to the size of the pressure point.
et le met sus le pertus dou sein por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois;	and place it on the breast pressure point to align the bone, and do not remove the large cloth except after many days once.
et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe,	and the one who is on the breast pressure point, remove often to remove the bone,
et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste;	And know what runs from the wound, whether it is poison or pus, or digested or undigested.
et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non,	and pay attention if the patient feels pain or not, and if there is an abscess or not,
et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sein,	and when your medicine has been applied in such a manner and you see that the pus rises above the wound's edge,
si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez;	If you know that breasts harden [or become firm], approach them with health.
et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie,	And then unbind it in the morning or afternoon, and when you are unbinding the wound,
si chainge .i. autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	If you change one [piece of] clothing and renew the dressing.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the breasts fall out improperly after many days, know that breasts do not harden [or become firm].
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit,	And if subtle poisons creep up after a long time, do not despair of health,
car li santez aproche. Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire;	for the health approaches. For there are people whose wounds swell up slowly in their wounds, and those who do the opposite.
et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie;	and if the stomach bloats too quickly after many days, know that the breast does not become sour.
et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut,	and if the breasts take a long time to dry out and are swollen, apply drying medicines that are moist in substance but dry in effect.
si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine;	As an egg is defined, for it contains much vitriol, and it is the last of medicines;
pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance;	take an egg white, define it with rose oil and stir equal parts of old wine in substance.
puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez,	then cook it and use it; this method makes it more cooked and thickened.
quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens,	When the diaphysis (long cylindrical part of a long bone) is not present,
ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu;	and take myrrh and aloes and incense, grind them together, and sprinkle the powder over the honey when it is on the fire.
et puis en glue .i. drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe,	and then dip one cloth, and lay it on the breast, and sometimes administer an Aristotle-long liniment,
et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire;	and roots of celestial lily (an ancient medicinal herb), which is like flour made from peas and quince.
et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use;	And in using simple or compound substances: grind them up, make it into powder, and put it on the honey as I said, and apply it.
et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure,	and if the patient is ill for a long time and is not cured by this treatment,
adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens;	then understand that the corruption has entered completely, and causes pressure on the bone or hard tissue, or ligaments;
si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	if the patient is cured by the treatment for fistula, as we have said before.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	Of the abscess of the nail
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main,	Panaric is an abscess that arises under the nail at the base of the hand.
ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois;	or at the foot, or by chance arises in other places;
et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient .i. aposteme chaus,	And when it (the wound) becomes inflamed and no care is taken, an abscess may form.
et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute;	And cut and pull out the nail until it reaches the root, and by chance you may cut through it completely.
et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	The corruption reaches the bone, causing a stinking pain, and the shoulder is large and discolored.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie,	When you follow the treatment as we have described in the previous section, but it does not help,
si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle,	It is necessary that you cut off all the superfluidity which has accumulated on the nail.
puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	then cauterize the wound after.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne;	The cauteries are very great aid if the bone is healthy and the nail is healthy;
et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece,	and when the nail after the flesh adheres, and it starts to thicken and swell,
si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char,	It is necessary that you place the rod under the nail so as not to touch it.
et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement,	and push it upwards, and strike the soft tissue gently and lightly.
et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout;	and place on top of the remaining soft tissue medical substances that are burning and corrosive to remove everything.
puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then, heal it with ointments until it is healed.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner;	And if the corruption is in the bone, strike it and draw it out, for as much as the bone is corrupted, it cannot heal.
et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en .i. des nous si com il est devant dit,	and if you see the tooth decayed, strike it with one of these tools as said before,
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	then heal it until it is healed.
et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier;	and if it is wounded and boiled, and feels great pain, it is necessary that you drain it first;
puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus,	Then pierce the angle of the spur with a pointed spatula while cutting across it.
et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor;	And ensure that the cut does not reach the flesh underneath the angle, because the patient would feel too much pain.
et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	and if it happens, place something over it to ease the pain.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	the pain in the thumb joint of the hand
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus,	The patient who is born with tumors on their hands by chance, are entirely fleshy.
et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle,	and by chance it has bone or nail, and sometimes it has a nail.
et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	and none of them are born at the root of the joint, but rather in some of our fingers.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet,	The one who is born in any knuckle of the finger does not move,
et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet;	And the one born at the joint of the thumb, by chance becomes mute;
la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere:	the size of the one who is fat is light, in this manner:
taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	The size of it at its root is as wide as a large spatula.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	The one born in the root of the joint is difficult to treat: keep him covered.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os,	In one who is born or about to die, it is necessary that you cut round the cartilage up to the bone,
puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	then cut the bone with an appropriate saw, then heal it until it is healed.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	Simultaneously, swelling comes at the joints due to birth, or from an injury, or burn, or similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz;	It is necessary that you cut this swelling so that it can heal according to its natural forms;
puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent;	Then put between two tents or cloths soaked in rose oil, so that they do not stick.
ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	And you place between two thin planks, until the limbs are fixed as required.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	If it comes to any of its joints with the palm, then strike that bond as required.
Des vils	Poor people
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors;	The veins are large, swollen, filled with melancholic excesses that come into various members of the body;
et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	and it happens in legs more often in those who walk and work and carry, than in others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	Therefore, you must occasionally administer purge of the gall and then cleanse the basilica.
Li cure de fer si est selonc .ij. manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir;	The iron cure is in two ways: one is to strike it, and draw out black blood;
et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	And another way is to open a vein, and draw all its blood out.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez,	The incision method is as follows: first cut deeply into the leg with hot sharp steel until the flesh becomes soft,
puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil;	Then hold the leg of the patient above the knee to the part below the thigh;
puis cope la voinne en .i. leu, ou en .ij. ou en .iij., d’une taille large,	Then open the vein in one, two or three places, of a large size,
puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir;	Then slit and draw out the black blood from the arm to the hand, from one end to the other, as much blood as the strength of the patient can withstand;
et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire;	and then tie it up, and command him to bind himself with meat that makes black bile disappear.
et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	And recommence the evacuation and the purge when the veins are full, and it harms the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil,	The elevation of it is as follows: raise the leg of the patient, if there is much hair,
puis le met ou bain, et li. arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes;	then put it in water and heat the leg with warm, hot water until it turns red and swells the veins;
et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville;	And if you have no other remedy, heat it with fire, and then strike it towards the vein near the top of the thigh, or in the part below the knee.
puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent;	Then scrape the skin with the knife and peel back the vein from both sides, as far as it appears when felt.
et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche;	and when it is seen red and black, and when it enters the skin, it seems like a white cord.
puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier,	Then push the thigh bone downwards until it is raised to the skin, and then bend it slightly at the angle.
puis le cope en .i. autre leu ensus iij. dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere,	Then break the arm into another place four fingers' breadth below; then scrape the skin over the vein until it appears.
puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers;	Then tie up the thigh bone, as you did before, and bend it to another angle, as you did first.
puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet,	Then break a different size (or multiple sizes if necessary), tie it up, and bend it to the thigh bone.
puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope;	Then draw and extract up to the second joint; then remove joint by joint until it comes out entirely, then strike (the dislocation).
et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout .i. fil fort double,	and if you cannot draw and lift it, push an awl with very thick double thread through it.
et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz .i. rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse;	and draw and lift it (the dislocated joint), and you push a splint under one rib, and turn your hand from side to side until it comes out.
et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide;	And keep it from bursting, for if it bursts, it cannot be drawn or lifted, and it harms the patient.
et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have treated it all, place linen soaked in wine and rose oil on the wound site; and care for it until it heals.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit,	And if the vision is constricted, twisted, and wrapped together, and it is not straight as we have said,
si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	Therefore, you must cut it forcefully but do not cover it; drag it as we have said before.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne;	The form of iron used to pierce the bladder does not bend and does not cut, but it should pierce the vein.
et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	and is large-curved, for if it is thin, it would pierce the vein, but be thick as we have said, and here is the shape:
De la voinne civile	From the civil vein
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor;	This vein is located in the legs, in warm parts where there are no herbs or trees, and on land with no moisture.
et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir,	And by chance, a boil arises somewhere other than in legs, and this happens from the corruption that comes beneath the skin.
si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	When it comes within the body like a snake and spreads, incise between the skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation,	And if the signs of the beginning of this vein are such that there is a very large inflammation in the leg.
puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	Then the joint changes (dislocates), and the vein begins to forcefully come out, just like a root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a .ij. З., et la noe,	When the joint opens, it is necessary that you wrap around a piece of wood from 6 to 8 inches long and tie it.
et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe;	and leave the wood (plank) at the leg, and every time it (the shoulder) slips out, you wrap it around the plank and tie it.
et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue;	And if it is too long, take a part of it, roll up the rest, and do not cover it at its root until it is all out.
car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie;	for if you cut it, it goes back into the flesh, causes an abscess and pus or a bad disease.
por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors;	therefore, it must be treated little by little until the end, and nothing is left on the body.
et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de .v. paumes de lonc, ou de .x.,	And sometimes this vein is about five or ten fingers in length.
et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de .x. paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute .i. rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons,	And a man came to me whose length was ten fingers, and when you sew it, push one bean or pea through it and pierce it all the way through.
si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	So that everything comes out; empty the matter within it, and bring medicine to the place, allowing it to decay for any length of time, then heal it as one heals an abscess.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet,	And sometimes in this vein there are more rain-like substances, and similarly when it opens at the joint of the finger or toe.
et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	And it comes much from wounds, and from which it jumps out; treat it then as we have said before.
Des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	From the worms that are born between skin and flesh
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués,	This disease is called in our land "cow disease", because it often happens to cows.
et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant,	and it is a small worm that is born between skin and flesh, and travels through the whole body expanding and contracting,
et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer;	And it feels very painful to move from one limb to another, until it rips the skin or jumps out.
et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre;	And it is infested by purulent humors, like worms and snakes and roundworms or belly lice.
et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil,	And there is doubt about its nature, for when it travels through the body, it rises to the head and reaches the eye.
par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	By chance it enters and destroys the eye; and this happens many times.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait:	When you see it to cure and draw, one can force it only when it goes:
si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement,	then you must lie the limb above and below with a strong rope tightly.
puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves,	then strike on top and pull forcefully, and if the limb is fully inserted into the flesh, do not pull it back,
si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire;	if you cauterize it with fire, until it dies;
et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit;	And the greatest harm it does is that it runs the oil, as we have said.
et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer;	and if you see it coming or close to the oil, hold the sorcerer beneath it in form, then strike above, and pull it out.
et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries,	And it is necessary for the patient to use body purification with medicines that dissolve bad humors.
et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	And let them eat boiled meat that has been purified.
De la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	Of the pain coming from windiness
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres,	This disease is called on our land "wind-disease," and it is a pain that comes in some limbs.
et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	And it moves from limb to limb; and I saw what I am telling you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais;	I was summoned to a sick woman, and I uncovered her arm, and saw a small swelling in the armpit of the arm.
et .i. poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule,	And after that, it started swelling as if a worm were climbing towards the shoulder.
plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre;	more rapidly than any other thing, just like living silver when it cuts from one place to another.
li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule,	the pain moved away from that place and pierced into the shoulder.
et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais;	And a little while later, it runs through the entire body until it reaches the other arm;
puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	Then I found that it keeps turning around the body, as I saw it.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I marveled much how it moves from member to member, for I had never seen this disease in such a manner before.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre,	However, I had often heard that the pain moves from one place to another,
mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme;	but I did not want it at all, as I saw it in the woman;
et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes,	and I thought that it was because the woman had a dry body, and her veins exposed.
et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte;	and this is where that constricted wind appears.
et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	and it does not appear according to this reasoning to those who are luxurious and have moist bodies and covered veins.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit,	And when you wish to treat this illness, and the patient feels that pain, if it opens as we have said,
si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer;	then press above and below forcefully, and then press firmly until those windings are forced back to their place.
et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz,	and cauterize the place; if you do not see it with your eyes,
si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	if you treat those that push out the windings, like corrupted pills and pills of snakeroot, and similar things.
Des saiettes	Of arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Arrows come in various forms, depending on their appearances and the places in the body they strike.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees;	The differences between them are that some have large points, small ones, pointed and flat-tipped;
et de celles qui ont .ij. angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces;	and those that have two points, those with barbs, and those that have splinters.
et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc .ij. manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit,	and a dislocation occurring in any member occurs in two ways: either in the main member (head),
si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	or in secondary members such as the brain, heart, liver, spleen, lungs, intestines, bladder, and similar organs.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent:	When it (the dislocation) occurs in any place of these members, and the signs of death, which I will tell you afterwards, appear:
si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions;	Therefore, you must be careful in the extraction of this arrow, for death may come after in many situations;
et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	And when this bad sign does not become apparent, and the arrow is not completely in, pull it out, and treat the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil,	And when the arrowhead pierces the skull bone and the piece of bone splinters off above the skull,
est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole;	It is when the eyesight darkens and swells, and reddening and pain in the tongue, and convulsions and confusion of mind, and vomiting of bile.
et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix;	And by chance, without force from the nostrils, or ears; and by chance, loses speech and voice;
et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char;	Jumps out of the wound white matter like cheese, and also jumps as if burned by hot iron;
et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	If this sign appears, refrain from treatment and pull out the arrow if it is not in.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide;	The sign of the arrow when it falls or pierces, is that it is near the left breast and feels like it has been driven into something hard, not empty;
et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope:	And by chance, the patient may fall silent like the hairs, and black cold blood appears, and chilliness and cold sweat, and fainting occur.
saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	Therefore, the patient senses doubt that death is near.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	The sign of an arrow that never pierced the flesh is that without pus gushing from the wound, the throat swells, and the patient's complexion changes, he breathes heavily and seeks fresh air.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	If the arrow falls on the blanket of the bed, it is lodged in the ribs; and it expels a large pus, great pain, and heavy breathing; and all the limbs of the shoulder move.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if an arrow or stomach falls out from the wound, by chance, anything of undigested meat may jump out from the wound.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if an arrow or stomach falls in (the wound), and anything of excrement jumps out through the intestine route, there is no hope for the cure, nor in the extraction of the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	If an arrow falls in the bladder and urine jumps out and comes out, and the patient feels great pain; know that the wound is fatal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other limbs, such as the arms and legs, neck, shoulders, hips, buttocks, spine of the back, ribs, and feet; and similar members are safe according to several conditions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in the nerve or artery and it is not poisoned, as I will tell you what happened to me, do this instead.
Il avint a .i. home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis:	It happened to a man that an arrow pierced or wounded the root of his nose:
je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	I pulled it, and drew it out beneath the fat of the ear, and it was saved without damage.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz,	And pulled out an arrow that had pierced the oil gland beneath the paper-like membrane.
et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust,	And the arrow was inserted, and it could not reach further than the tip towards the flesh,
et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout .i. fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	And the arrow was large like a Turkish bow, with a light iron point shaped like ears; it pierced through, and no bad accidents happened to him.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles:	And the arrow passed through the throat of a Christian, and the arrow was an Arabic one with ears,
je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	I was a bearded man, and became subtle enough to pass through, and the Christian was unharmed.
Et traï une saiette a .i. home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit;	And draw an arrow out of a man who was shot or wounded, and I thought he would die;
et puis qu’il ot passez .xxx. jors, si ne mua point sa disposition;	and then after thirty days, his condition did not change;
je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	I cut above the arrow, trapped it, drew it out, and there was no bad incident.
Et si vis .i. home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus;	And if you want to treat a man who has an arrow lodged or stuck into his back, and the wound is sewn up;
et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez,	and the arrow remains inside him, and does not change its position naturally,
ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	nor can it be found in any of his natural movements.
Et vis .i. autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie;	And you want to treat another man who has an arrow lodged in his face, and the wound is sewn up;
et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	And it remains in such a way, enduring great pain; many other similar things.
Et traï une saiette a .i. home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz,	Take an arrow out of one of the princes' king, who was pierced in the neck,
et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue	and was slightly leaning towards the right side; the arrow was completely straightened.
Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue .iij. jors. Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I was summoned to the treatment after she had fallen ill for three days. I found the wound very narrow.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie;	I tried to probe it with a subtle instrument but felt nothing.
et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	and it felt pointed and pain beneath her right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette	I thought it was from the tip of the arrowhead.
Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast;	I apply the plaster soothing and digestive to the joint, as it does not swell.
et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	And the arrowhead appeared at the joint.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens,	I applied the plaster for many days, and straightened the wound directly, and the patient remained healthy for a long time.
tant qu’il sentit la saiette .i. jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	until he felt the arrowhead in his intestines for one day; and he told me.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte,	I apply corrosive medicine to the wound by hand for several days until it is drained.
et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu;	and pull, and feel the head of the arrowhead which protrudes from its place;
puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement;	then I pierced the wound with that corrosive medicine until the head of the arrow appeared clearly.
et trespassa bien li termines entor .iiij. mois,	And he passed beyond the limits in four months.
et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir;	Then I will lance the wound that I have pierced with the forceps and split it open from both sides, but it could not heal.
adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris .i. jor as tenailles bien faites,	Then I continued to refine and invent various methods of instruments, until I made the forceps well for one day.
selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	According to its shape that will come at the end of this chapter, I will keep it until its end and restore the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer:	And the physicians judge that the nose cartilage cannot be restored:
je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	Then I will restore it, and the wound will heal, and the patient will be completely healed.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes,	I have told you about the extraction of some arrows,
si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre;	If you apply your remedy to this (condition), I do not say to which specifically, for books cannot fully grasp everything.
mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant,	but wise masters understand well about a little thing and about that which is failing and in need.
trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	true nine works, and nine tools, at the end of things strange that happen in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc .ij. manieres:	I say that arrows do not enter members where they are inserted except according to two ways:
ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part;	or through the side where they enter, or by some other way;
et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	and that which flies out from there where it enters is an arrow entering the flesh, and occasionally flies away at some point.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue;	If it does not fly away immediately, leave it until the flesh heals around it, and let the opening heal;
et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor;	And if it is embedded in bone and cannot be removed, leave it for several days and try to extract it every day.
et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout .i. foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	And then it jumps, and if it does not jump, pierce it all around with a sharp tool, as long as the area around is widened, and then pull it.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil,	If the arrow is driven into the skull bone and goes to one of the brain ventricles,
et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors,	And some of the accidents that I have mentioned to the patient: do not draw it out immediately, but let it heal evenly after several days.
car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	If the arrow reaches thus far, it is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac,	And if the arrow is only pierced in the bone but does not reach thus far,
et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And the patient remains for some days with bad accidents if he cannot draw the bow.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is deeply pierced and cannot come out by itself, then administer tourniquets around it as I have told you; then cure the wound until it heals.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente;	And if the arrow is put back into place within the body so that it cannot be seen, pull on it firmly;
et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble;	and if you feel it, pull it with any suitable instrument;
et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette,	and if the narrowness of the wound or the depth of the arrow prevent you from pulling it out,
et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans;	And there is no bone, nerve, or vein, if the wound is large enough.
et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient,	and pull out the arrow if possible, and if it has ears in the arrow as they are,
si oste la char qui est ens fichie de .ij. pars au mues que tu pues,	if you can remove the bone that has been impaled by two parts in the muscles.
et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire;	and then break or fold the arrow's ears (barbs) as much as possible so you can pull it out.
et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	And be careful not to break the arrowhead, but rather pull it out more gently.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	If you cannot do it at once, push the lance to the bone and then pull, for extraction will be easier in this case.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre;	If the flow of blood obstructs you, bring to hand what we have said about the cure in its chapter;
et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril,	And beware of cutting the nerve and vein, and use tools as you can safely pull out the arrow without risk.
ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens,	Either quickly or slowly, either firmly or gently; place the patient according to the form he was in when the arrow struck him.
car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	for this is the greatest aid that can be, and if you cannot do it, place him according to what the signs show you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment:	The arrow that comes from another place, if it opens anything of it, or the skin is swollen in that spot as one can see or feel:
taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	then cut along that spot, as long as the scissors can grasp it, and then pull it out; if it does not come out now.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is retained in the bone, round your hand and turn it until it enters the bone, expand the bone, then pull it out.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer;	And if it cannot come out, let it stay for a while, and then continue the extraction until it comes out completely.
et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust;	and if it were of an arrow shaft, push it all the way through.
et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre .i. estrument cheveit,	and if it had fallen and you see that it requires a pointed instrument, use a pointed instrument to remove it.
si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer,	If the tip of the arrow enters the hair of the instrument; then push forcefully,
et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute .i. estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	and if the arrow is stuck in the instrument's hair, use the instrument with its pointed end entering it to facilitate extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues,	And if the arrow is touched, you must cut around the affected area where the poison is, if possible,
puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	then treat the wound as appropriate.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope;	And if an arrow falls or pierces the belly, bladder, side, or kidney, and it is near, and you can cover over it, then do so.
et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est;	And be careful not to cover the vein and nerve, then extract it, then stitch the wound if necessary.
et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	heal it until it is healed.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the tweezers used for removing arrows is similar to an owl's beak, and here is its shape:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And there are many ways to do it: large, medium, and small, according to the size of the arrowhead.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel,	The shape at the tip of the hair is also like the feather of a bird,
por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	to stick the point of the arrow, as its shape is:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	The shape of the pliers for sticking and extracting is as follows:
des voinnes dou cors communes	Openings of common veins
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont .xxxi., de coi il a ou chef xvi.,	Openings of veins from which one drains are 31, of which there are 16 heads
c’est a savoir: .ij. batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»;	This means: two veins that are behind the ears, which are called "doubs 'herbech'"
et les .ij. arteres qui sont en .ij. temples apparans;	And the two arteries which are in the two temples appear;
et .ij. voines que sont en .ij. larmiers des .ij. eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»;	And the two veins that are in the two eyes of the eyelids, which are called "aspirates";
et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis;	and the vein that is on the forehead; and the vein that is at the top of the neck;
et les .ij. guindeges qui sont ou col;	And the two glands which are at the neck;
et les .ij. voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»;	and the two veins that are above the mouth, and these veins are called "augeherich";
et .ij. voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	and the two veins that are under the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont .v. en chescun bras:	The veins that are commonly known to be five in each arm:
l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»;	The first one is cephalic, located on the left side of the chest, and lay people call it "vein of the head".
et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique,	The second one is called "fistula," and is composed of the cephalic and basilic.
et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit,	And lay people call it "vein of the heart"; the basilic is located on the right side of the chest.
et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile,	And lay people call it "vein of the belly," and it is above the abdomen.
et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	And this [refers to] the one who is healed, whose wound clearly opens above the pocket.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a .ij. rains;	The vein that is between the little finger and the ring finger, and if it has two joints.
et en la jambe et ou piet sont .iij. voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit,	And in the leg and foot there are four veins: one is beneath the calf of the left,
et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei;	And the second tendon which is at the right ankle; and the vein called "nasse," which is in the left ankle.
et en l’autre jambe sont .iij. voinnes desoz celles.	In the other leg there are three veins beneath these (veins).
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine;	The venous sinus after the ears assists in ancient catarrhs and migraines.
et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide,	The quality of the vein as I tell you is that you raise the head of the patient,
et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis,	And rub the joint or veins with a rough cloth; then tighten the patient's neck with a screw.
tant que les .ij. voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en .ij. leus dependens dou chief:	until the two veins appear behind the ears in the two places depending on the head.
quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche;	then take hold of it (the pulse), and where you feel the throbbing under your hand, press down on it firmly.
puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont,	then take the lance and thrust it through the vein up to the bone, then move your hand up along the whole vein.
et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien .ij. dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues;	And make two incisions through the skin and vein well with a knife, and draw out the blood until it stops.
puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee;	then strain and tie it until it heals;
et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	And I have already said the incision and the cautery in the first book.
Li sainie des .ij. arteres que sont en .ij. temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene,	The healing of the two arteries that are in the temples, it is worth using emigraine for older people.
et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz;	and sodium, and ophthalmia treated, and at the eyes sore with tears.
et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis:	and the qualities of the healer are as I say:
et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les .ij. voinnes aperent apertement;	and it is that the patient extends his neck, until the two veins appear openly.
et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche;	and feel the pulse beneath your thumb, then press gently.
puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz,	Then, lift the key on the vein at its top, indicated by your finger, and push the lance beneath.
et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en .ij. autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit;	and lift the vein at its top, and prick (it), just as you have done in two other veins, and make an incision for the blood according to your need.
puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton;	then undo the patient, and place your finger on the vein for an hour, then put cotton over it.
et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	and then close (the vein) forming it, and let it heal until it is healed; and we have already spoken of their dressing and extraction, where the book begins.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor;	The vein at the forehead is as valuable as the cephalic vein in ancient facial diseases, and it has migrated and turned red;
et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere;	And its characteristic is that the patient extends his neck while twisting, until the vein appears;
puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	then take the instrument called "fosseur", whose shape is:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues;	And place the point on the vein, and press down from your hand, or something else, and let the blood come out according to the quantity that you see;
puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	Then loosen the patient's neck and tie the vein when it is healthy, without ever using a wide flame.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	Moreover, the flames should not be too sharp; and take care to pierce through the side because the bone is near, and by accident break the flames when they are fine.
Li sainie des .ij. voines que sont en .ij. larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice;	The piercing of the two veins that are in the two armpits helps the eyes, the thigh, the groin, and the wound in the oil, and the diseases of the face;
et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant;	And the quality of their blood is such that the patient twists their neck in turning it with some cord, as before.
puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	Then the blood, and let the vein be crossed, a little long by the flame a little wide, for there is no flesh there.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	If the iron is fine and breaks, then make a suture of blood, as much as you need, and then tie it up with cotton, and bind it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice,	The sanity of the vein from the neck is beneficial against ague, and against smallpox, and diseases of the face.
si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene;	like emigraine (migraines) and redness that comes in the face, and especially when it is old;
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre,	and the qualities of the sanity are that the patients compress their neck, then squeeze their nose with your left hand,
et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les .ij. narines,	And take the subtle flame long, and thrust it into the gap between the two nostrils,
car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre;	because the vein does not open well in that manner, and the wound will begin to heal now.
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree;	do not go too deep, and let the blood flow as needed, then bind it for a night, because it is quickly restored.
et c’est li forme dou flaime:	this is the shape of the flame:
Li sainie des .ij. guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes;	The first joint of the two fingers helps in the stiffness of the elbow, at the beginning of swelling, and in many diseases, abscesses, corrosions, herpes, and inflammations.
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit;	And the qualities of the joint are such that the patient straightens his neck from under one and the other, as we have said;
et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus .i. siege,	let the master be standing over the head of the patient, and the patient lie on one seat,
puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est;	Then, open the vein lengthwise a little widely, then drain the blood gently, as necessary.
puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement,	Then repair the other side of the vein, then untie the ligature, and tighten all the veins moderately.
que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	Do not strangle the patients; let them be until morning so that the wounds heal.
De la sainie des leivres	Of the treatment of livestock (or animals)
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The treatment of wounds of the upper lip helps with swelling in the mouth, decay of gums, and cuts or splits in the lips, as well as teeth problems and around them.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit;	And the qualities of the treatment are to make the patient sit before you and hold his neck as I have said;
puis torne la levre, et regarde as .ij. voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre,	then turn the upper lip, and look at the two places: one is on the right upper lip, and the other is on the left.
et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires:	And they are recognized by the fact that they are black, and by the fact that around them there are small black veins.
cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance,	Take hold of both of them then, and if you do not recognize them, and you are in doubt about it.
si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des .ij. voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	grasp the largest one of each pair, and also do the same for the two veins above and below, because it is done in the same way.
De la sainie desoz la lengue	From beneath the tongue.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche;	The evacuation of veins that are below the tongue helps after the head injury, and it is at the incision of the neck, and the diseases of the eye, and the diseases of the mouth;
et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire:	and the quality of bleeding is that the patient should squeeze between your hands before the sun, lift the tongue, and look at every side a black vein:
saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	then one and the other, but do not go too deep, for below are the arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc .ij. manieres:	The veins of the cost are commonly healed according to two methods:
ou em poignant a tout .i. flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»;	or when pricking at any one spot with large mirrhin or olive oil of subtle kind as you cut through it, and it is called "anesil";
et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	and are broad and thin according to the width and narrowness of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The shape of the mirrhin flame is very renowned and is broad as you can see:
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble;	And it is necessary to open the swollen veins that contain thick blood and are troubled.
et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	and this is the form of olive oil flame:
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	and it is pointed more finely, and it is for thinning subtle veins that contain thin yellow blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre;	The sanitation of the basilica vein, which is one of these veins, helps with diseases that are under the throat, neck, chest, and abdomen.
et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	And it is necessary for the lord [physician] to drain the blood well, and to pierce the artery that is below.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit;	And if he touches the artery, and bleeding comes out, it needs to be stopped, as I have said;
et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	And the flame should not be pressed, but rather sliced like an incense stick.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre;	And if the basilica does not open manifestly, then you must force it open and change another.
ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement;	or you wish to have no pain in it, or you open the vein in its place with the arm: it opens manifestly.
et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	and apply the copper to the fire as we have said.
