Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz;	And if you wish to know the place of the wound, then it is necessary that you pull on the arm, and you touch until you find the pulse.
puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil;	Then sign the place with a cross, then tie the arm, and burn the vein with fire.
et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	And beware not to hit the artery when you see the place swollen, for it is an artery; avoid it then.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere:	If you see it swelling up high like the urine of a child and it is red and thin, know that it is not from an artery:
haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient;	Then hasten yourself, put your finger on it for a long time, then cut off your finger if the blood does not stop flowing, which often happens;
se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	The patient should keep his arm still, and let it be like that, the sick person does not move it; he should be in fear, and not move it until it is healthy again.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	If the wound is not staunched, and it bleeds, and the medicine is not present, then cut the artery if it is open, because the head of it recedes; stop the bleeding from the wound.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor;	Take a piece of the outer bark of the willow, cut it, and take one half and apply it well until the next day.
se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc;	If it does not stop bleeding, that is good; if it does not, heal it as we have said, with powders that stop blood.
et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	And the stopping of bleeding is not necessary in many situations because of the small size of the wound and the strength of the ligament of the arm.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz,	The vein in the middle helps to drain blood from the head above, and from the body below,
por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit;	Because it is composed of the basilica and the cephalica, as we have said;
et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf,	and the lord should pierce through to the nerve that is beneath, and if it pricks too deep, and he finds the nerve,
et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner;	and it swells and the patient becomes sickly and grey, and by chance cannot be cured;
et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	and this nerve opens up frequently, and if it does not open in any man due to its subtlety, then you must cauterize it with the instrument anesthetic; and cut off the nerve to your ability.
Et se il a voinne entre les .ij. ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if there is a vein between the two nerves, make it long.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz;	The vein of the head, if it draws blood from the head, helps the eyes;
et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	It is necessary to vein with olive oil or myrtle fire, for it is the safest of all veins, because there is no nerve or artery beneath it.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence;	Therefore, one must seek the lighter joint, and not to worry if it is necessary for the first time, and start again.
et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	If the joints swell in some men, when it is necessary for the first time, but he does not worry about it.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the blood is according to your judgment.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit,	The first thing you should know about bleeding is that bleeding is not performed for any other purpose than to preserve health.
et por eschuir les maladies a venir;	And to avoid future illnesses;
et soit li sainie faite en l’une des .iij. voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique;	And the incision shall be made in one of the four veins that are named: namely, cephalic, saphenous, and basilic.
et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent;	And it should be incised at the beginning of spring, and in autumn and winter after eating, when the signs of filling appear;
et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés .ij. houres ou .iij. dou jor.	And it should be bled for the first or third day, after 2 hours or 3 days.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens;	The bleeding given to diseases has no fixed hour, but when there is a need for day or night, in all hours and at all times.
et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a .xiiij. ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	And it should not be bled children under 14 years old, nor women in the fourth month of pregnancy up to the seventh.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez .lx. ans.	Nor elderly people who have passed 60 years.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier,	And when someone wishes to heal themselves, in whatever way that may be, it is necessary that they empty their intestines with a gentle enema.
s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz;	if there is much feces retained, so that the veins do not carry away the superfluidities harmful to the main limbs.
ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques;	he who is excessively salted with meats, or drunk, until he recovers from that state, or watery.
et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors;	And if there is wounding after the passion of colic, vomiting, loosening of the belly, multiplication of abscesses in a woman, and work, watchfulness, and labor, and whatever the virtue of the body or the weapon,
puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir;	then thin the fluids, if he does not have a thick constitution, with foods and drinks and medicines, if you have that power.
puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc,	then immerse or bathe him, if nothing hinders, to thin the blood,
et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit;	And heal the vein with the plaster as we have said;
et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses;	Keep yourself on that day from work, and from pain, and from lust, and similar things;
et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras .ij. fois ou .iij.,	and be lying down and joyful, and let the healer raise himself higher than the one being healed, and rub the arm 2 or 3 times;
puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans;	then draw the thread moderately, because when it is too tight or loose, it cannot cure him;
et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on;	And then rub the joint with your hands until the veins swell, and feel for them.
puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier,	Then wet the linen cloth with a little bit of old oil, then place your fingertip of your left hand on that vein beneath the joint where you want to cauterize.
que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	so that the vein does not burst when pierced.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit,	For there are veins that run like cords in a sieve, and some of them are filled with windiness.
si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus;	if you put fire upon it, the flame retreats and cannot open the vein, and thus it is one of these.
et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	and if it opens the vein, the wound is too narrow, therefore the sieve-makers must be cautious in these matters.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the vein is opened for the first time, it is good; if not, then begin again slightly under that place or quickly above, if the places are not swollen.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse .i. jor ou .ij., et ne liier mie le bras:	And if the places are swollen, and the patient is afraid, let it rest for one or two days, and do not bind the arm:
par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait;	In case there comes an abscess, let it not enter bathing; then begin the healing if it pleases the patient:
et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement;	If the hole is small or you doubt whether it does not emit as much blood as you see, then apply heat directly to that hole:
et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	And the wound is opened slightly, so that the area swells; for this often happens when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile;	If you see the area swollen, do not start draining immediately, but put some oil on it, for it will heal the body of blood and make the oil spread in this place.
et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc;	and administer the oil in each wound that you drain, to stop the flow of blood;
et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	And this same thing happens with triceps and biceps when set in place; if they are too subtle (small) and split apart when they are too large.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite,	If there comes a large abscess, which often happens, especially when the opening of the vein is small,
si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre;	If you hurry, put wet sponge (sponge soaked in warm water and oil) on it for an hour;
et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie;	And it is necessary that you do this after the evacuation of blood from the vein, and if it remains in place after some days without any blackness or greenness, that does not harm it.
et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	And if you see, place something of aloes or myrrh in its lower part, under the wound, as a mark, or similar.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And many times there appears an abscess and signs at the wound of the basilica; therefore place your hand over it, and if you find it soft when compressed by the hand, then that is the bad sign.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai .i. emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore do not place anything of what has been said, for by chance without the artery; but make one dry compress to harden the place, then cure it with another remedy until it is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And draw blood from each according to the amount of its virtue and the color of the blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	For if the wound is black, let it bleed until it becomes red; and if you see it thick, let it become thinner; and if it is too hot, let it cool down.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges;	And it is necessary for the one who is wounded and has need of bloodletting, to make a larger incision, and let the veins be wide.
et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant;	And for the weak one, do the opposite, and it is necessary to let him bleed little by little, and it should be done by cutting across, not by pricking.
et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	And this method of bloodletting is safe from discharge and paralysis of nerves, and it is better than the long bloodletting or the wide one.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc .iij. fois ou .iiij.	And for the body which needs bloodletting, it is necessary to give bread soaked in apple pulp; if he is heated, let him bleed 4 or 6 times.
Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	And if it is of cold complexion, let it eat soft bread soaked in sweet syrup, or sweet scented syrup with spices such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and sesame, and fragrant syrup.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil,	And if it swells at the wound after bleeding, you must give him broth of cooked meat and fragrant subtle syrup.
et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	and use other things as we have said in the section or chapter on fainting, for the evacuation of blood.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	If you want to dislocate someone's arm and heal it again, if necessary, when it has been weakened by prolonged healing, it should heal little by little, according to the quantity of its strength continually.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine .vij. houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	If you want to dislocate someone's arm after the first healing, and it has healed in seven hours after the first healing or after the ninth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	If you want to heal from another part, it should heal on the second day or the third day.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson;	Because there is much blood within the body which is already heated, and it brings fever; therefore a large amount should be drained, and the opening widened until it gushes out in a pan.
puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson,	then you treat all the conditions of health, and place your hand on top of the toes when they heal, so that death does not come in the place of a pan.
et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens;	and this happens many times, when the healers are negligent;
et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus;	And it is not good that when you dislocate the arm and draw blood a second time, and the wound is closed, that you press forcefully.
ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz;	If it is bent, extend the arm as much as possible, for this would be bad;
mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer,	but leave it until blood flows out again; or you will prick it with the tip of the flame, causing the coagulated blood in the vein to flow out.
et met sus .i. poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	and put .1 piece of fresh linen on top and press lightly.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein has burst, do not tie it or squeeze it until the abscess is appeased.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if you need to draw blood a second time, do it in the same place or another vein or the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The veins in the arm are not found in the neck because they are composed of something else.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges;	And the method of bloodletting is that the patient puts his hand in hot water until the veins are red.
puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc;	Then it shall be tied moderately, so that the vein appears clearly, then press gently across, neither too wide nor too long.
et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez;	and the wounds shall be cut open wide, and press firmly near the joint of the hand, and if it cannot heal, place the hand in hot water and let the blood flow out into the water until you have enough.
et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit;	and if it is on the inside (of the chest), do not push the hand into hot water, for it puts it more in winter than summer.
et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	And the vein of this vessel is safer than all other vessels, as there are neither artery nor nerve in it.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere:	The vein of the right arm's savings vein is valuable for all liver diseases, and this is the method:
estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie;	Press the arm and apply hot cupping, until the vein is full, if you see it.
et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien;	and if the vein runs transversely (crosswise), and you apply cupping all over it, there will be no harm.
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char,	And do not go too deep, for the nerves are all exposed bare beneath.
et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	Then place the hand in hot water, if it freezes in the wound and cannot come out.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have drained the blood as necessary, place oil and linen over the vein to heal it quickly, and do the same for each wound.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The purgation of pus from the hand on the left side has the same effect as the disease of the mice, and do it exactly as I told you regarding the right side.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors,	The purge of the spine has the same effect for all the diseases that are beneath the chest,
si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	as the disease of marriage (syphilis), retention of urine, sciatica, and diseases of the thighs and old legs, and similar diseases.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere,	And the quality of its purge is that the patient should put their foot in hot water and rub on the vein until it perishes,
et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains;	And lay [something] above the joint of the foot; and if the vein is at the ankle, and above the foot it goes much [further].
saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	Cut it then along a healthy artery or one that is larger at the ankle, as it has more value.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you cut above the foot, beware of nerves that are below, and cut through it as when sharpening; let the flames be annihilated.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if the bone cannot come out, put the foot in water and let the vein drain well.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz;	And if the blisters need to be lanced for the first time, start the second one a little above, because the skin is salted.
ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	Do not doubt the nerve, as we have said, and do the same with the saphena of the other side equally.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The skin of the sciatic vein is at the ankle joint, and its lancing is worth pain relief from the hamstring, when it's for hot blood.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville .iiij. dois en tordant,	And the qualities of his health are such that the patient bathes or immerses and stretches the leg above the ankle four times in twisting.
car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant;	for otherwise the vein does not open; and if it opens, heal it in all ways that you can, and by crossing.
et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	it is better that you crush it, for the wound is hollow and it responds well to human hands.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners;	And if you do not pierce it, there is no healing for the pain in the hip or back, and towards the small of the back, keep away from nerves;
et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	Then make such a cut to let the blood out as you see fit, then unbind the ligament and place cotton on it and bind it; it is now healed.
Des sainies de ventouse	Wounds caused by cupping
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc .ij. manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Cupping glasses are made of horn, or bone, or glass; and cupping is done in two ways: either by cutting and drawing blood, or without cutting.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu;	And this cauterization, which is to wound, has two ways: either it is with all fire, or without fire;
et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en .xiiij. leus dou cors,	and this cauterization that is made by wounding and extraction of blood is done in twelve parts of the body,
de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col;	because one is entirely in the head, and others are in the neck;
et .ij. autres en .ij. costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton;	and two others on each side of the neck; and the cauterization under the chin;
et li ventouse des .ij. espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies;	And the boils on both shoulders; and the boils on the knees;
et les ventouses emmi les .ij. bras; et les ventouses des .ij. jambes;	And the boils on both arms; and the boils on both legs;
et les ventouses des .ij. chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char,	and the boils on both ankles; and the ventosation does not treat blood, but only small veins that are scattered in the flesh,
et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne;	and for this reason, it should not be avoided at all, as is done with blood-letting from the vein;
et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	And it should not be administered at all; neither with fire nor hot fire, in any disease arising from congestion, until the entire body is emptied.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens;	If it is necessary for diseases to ventose (use cupping glass), or by habit, then we shall administer it every hour at the beginning of the month, or at the end, and in the middle and each time.
car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief;	because there are some who, when they need to ventose, have a heavy head;
et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz;	And for those who find swelling and redness in their body, in their head, and at the neck, and darkness of the eyes:
et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc;	And for those who find a pool of blood in their mouth, with their tongue swollen and bleeding:
et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	And if there are such people who think, see black bile and have fevers and similar symptoms:
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés .iij. houres dou jor.	And when we observe these signs, especially during the month, we command them to be bled after four hours of the day:
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors;	The purgation of the mouth helps with the swelling of the head ... that comes to the eyes, and it should not be after the evacuation of all the body;
et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique,	and this ventilation is in place of the purgation of the headache,
et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement;	and it should not be used by those with cold complexion or who have constipation, for it causes them great harm;
et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	and it should also not be used by the watchmen, nor those with cold head diseases.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And he who recovers often becomes oblivious, and therefore it is necessary to place the cupping glass a little lower due to the fear of forgetting.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis,	The cupping at the neck is in place for healing the head and basilica, and therefore it is beneficial for the fracture.
et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion;	and to split the channel of the arm, and immediately, and to fill it up.
et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	And it must be pushed gently, for if it holds too tightly, it induces forgetfulness or stomach and heart trouble.
Li ventosations as .ij. costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens,	The ventosations at the 2 costal bones of the neck are worth the pains in the head, and migraines, and strangulations, and the pain in the roots of the teeth,
et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	and is in the position of the artery in the basilica; and you must instruct the lord to press his hand when inserting it, not to touch the artery, and not let there be any bleeding.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des .ij. levres.	Ventosations below the chin are worth oral disease and tooth decay, and similar illnesses in the mouth; and they are found near the arteries of the 2 lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	The dislocations of the shoulders are harmful to the patient who comes from heat and fullness.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des .iij. voinnes dou bras,	The dislocations of the ribs are as bad as four veins in the arm.
car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes;	because it draws blood from these large veins;
et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	and command the Lord not to be too deep, for the flesh is bare and knows beneath black and arteries.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The swelling that is on the rump is useful for drawing out the hemorrhoids from their foundation and diseases beneath, and it should be large and made of a linen cloth that needs to be well pulled; and by chance, if it is too thin, it will break; and this causes large wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des .ij. sophenes, et des .ij. chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	The swellings of the legs open widely, as they draw blood from all over the body, and are useful for ancient pain in the loins, the back, and the bladder, and remove flowers; and they are located at the elbows and knees, but weaken the body after long use, and bring pus in various dispositions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The method of placing the swelling is that you place it first empty, and squeeze gently and quickly, and move it evenly, and do not stop until you see the location becoming red and swollen, and the blood appearing red; then press firmly, and remove the swellings, and take care in the disposition of the body, as there are some who have tender skin and clear pores: it is necessary to make a single incision, and to make large and deep wounds, and a little shallowly.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir .ij. fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if the wound is large, it should be cut twice: the first time to make a way for thick blood.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if the wound is very deep, it should be cut three times; and when we want to draw out little by little blood drops, we only have to prick once.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement,	If we want a lot of blood, we encourage it to flow more frequently; and if the wound is deep, we should make an incision all the way through, and when we pierce the heart, it should be done quickly.
et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif:	And for those with thick and hard skin, and narrow pores, you should anoint the joints of the affected areas with penetrating and soluble oil.
se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite;	If it is oil of violets, sweet almond oil, or oil of the seeds of pumpkin,
et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	and if it is vinegar, oil of watercress, lily oil, chamomile oil, or similar.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the excess is large and cold, take oil of amatina, or balm oil, or anise oil, and similar ones.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile,	If the person to be treated has tender flesh and large pores, it is not necessary to use oil,
mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	But it is necessary to wash after the dislocation with rose water, or cold water, or water of marshmallow, or water of gourd, or water of porcelain, or another similar substance.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And if the patient has much moisture, he should rise from ashes of nettles, or marsh water, and sumac, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans;	And those with large excesses should rise from old wine, or water of vinegar, or a decoction of dais or chamomile, or similar things.
et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou .ij.; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion,	And it is not advisable to apply a cupping glass before bathing or in the bath, but after the bath for an hour or two; and do not sleep after cupping.
et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	And it is necessary that he wash, when he should be cupped and when he has been cupped.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez;	And guard the one who is cupping (the patient) is bilious, and him without is too sharp and inflamed;
si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses;	it is necessary that he take cool things, such as pomegranates and endives and lettuce leaves, etc.;
et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	And cooked peas, meat broth, and moist meats.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons;	And he who has a cold constitution, let him take honey syrup and fragrant diluted wine, which is between old and new, and eat peas, cabbage, and small birds and pigeons;
et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier;	and on the day he will purge himself, he should drink more than eat;
et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz;	It is necessary to give certain men sometimes triacle or muscatel before purge, or afterwards, to strengthen the main limbs;
et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	And let the wine be made subtle, but it is not suitable for those who drink hot liquids.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz,	The blisters placed on wounds are those placed on the liver, spleen, gout, belly, buttock, and thighs, for these members cannot bear to be wounded under the blisters.
et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre,	and it should not be done to draw blood from one member to another,
si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus lou ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre;	As we place the bandages on the limbs when they swell; to remove the viscosity from the member, as we apply leeches on the belly and on the buttocks to reduce it.
et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu;	and remove the pain when there is an abscess or arrow, remove it by attracting its position through its virtue accidentally or dislodge the arrow from its place.
et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue,	and in this way, it is done when it is placed on the liver and spleen when there is retained windiness,
et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede,	And these blisters are applied empty to be sucked only; and sometimes they are applied along with fire, and sometimes filled with cold water.
si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	as in diseases of the lungs, and in such manner one fills the bladder with hot water or water in which cooked herbs suitable for this purpose have been steeped.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The form of the bladder applied to fire is as follows:
Et ait .ij. dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu .i. petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille,	And it should have two holes of about half a palm's width and depth, and it should have one small hole around the middle, just like pushing an awl.
et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre;	and made of iron, soft before so that it does not burn the patient when placed on the member;
et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise,	and have a rod of iron or steel through its middle to insert a handle.
et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent;	and be large and small according to the diseases and age of those who take them.
car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	For the boils of children are different from those of adults, and thin ones from fat ones.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre:	And this boil should be placed upon the member thusly:
empren la chandoile de cire ou .i. linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse,	Take the beeswax candle or linen thread and insert it through the boil to the member beneath it,
si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide;	so that the light is inside the boil so as not to burn the patient;
et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse;	And then place it on the limb, and your fingers should be above the opening that we have mentioned, so when one wants to see, if steam is coming out, remove the blister.
et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	Wrap it in linen thread as previously described, and repeat the process often if necessary.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement;	In the blister that is administered in case of pleurisy, it should not have a hole or opening, and it should only be applied when it is full of liquid.
et c’est li forme:	And this is its shape: [In this context, 'it' refers to the dislocation mentioned earlier]
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus;	Sinews are not tied up unless in members where no bandages can be applied due to their small size, such as lips and gums, and similar places.
et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans;	and in naked flesh areas, such as the elbow or ankle, and other similar locations;
et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren;	and the quality of the user is that when you find sinews in clear, clean waters, without any pollution, you should take them.
et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres;	And put them in a warm mild broth until they are tender and have nothing in their stomachs;
et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues;	Then let it be drained of blood and pus, then rub the limb until it is red, and apply sulphur;
et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	And when they swell up and become hot, if it is a place where a poultice can be applied, apply one, for it is very beneficial;
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint;	If it is not so, lift the joint gently, then with water, very well, and then press on it.
et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille .i. drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés;	And if the joint becomes too much swollen after the body, moisten a linen cloth with cold water and put it on until the swelling subsides.
et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez;	And if the swelling is increased, apply powdered vitriol or other similar things until it subsides.
ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant;	or place half-peeled beans on the joint and leave them until they harden onto the joint, which will cause it to subside now.
et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	And if you need more lances (or instruments), take others as well.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse,	And if the instruments are not to be taken, rub fresh blood on the place, and insert a needle until it comes out.
et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent;	Then, lay them down and as soon as they feel the blood, they heal themselves.
et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	And when you see that they are dripping, sprinkle a little of powdered aloe and crushed seeds, or ash on them, they will now stop.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	Here comes the book of breaks (or fractures)
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine and it is about restoration of a break and dislocation.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent;	Instruct the dear son that the foolish man should abandon this chapter, as he will never see any old books or read letters from them.
et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin;	And because of this, knowledge in our land is strange, as I have never found anyone good at it.
et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie;	And I know nothing about it, except for the knowledge from old books, which I have studied extensively and applied through experience, and by the habit of my life.
et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces .ij. chapistres ci devant.	and I have described it in this chapter what is contained, and I have summarized it at the end, and shown clearly the forms of the instruments that are brought in, as I have done in these two chapters before.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	Therefore, it is necessary that we say the prologue of this book, the sum of the word and the chapters where the wise put their understanding, and remain on truth, so that those who are experienced know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars;	When fracture or dislocation or twisting or distortion comes to anyone, it is necessary that you treat the patient from both sides, unless something prevents you, such as frailty of body, infancy, or old age.
ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	or if the time is not very hot or too cold; and avoid cold foods, that is to say cold meats, and chicken and beef, and do not drink wine, nor consume any fatty meats, and do not overfill yourself with foods that fill the veins with blood, until you have doubt of abscess heat or spreading of matter in the member; then the patient will recover again under his first regular government as he has used it.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bones begin to heal, it is necessary to feed the patient with thick foods that make large stools, or he must have viscosity, as cooked wheat in water and peas, and meats like beef, pork, mutton, veal, fish, eggs, fresh fish, strong wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For this thick feeding speeds up the healing of the bones.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans;	Know that the broken bones of the old and weak cannot be well healed or mended according to their nature due to the weakness of the members, nor those that are too tender, such as the bones of small children.
mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet .i. gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	But has no cure, reset above the broken bone, i.e., large tendons that straighten and join the limb together, until it heals as it was before; and not to touch it at all, and for this reason, it is necessary to feed it with large meats, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that the fractures are diverse in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the fracture of the head is other than the fracture of the foot or leg, and I will tell you in this chapter all ways of fractures.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For it is a fracture that grows toward the ear, and another one lengthens like the quill of a pen for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And there is also a fracture with an open wound, and a fracture with a small crack.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu;	And each kind has its tool, and appropriate device for restoration, as memory recalls in its place;
et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main;	And it is known as the break of the bone when the joint is twisted, and wide open by displacement, and sounds under pressure from the hand;
et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure;	And when there is no twisting or touching, and the patient does not feel great pain, then there is no break.
mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	But it can have a twist, a fracture, or a small break.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	Do not move the hand, but place the remedies that come after here, and then gently hold it now.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les .ij. parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne;	And know that the fractures going to the branch, and are the two parts disjoined, it is necessary now to set them equally aligned, so that abscesses grow not there.
et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez;	and if abscesses come there, let it be left for any day, until the abscess is calmed.
puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	then set it equal to the muscle that you can easily and wisely move, and know that the restoration of it is easier than the restoration where there are fragments; then tighten, as necessary hereafter.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de .ij. pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a .ij. cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main;	And if in the bone there are broken pieces, if it is less than two parts, whether it is hand or foot, or with your hand if it is one of the small members, or if it is two ropes, or one rope and your hand;
et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor;	align the limb according to its natural shape, so that when the parts of the member are dislocated they are realigned with all means available, and ensure that through your work there is no injury or pain for the patient.
et ajoste bien les .ij. chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	and adjust well the two bones according to the best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And it feels well to the touch if it seems not good: straighten it nicely, and do not strain it too much, nor press as those who bring it by their work abscesses hot and contractions to the member, as we have seen many times.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere;	And when the limb is healed, correct the patient so that they do not move it, neither by watching nor sleeping, nor turning, nor in any other way;
et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	and watch carefully that the limb is so secure that it feels no pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor;	For when it feels no pain, it is not broken, and it must be set in such a way that it feels no pain.
et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez;	and keep it straight so that crookedness does not come when it is restored;
et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	and the quality of the broken limb is as I tell you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	Know that broken limbs are various in smallness, great size, and form.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz;	For there are small members, such as arms and fingers, etc.: it is necessary to wrap linen cloths soft and fine.
et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche;	and those that are thick, such as thighs and legs: it is necessary to wrap with a large and hard rope, because the large ropes embrace the whole large member evenly, and they press from all sides equally, so there is no bruise.
puis lie entor estoupes legieres, .iij. tours ou iiij. selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure;	then tie light tourniquets around it, three or four turns according to the member, and hold your hand a little on the rope, then go above the break and tighten less than the break, then move away from the break.
et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren .i. autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet;	And soften the ligament little by little, until you take a large part of the healthy joint, then take another ligament and turn it around reversely over the broken joint.
puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus;	Then return to the part below the break and hold it moderately, not too hard nor too loosely, as we have said in the first place above.
puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus .i. bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	Then place padding of linen or fabric between the ligaments until they are all even, then tie it all up with a bandage, and then place your well-made splints on top if there is no abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors;	And if there is swelling or abscess, put on top something soothing for the abscess and one who extracts the swelling, and leave it like that for some days.
puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	then hold your elbows, and they should be the thickness of half a thick cane, well-healed, or of a staff that is used to split logs, or of palm reeds, and should be shaped like this:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres;	but it is necessary that the elbow one puts on the fracture should be a little larger and wider than the others;
et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor;	And let it be as long as required for the limb, whether large or small.
puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure;	then hold it steady on the stirrups as you did at the first joint, then tie it above with a thread coming along, just like in the first joint when breaking it.
plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol;	The following is narrower, shorter now; and the thread should be medium-sized, not too thick nor too thin, and made of soft linen.
car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	because if the thread is thick, as I have seen in the work of fools who make their ropes with twisted linen threads, and this is a great error, for the rope cannot be even if it is too thin; and it should not have less than two fingers' space between each stirrup.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is wounded by the heads of arrows after setting in healthy bones, place linen or cloth bandages under them so that they do not become inflamed.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is with a break and the veins are severed, I will tell you the cure below.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that it is not appropriate to set arrows in broken limbs on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés .v. jors ou .vij., ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant;	For when the limbs are large, there should be no need to apply hot irons before 5 or 7 days, or more, according to your certainty of the abscess healing process.
et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	And here is the method of ancient plasters for restoring fractures, dislocations, and twists: you should take flour that is kept in the mill walls, mix it with an abundance of egg, and apply this mixture, neither too thick nor too thin, and use it, and this is the common method of a plaster for restoring a fracture in various positions, and equally for women and small children, as it is not too hot or too cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .v. З.; alechil .viiij. З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another method of plaster for restoring fractures, dislocations, and twists: take barberries, dandelion leaves, nettles, tansy, and Arabic gum, in equal amounts; myrrh and aloeswood, 5 parts; alchemil, 8 parts; and make powder of these ingredients, mix them with an abundance of egg; if the complexion of the person is hot, use this plaster as it has a good composition and quickly restores broken bones for many men.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .viiij. З.; acaice vi. З.; bolic armenic .x. З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Another method of plaster that is beneficial for twisting: take mugat and vismalve, mix together 10 times its volume; add mirrhe and aloes, 8 times its volume; acaice 6 times its volume; bolic armenic 10 times its volume, grind well, and concoct with vinegar or abundant egg, and administer it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu. Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	Another method of plaster for joints and dislocated bones, to relieve the pain arising from them, and for treating wounds: take new linen, wet it in vinegar and cooked oil, and apply it on the area. This plaster does not restore [the bones], but it is good for soothing a hot abscess and proper wound pain.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another method of plaster that mends broken bones: take dried fig leaves and earth-purslane leaves, grind together, and make a plaster.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme. Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Another method of plaster for the restoration of bone fracture and to hasten the healing of an abscess. Take root of comfrey, chamomile, flowers of violets, flour of peas, of each one part; grind and mix with wine, and if the limb is scalded, mix with moist coriander juice or water, and use it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre. Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Another method of plaster more forceful than the first, when a hard abscess comes to the restoration of the limb. Take roots of comfrey, flax seed, balm, lentil, and sage, flowers of violets and chamomile, of all one part; grind and make with salty water, sweet water, or with wine, according to the heat of the limb, and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Hippocrates said in his book that no other plaster should be placed on a broken limb for restoration except beeswax and oil, and nothing else, and he said it should be between soft and hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems Galenic that one should place hot and slightly warm dry things on the broken limb, to restore it, such as myrrh, aloeswood, incense, and similar things, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another way of poultice that is good for wounds and pain: take ground mugwort and human hair shavings, or bird feathers, and yarrow, equal amounts, grind them up, and make a poultice from it and apply to the affected area.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors	Then wait a little after that, and take care to ensure the patient feels no pain, or the bone has not moved from its place; do not dislocate it by hand for many days.
Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor;	And if pain or itching comes at the joint, without rest or swelling, hurry up, dislocate it, and remove the emplastrum (medication) immediately; then take a light cloth, a sea sponge moistened, dip it in water, and lift up the joint, until the itching stops, and the pain is soothed.
puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut;	Then let the limb rest for an hour, then put on dry linen moistened with water or rose oil, and tie it up with a bandage, until you are sure of the abscess heating.
et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	and let the inflammation of the limb rest, and remove the pain, then continue the binding gently, and a little emplastrum, and do not strain it too much as before; and bind it until it is healed.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that an abscess swells and reddens and hurts and inflames are entirely opened up, and you need to plug and bind it, proceed as you did equally before.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés .iij. jors ou .iiij. ou .v. ou .vij.; et aucune fois le laisse .xx. jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus;	And if no blood comes from the limb as we have said, do not unbind it before 3 or 4 or 5 or 7 days; and sometimes leave it for 20 days, according to what one sees, until the break heals, and bring the wound close to the skin above.
adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir;	Then you bind it more tightly than before, and let the meat swell, as I have said before; and if you see the wound dry out more than necessary, know that pus cannot come in.
arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure;	Arises then from hot, warm water, always when you dislocate it, and this should be done every third day, and apply a little cold on the joint.
par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	By this work, then cut the nerves in the limb, and correct immediately what the foolish surgeon does, who keeps the member twisted: this is harmful, and it is dangerous work, and I see nothing else but to tire oneself and to work correctly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	Of various ways of breaking
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees;	Many ways of fractures are, and various shapes, and the causes are intended.
car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	fractures are made by sword percussion, and the bones are broken all the way to the shaft that is beneath the bone, as it happens with hacks or thrusts; this type of fracture is called "hackure".
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces .ij. brisures grans ou petite.	When the sword strikes the bone from above, causing it to pierce, this type of fracture is called "absolute"; and these are either large or small breaks in the bone.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is a blow embedded, or wound, or cuts from arrows, or falling on stones, or similar things.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is a persistent breakthrough to the membrane beneath the bone, which protrudes above or below the bone, and this wound is large or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»;	And if there is a wound that penetrates into the bone as fine as a hair, and it is a small tear, and for this reason it is called "hairline fracture".
et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	And if the wound is made by striking with stones or falling, or similar things, and makes the bone piece to enter within, and the limb becomes swollen like a baker when he puts it in the oven; if the stone enters within.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant;	And this happens more often to those who have moist bones, such as a child's head;
et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	and in all these ways of fracture, small pieces are dislodged as well; and I will speak about it specifically.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	We should be familiar with all ways of fractures by the dissection above them, and the investigation at attempts, and by the corrupt flesh that is upon it.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The hairy appearance is known to those who, when the bone has been exposed and scraped on top, if the fracture is black it appears open.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of fracture, take care of the patient's condition, and if you see any harmful symptom such as vomiting of blood, loss of consciousness, swelling, fever ague, hairs falling out and reddening, or other similar signs in various conditions, it cannot heal without doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see any doubtful symptom, and you hope for recovery, then begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the wound first comes to you during winter, it is necessary to remove the bone before the 14th day at the muscle that you can reach.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if this is the case, hasten to remove the bone before the seventh day, so that the tissue beneath the bone is not corrupted, and the event that we have mentioned occurs.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues,	And if the bone fracture reaches the tissue that covers the brain, you must cut the broken part in such a way: and it is that you take hold of the patient's head, and expose above the bone in all ways as you can, and over the figure of the wound more gently than you can,
et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset;	and if the flow of blood or an abscess occurs when exposing the bone, use what is appropriate, and it is that you fill the cavity with damp cloths soaked in rose oil;
et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc .ij. manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	And let the wound rest until the abscess subsides and ensure the flow of blood has stopped; then start to remove the bone around it. This is done in two ways of treatment: one method is that you cut at a narrow incision before, and this is the shape:
Et puis i boute .i. autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then make another incision larger than the first.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	The second method is that you have several incisions of various sizes, some narrow and others wide, sharp, and made with iron tools; and work lightly to avoid piercing the bone.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou .i. cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des .iij. manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is displaced and hard, then you must pierce it around, so as to administer splints with splints, not allowing them to penetrate beyond the bone's surface, and there should be a margin or circle above its point, which prevents the splint from passing beyond the bone; and you must have more than one, such that each comes in its place at the bone's edge, so that you have splints for all sides; and this is the form of the four kinds of splints:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes .i. tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The quality for piercing around the broken bone is that you place one splint on the bone, and turn your hand until you feel that the bone is perforated; then replace the splint elsewhere a little later, and do this all around, then cut the space of the bone between the fracture pieces as finely and gently as possible, and do so as we have said, pulling the bone to your hand or any other tool such as pliers, forceps; and ensure that you do not touch the brain nor the nerves.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout .i. autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire;	And when you have perforated and treated the bone, it is necessary that you reset the sharpness which remains in the bone with any other tool resembling an incision blade, but it must be thinner and finer than the other blades.
et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a .i. des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.
