And if there remains something of small bones, no scales, lightly remove them with instruments; then treat the wound with bandages and ointments as we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And another method of work, which is more secure, is that which the Greeks called, and it is highly praised, and this is his word.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	First, you must uncover a part of the bone where the fracture is open so that when you have uncovered this part, you will place the lenticular anvil under it as shown in its form:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en .ij. costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz;	And do not cut from only one side, and the part is hollow on two sides, so that the cutting is towards the bone; then strike with a small hammer on it, so that you gently break the bone all around, and take great care of the cloth that is underneath;
s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	If it is adhered to the bone, gently split it, because one can easily harm it and cause fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	If the bone does not break through to the cloth and it is cut only from above, making small pieces, then you should scrape it roughness, remove scales with a sharp rasp and different quantities, depending on the work and shape of the fracture.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If the king shaves with great razors, and afterwards with more subtle ones, and does not stop until it is well done.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In other hair cuts and breaks of subtle shape, it is necessary that you bring the cause according to his discretion; and this is not something that can be replied to by one who has put his study into this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes .i. drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie;	And if the sore is exposed, it is necessary that you take one linen cloth, according to the quantity of the wound, and wet it in rose oil, and place it on the wound;
puis pren .i. autre drapeil doublé en .ij. ou en .iij., et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus .i. autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement;	then take another cloth doubled in 2 or 4 layers, and wet it in wine and rose oil, and place it on the first cloth; and do this more lightly than you can, so as not to burden the sore, then administer another linen, but do not strain it any further than covering the wound only;
et le laisse ensi .i. jor ou .ij., tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication;	And leave it for a day or two until the abscesses calm down, then cut it open and administer the following medications like root of lily, flour of wheat, incense powder, aristolochia, and similar things; make powder from these items and sprinkle on the wound, and immediately provide reliable medicines without bitterness.
et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	Ensure that the wound is always kept clean, you must not leave ointment or pus on it, nor let scabs form on the brain tissue, because when scabs form on the cloth, they rot and can cause great harm to the patient; because when something bitter is applied to it, it causes pain.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Therefore, be cautious in case any bad accident happens to the patient as we have said, it is doubtful and full of uncertainty.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et .iij. parties d’oile roset et en glue .i. drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac;	And if blackness does not come violently except by the medicine that has been applied, then you should take a part of honey and 3 parts of rose oil and 1 piece of linen cloth and mix them together and apply it on the affected area.
puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then heal in the manner of treatments that are required, until it heals.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les .ij. parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont .ij. os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	Know that sometimes the two parts of the nose above are broken, or one of them alone because there are two bones; and the one below is cartilaginous and does not break, but only bows or twists, and then heals.
Et se l’une des .ij. parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil;	And if one of the two parts is broken, it must be that you insert your little finger or thumb into the neck, and place the break inside the index finger, and in the hollow by the side, until the neck returns according to its natural figure.
et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	And do this gently, and be careful that the patient does not feel pain from your work.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the break is in the part above the neck and the finger cannot reach the place, then you must put a small splint on the head of the finger.
Et se li brisure est de .ij. pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues;	And if the fracture is in two parts, you must set it again, and hasten to restore it as soon as possible.
se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	If not, after the seventh or tenth day, when the abscess has calmed down, then you bind to the head of the nose pieces of linen cloth, if the fracture is in one part.
Ou tu boutes .i. autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	Or you bind another on the other side, if there is a fracture there; and let the pieces be as thick as they fill the nostrils of the nose.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor. Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	And they said that one should moisten the pieces in butter and soften them each day. I do not think it is good, but they must be moistened with a mixture of egg white and flour; then leave the piece until the bone is hard, and the cartilage is hardened.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a .i. souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	And at times, feathers of geese are inserted instead of thorns, and if a single piece of soft linen is wrapped around it, and the breakage is held, then blow into the patient's nostrils; do as you see fit.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en .i. poc de dyaquilon.	If an abscess opens during the incision while you are working on it, put cotton wool soaked in rose oil or a little piece of onion there.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis;	If an abscess does not open, apply a plaster from the inside, made of wheat flour and incense powder mixed with egg white, then put light compresses on top, but do not tie it shut.
et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu;	And if the break of the neck is small and it breaks into small pieces, then take appropriate instruments to extract it, then make an incision, and apply things that promote healing such as char, suture, plasters, and ointments suitable for this purpose.
et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if there is no wound inside the neck, then heal it with bandages and place wooden splints on it until it is healed.
de la routure de la mandibule	of the fracture of the jawbone
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jawbone is dislocated beneath and there is no wound outside, and the fracture is only displaced, but not broken in two, if one recognizes it easily, then it is corbeled within.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	If the fracture is on the right side, you must insert your index finger in the patient's mouth; if it is on the left jawbone, insert the index finger of your right hand and press gently into the fracture, then align it by pushing from the outside with your other hand.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en .ij., si covient que tu aministres extension de .ij. pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the fracture of the jawbone is displaced in two parts, then you must administer extension of two parts, until they are equal.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus .i. drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And if there is movement of the teeth or fracture, hold them with a thread of gold or silver or silk, then place on it a broken mandible splint, and place on it one double cloth; and place upon the cloth a large and well-made plaster, or an equal piece of skin, long and wide according to the mandible, and attach it to the jaw as you can, and command the patient to rest, and provide light foods.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en .iij. semainnes.	And if you see that the figure changes, dislocate it on the third day, and then reset what has changed; place plaster upon it, with milled powder mixed with egg or flour of wheat after removing the splint; and place upon the plaster a light linen, and if the plaster sticks to him, and the condition of the patient does not change, leave it until it is healed; many times it heals within four weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if abscesses come up, bring what we have said previously.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if there is a fracture and wound together, carefully remove no piece of the bone; if it can be removed with delicate tools appropriate for this purpose.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, stretch it with fire as needed.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus .i. des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have removed all these pieces and it does not dislocate anymore, if the wound is wide, stitch it up with one layer of appropriate dressing to promote healing until it is healed.
de la forcele	from the forceps (a medical instrument)
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc .iij. manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en .ij., et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	The forceps breaks frequently in front of the shoulder, and the breakage occurs in three ways: either it is broken and dislocated in two places and divided into several pieces, being the easiest to restore; or there is a break with an open wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies .ij. ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	And the procedure is when the breakage has an open wound, that you have two assistants, one to hold the shoulder where the forceps are broken; and the other to extend the neck towards the affected part; then adjust the dislocation with your hands so that the form is as it should be, having no appearance or displacement.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And if you need to extend it more, place a round cushion of cloth or linen on the patient's shoulder, and make it large according to your needs; stretch and lift the forceps, and hold the cushion with your hand so that you adjust the dislocation as needed.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule .i. oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot draw the head of the shoulder outwards because it comes in fully, then the patient must lie on his affected side, and place one small pillow under the shoulder, and push the assistant's hand downward on the shoulder until the bone of the joint is raised.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	Then direct the fracture to your fingers, and if you find debris, then it is necessary that you cut above it; and draw out the pieces gently, and if the bone cannot join due to any obstruction, strike it at one of the incisions that you have made; but place this instrument under the joint to prevent it from dislocating:
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait .ij. chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os;	and is shaped like a spoon, but not concave, and should be as wide as necessary, according to the size of the bone and the strength of the work; and it should have two prongs, as you see, and one should be wide, and the other narrow, just as the opening of the wound that you made when treating the bones:
et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	And when you are sure of the abscess being hot, if it opens and the wound is small, or you doubt that the abscess is hot, then apply bandages and lint to the wound, according to its size.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille .i. drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if it is a hot abscess that comes, wet a linen cloth with rose oil, asafetida, and wine and place on top.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier;	The bone compression when there are wounds or cuts is to place a plaster of flour and egg powder on the bone, put light packs on top, and put a spear beneath if necessary.
puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met .i. drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de .iij. dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant;	Then take a very large bandage, one palm wide, then put a double cloth damp on it and wrap it up; then take a subtle awl three fingers wide and long, and wrap it around the bandage so that the head of the bandage hangs down.
et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint;	and place the awl on the break, turn the bandage around the neck, and under the skin of the healthy person and the sick person, and pull from each side, and when you see that the sutures hold the bandage in place, and you see clearly that the awl does not move above the broken bone, keep it in place every day, and when the threads loosen, tighten them.
et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort .i. petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a .xx. jors;	and make the patient lie on his back, and put a small pillow under his armpit to lift the shoulder up; align the break with the forceps by adjusting the shoulder, or tie the arm to the neck, and do not untie it unless a bad accident occurs, for up to 20 days.
puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en .xxviij. jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	Then repeat the application of pressure, if necessary, and hold it and leave it in that state until it is restored; and it is restored in most cases within 28 days, and less in some men.
de la brisure de l’espaule	for the break of the shoulder
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus .i. drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en .xx. jors ou en xxv,  Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	It happens that the broken or dislocated shoulder does not heal on its own and needs to be forced back into place; it should be aligned according to the figure of the dislocation, and reset according to its natural shape in all possible ways; then put powder from a mill with abundant egg white and fine starch, and cover it with two layers of cloth; then put a wide and thin splint, a little larger than the shoulder, on top, and if there is any hollow in the shoulder under the splint, use lin starch to fill it so that the splint fits evenly; and then firmly bind it all in one strong bandage so that the splint does not move from its place, and observe the bandage every day; whenever it softens, bind it again, and if the splint moves out of place, adjust it and lie the patient on his side; and the shoulder will be restored in 20 or 25 days. And when this number is completed, unbind it, and be careful, for it is not a bone that becomes loose easily.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a bone fragment protrudes in front, and not beneath the skin, lift it up, and the bone, and do as we have said in the treatment of an abscess to calm it with hot cautery.
de la brisure dou pis	of the fracture on the thigh
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer. Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	The thigh bone is sometimes fractured in the middle, but it happens seldom; but it often breaks at the end. And when it is fractured obliquely, it falls below, and the patient feels great pain, and lack of strength, and immediately vomits blood, and the openings in the broken bones become apparent, and the joint feels cold.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met .i. cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des .ij. costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en .i. drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is such that the patient lies on his back with one cushion between the shoulders, then presses the shoulders and assembles the ribs of the two sides to your hands, very carefully making it equal in all ways as you can, until the figure of the bone is as it should be; then place plasters and bandages made of thin fabric over the broken bone, or something light, and wrap it in one cloth, and tie it to the broken bone so that it does not move; turn the arm round several times, and tighten the bandage gradually, and check each hour whether it is healing, if it softens, tighten it again; and if it needs to be released due to corruption or itching at the site, or pain or abscess, hurry, release it, remove the plaster, and direct those who came to treat it in a healing manner; then bandage the plaster again, and tighten it until it is healed.
de la brisure des costes	of the broken ribs
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	It is known that the fracture of the ribs occurs only in large ones after the back, and in the chest within, and they do not pierce except because they are slippery; and one can feel this easily at the investigation of the joints.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient. Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	And the restoration is that you set it equally, as required. Then put the splint, and hold it with a stick, if necessary.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile; et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	If the fracture of the ribs is concave within, it causes the patient great pain and shortness of breath, as if from pleurisy, for the bone pierces the membrane; it points to the ends, and immediately vomits a large quantity of blood, which is a serious illness, and the ancients used great devices.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And if there are those who say that it is necessary to administer foods that swell the belly, to push the fracture outwards.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We should not cause abscesses to become hot unless they have come.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	If it has come, let it heal.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	And they said that anyone who puts leeches on the wound to drain it is reasonable; however, there is doubt whether the leeches attract waste to the wound due to their weak positioning.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And they said that one should cover the wound with damp linen soaked in hot oil and put towels between the ribs to make the wound even, then it should be cured by sweating, meat, and medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz .i. estrument por warder lou syfac; et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les .ij. levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez. Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu; et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the patient feels intense pain that it cannot be endured due to the broken bone, and there is fear in the patient, then it is necessary to make an incision above the broken rib, and it is necessary to put one instrument underneath for support; and then it must be cut, drawn lightly, and then sew the two edges of the wound, if they are large, and heal with plasters until it heals. And when abscesses come, place damp cloths soaked in rose oil on top, and on the broken rib; and heal the broken rib as needed, and lie still on the affected side until it is healed.
de la brisure dou col	of the break of the collarbone
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	Occasionally comes a break in the collarbone or spine. And similarly...
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent. Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	And when this happens to anyone, and you wish to know if he will be well or not, take notice if his hands are softened, swollen, and dead, and cannot move nor stretch, and when you prick them with a needle, he does not feel it. Know that he is mortal in many positions, and if they become mute and feel well when squeezed and pricked, know that the jointure of the bone is saved, and that the patient will be cured, if there is treatment applied.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit; et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit. Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet. Saiches qu’il est mortelz: si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	And when similar happens to the spine in the back, and you wish to know if it will be well or not, take notice if the feet are softened, and the symptoms are in the hands, and the vertebrae jump spontaneously and movement is against his will; and when it is soothed on his belly, it jumps again against his will. And when it is soothed on his back and he wishes to rest, he cannot. Know that it is mortal: do not labor at its cure.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if this accident does not come upon him, it is a lighter thing.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez; puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer; et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	And the cure is that you reward him if there is an abscess heated, put oil of roses or egg yolk oil on it until it is soothed; then put on one of the drying and comforting ointments, and tie it with a thread, and command the patient to rest; and let him not sleep on that part where he feels pain, as long as he is well.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur; et oste l’os, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier; puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If any bone dislocates, it is necessary to cover it; then remove the bone, and close the wound with two stitches if it is large, using a bandage; then treat the wound with an aromatic healing balm until it heals; and if the head of the bone is broken, which is called "the head of the cow," push your left thumb into the space between the bones, and make it even with your right hand as much as possible; then apply the ointment and oil, if you have any; then bind it, and if there are bones dislocated, lift them up, remove the bone, and treat the wound until it heals.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	of the break of the shinbone
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief; et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	It often happens that the bone of the hip is broken, and if it occurs, there will be a slight reduction in mobility at the site; and it extends for a long distance, bends towards the front, and causes pain at the location, swelling, and breaks the affected area.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure; et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li; et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	And the restoration is that you extend your hand above [the broken bone], so that you are on top of the breakage; and know what the break and its shape is; and if the break is only at the head, then make the break equal, as it is in its natural shape.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the break is long or it bends inside, make the patient lie on their stomach until the restoration of the break is made clear to you.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve; et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	And when you have set it even, place the splint on top, then place a rod or peg on top of the fracture and hold the break so that it does not move; and apply the position beneath the ribs until the fracture is even.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	Instruct the patient to sleep on his healthy side or back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit; et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident; et c’est li maniere.	If an abscess has erupted, do not touch it until it is quieted, and place on it what we have said before; then return to the treatment, and hold it as necessary, if there is no bad accident; this is the method.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	of the breakage of the shoulder
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des .ij. manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren .i. fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	The shoulder is that which is between the chest and the head of the upper arm, and if it is broken, it should be restored according to one of two ways: the first being that you take a rod filled with thick paste, in this form:
Et lie as .ij. chiés .ij. liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus .i. siege; puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval; puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	And tie the two shoulders with two ropes, and lift them up, and raise the patient on one seat; then let him lower his broken arm over the rod, until it comes to rest, and have a rope attached at its midpoint, then lift it on some heavy thing or the assistants extend it downward; then place the mire (assistant) holding the breakage with both hands together, until the breakage returns as required.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a .ij. ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout .i. liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And another way it is that one restrains the patient on his bed, and ties his hand to his neck, then commands two ministers that one presses where there is a break with his hands, and the others press below all around, extending each one to their part.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint .i. liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part. Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes .i. liien moien desoz l’assele, et .i. autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure; et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre .i. liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute; puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the extraction is more forceful, one tie a cord below the break, and above the break, and each minister extends to their part. If the break is near the shoulder head, it is necessary that you put a medium cord below the shoulder, and another towards the neck, below the break; and in the same way if the break is towards the neck, one should lightly tie a cord, without effort, until the break is even on the level, and on the neck; then make the break even as needed, and tie it, if no abscess comes.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a .vij. jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez; puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein; et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	If abscesses come, do not tighten it for more than 7 days, and put a soft cloth soaked in linen and rose oil on it to calm the abscess; then tighten it, and the method of tightening is that you put a cushion on the break, gather the arm towards the shoulder, and place your hand on the shoulder or chest; and tie the bandage, and tighten on the shoulder and on the arm, so that the arm is in a straight line, if nothing prevents it, or if the bone is not moving.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele .i. doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure .iij. dois de chescune part; puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	And if you doubt that the bone does not move, use splints, and place a larger and stronger splint on the fracture than the others, and have one inch of space between each splint, and let each splint be large enough to pass over the fracture by two inches on each side; then hold the splints in place, as I said at the beginning of the chapter regarding the fracture, more firmly and lessen it in alignment.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit; puis regarde chescuns .iij. jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois. Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	If you see the position of the splints and their binding, as we have said, when restoring the broken limb, and you doubt the abscess is heated, leave it to heal for seven days, as we have said; then observe every three days the binding, to ensure that pus does not swell or come to the place, or the new flesh does not come to the limb because it is too tight. Follow our advice.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés .iij. jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac; et met desoz l’ajutoire .i. cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens; si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz; et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse. Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en .xl. jors dou tout; et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.  Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier .l. jors ou .ij. mois.	If no such accidents occur, do not unbind it before four days or more, and let the patient lie on his back, with his hands on his stomach; and put under the shoulder one compress of equal wool, and observe every hour of the day or night that the shape of the broken limb does not move, or the bindings are not softened; follow our advice by the power of medicine, and give the meat as we have previously specified, in such a way that the meat is first soft; and when it starts to recover, it should be thick. It is customary that the shoulder and leg should be rebound in forty days altogether; then unbind it and administer baths and liniments for the place to heal properly. If the incision is ugly and inflamed, wait to unbind it for one day or two months.
de la brisure du bras	Of the fracture of the arm
Li bras est compos de .ij. os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	The arm consists of two bones, which are called the "ulna" and the "radius"; one is small, that which forms the elbow, and the other is large, that which is beneath, near the little finger; by chance, only one fractures, either the small or the large, or both together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble. Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	When the small ulna is fractured, restoration and healing are easy; but when the large one is fractured, healing is difficult and more painful than when both are fractured together. If it is only the small ulnar bone that is fractured, then you should extend it slightly and align it.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus .i. cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et .i. cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a .i. liien, et uns autres ministres a .i. autre au desus. Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	If it is the large bone that is fractured, then it should be pulled harder; stretch it over one fist, lift the elbow of the hand higher than the others, and the small finger lower than the others, and cross the arms above the patient's chest, with one fist in front of the other, so that the patient does not feel any pain; then extend the assistant's arm to the lower part under the fractured arm, or to the elbow, and another assistant above. Then align the bones as best you can.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if it is broken into pieces, put each one back in its place, and if there is any displaced piece that protrudes, you cannot restore it to its place, then cut off the bone as we have said before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	And if with the breaking into pieces, I have spoken in the individual chapter; take care.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue .i. drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz; et lie .i. drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez. Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres; et saiches que il doit avoir vj. esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions: soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en .ij.; et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre; et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres; et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit. Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And if, at the beginning of the resetting, abscesses arise, apply a cloth made of rosin and white beeswax that is neither too hard nor too soft; and glue one piece of cloth gently over it, until the abscesses are calmed down. Then remove the rosin, and place the plaster made with the powder of the mill with plenty of egg, then put on the splints, and make sure that the splint for the broken part is stronger and a little larger than the others; and be aware that it should have 7 splints or more in various positions: whether the broken part is in one bone, or two; and tighten more above the break than elsewhere, and always less when moving away, as I said at the beginning of the chapter; and let the cloth over the break be soft and moist, and neither too hard nor rough; and let the thread that holds it be made of linen, not too thick or too thin, as we have said. And check the member and the ligament afterwards after some days.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer. Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	If any bad accidents happen to the limb, such as itching that happens to the limb, then you must irrigate the limb with hot water until the itch is soothed; and let the limb not rest. Then begin the treatment again, and if the ligaments are damaged and the bones dislocated, address this similarly.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses .i. poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	If the nails cannot come to the limb because it is too narrow, then you must soften it slightly and wait for some days until the nails grow, and then set it.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a .xx. jors. ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos; et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en .xxx. jors ou en .xxxv., et par aventure en .xx. jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	If none of the things we have said come to the patient, then do not release him until 20 days or more. After that, you can put his hands at his neck and make them even, and watch for movement and dislocation, and let him sleep on his back; know that this break will heal in 30 or 40 days, or perhaps sooner, depending on the compositions and complexions of the properties.
de la brisure de la main	Of the fracture of the hand
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	For at the back of the hand and near the fingers there are few fractures, but it occurs multiple times.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement; puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint; et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu; et soit envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin.	And when the sole of the hand is fractured or dislocated, the patient should lie crosswise, straight and level; then put his hand on a cloth extended, and the attendant should extend the fractured bones and align them with mirrors, until they are well joined; and apply the plaster and padding, if no abscess comes, then put an iron splint according to the size of the place; and it should be wrapped in one linen cloth.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie; et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	And if the fracture is on the sides around the sole of the hand, make a splint of cloth, and instruct the patient to wrap it around his fractured sole; then bind it with a long piece of cloth, and let the iron splint be as large as the sole of the hand, and bind it as necessary.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	And if the break is on the outside (of a limb), it must be that you place a splint above, and another below in the heel, so that the hand is open and straight, then tie it all around the hand, and bind the joint between the fingers.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient; et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve; et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés; ou tu les lie toz en .i. tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet; et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	If the break occurs in any of the fingers (knuckles), it must be made equal as required; and hold with the heel, and if you see that you place a straight splint to lift the break, and do not move it; and if the break is in other fingers like the index or one of the others, make it equal, and tie with the sound finger which is after; or tie them all in one bandage, as needed, or put a splint above, as for a knuckle; and beware in the restoration and placement of abscess heat, and heal what comes there, as I said.
de la cuixe brisie	of the broken shin (or thigh)
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier; et li restauration si est c’on lie .i. liien desus la briseure, et .i. autre desoz.	The bones of the thigh are often broken, and one can see it when they twist it forward or backward; and the restoration is such that one ligament is tied above the break, and another below.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment; et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	And the patient lies on their face, then each attendant extends their ligament equally to its corresponding place; and this is when the fracture is within the bone.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure. Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval; puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses .ij. mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	If the fracture is near the root of the thigh, then one ligament should be towards the hip and others towards the fracture. And if it is near the knee, then ligaments should be below the knee, and extend beyond; then place the patient's leg equal to its two hands, as per its natural figure, and then apply the splint and the bandage, without an abscess coming up.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure; li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	And if there is an abscess that boils, let it cool down first, then return to your work and treatment; the incision is made in this manner.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure .i. bendeil dur doublé en .ij. ou .iij., et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute .i. fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus; puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe; puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment .iij. tors ou iiij. sus la briseure; et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint; puis enten as .ij. chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie .iij. esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet; et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	You should bind it up above the fracture with a thick doubled bandage for two or three days, and allow the superfluous material to drain out, then turn the leg so that the heels are at the root of the thigh, and insert one long pin between the thigh and the leg, just below the knee, and bring the head of the pin above; then turn the leg and the upper part of the bandage, then place the stirrups on the fracture and place a stirrup on the bone of the leg; then use soft cloth for seven inches between the leg and thigh to even out the tightness, then begin to bind tightly in four turns or more above the fracture; and as you go higher up the fracture, loosen it; then take the two pins that you inserted between the leg and thigh, and tie three stirrups over them, then return to beneath the head of the pin, so that you are below the hip, tighten it so that it does not move from its place, then leave it like this, until there is no sign of abscess or inflammation.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet; et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	If pieces of the bone are protruding, you must remove them if possible; and if not, you must cut the area and draw out pus; treat it as we have said until it is healed.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	And sometimes the leg is broken in such a way that splints are placed on it, as in the shoulder or arm; however, in the restoration made in this manner, the patient does not experience any pain.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en .l. jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	Know that the leg is restored within a day, or a little more or less, according to the different complexions.
de la ruelle dou genoil	of the alleyway of the knee
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois. Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou .i. pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	Know that in the alleyway of the knee occurs little breakage, but it bends frequently. And if it breaks, it is not just a fracture, but rather a split or a deep wound, and it causes pain everywhere, and this is felt by everyone.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet; puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant; si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is that one equalizes the round end to its socket, as long as it can be assembled; then place the arm, and place a round peg there if needed, and tighten it as required; then check all the arrangements we have said in other breakages, like an abscess, burn, and so on; place at each accident what is needed for it, until it heals.
de la brisure de la jambe	of the leg fracture
Saiches que en la jambe ait .ij. os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i.	Know that in the leg there are two bones, of which one is called directly "mustelz", and the others are called "foscile"; and it has the same kind of fracture as the arm, and for this reason, the restoration is the same as that of the arm equally, and the work is the same.
Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	And if both the bones of the limb are broken together, the leg turns in all directions.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if the slender bone is broken, it turns forward.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz. Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement; mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere; et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	And if the large bone is broken, it causes great pain and can be seen; it turns under. Then bring an extension, make it even, and tie the splinters equally; however, if the break is misaligned or has more pieces, the extension should be smaller and lighter; and align it according to your ability.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren .ij. faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en .ij. leus .i. bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent .i. bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have completed your work, take two fists of thick yarn that wrap around the leg on both sides and are as long as the leg from the knee to below; then wind them twice in two layers, one above and one below, and tie them at this point; the leg will not be able to decline to the right or left, and it is good; nor should anyone add a splint of the same length as the leg, and place the leg for protection from movement; it is done properly at the break where there is pain; move the leg every day to see if there is any abscess or other accident; cure it until it is healed.
de la brisure des os dou piet	Of the break of the bones from the foot
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	At the ankle, there is no breakage, but the bones of the foot sometimes suffer breakage and also the toes, and there is no force except for the shortening in various positions.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a .ij. chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	And if there is breakage in the bones of the foot and you see these bones rise up against each other, place the patient's foot on a flat surface like he wants to walk, then place your foot on his, where the bones are raised, then press them back into their places; then put a splint and bandages on it, and put a small board under the foot with two hollow spaces, then bind the foot evenly, as you have covered it with cloths and other things that you need.
Et quant .iij. jors ou .iiij. seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And when four or six days have passed, unbind the bandages, for you will find the bones even, whether they are broken or dislocated.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a .ij. ou .iij., ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	And if any of the two [shoulders] are broken, restore them as we have said for the hands of the hand; then place a splint on the broken one according to the length of the arm, and let it be slightly larger; then place a piece of wood under the affected shoulder as I have said, and hold it in position; and if there are 2 or 3, or more [broken shoulders], break each one, placing a splint on it according to its size, wrapped in one linen cloth, and hold the wood under the affected shoulder; and let the top of the wood be turned away from the stomach of the shoulder so that it covers well.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit; et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	And do not forget the other things I have said about broken bones, after we have spoken of them; and treat each accident according to its need.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	on the break of the wrist bone
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com .i. sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice .vij. jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the bone of the woman's pelvis is broken, make her sit with her legs apart, then incline her to the lower back part and hold her from behind; then fill the cavity in the pelvis with cotton and put in as much as a pound; then turn the woman, tilt her hips and scoop out the lower back gently, and when the cotton comes to the entrance of the pelvis, the bone returns with the pound; and whenever she wants to urinate, remove the cotton, and whenever she has emptied it, put it back, and do this for 7 days: the break will heal, and if you see, take a bladder of barley, tie one end of a cord to it, and push the whole bladder into the pelvis; then inflate the bladder forcefully through the cord until it is filled inside: the break will return; then fill it with cotton, and leave it for some days until it heals.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre. Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	And when the bone of the man's thumb is broken or that of a woman, restore it as we have said in the treatment for the pelvis; and these breaks shall not be hidden from him who applies his study and experience to them, and my book is intended for this purpose. For the break indicates various dispositions towards restoration: take note of this then.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse .iij. jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	In a spear (shaft), when it is broken, take an owl's gullet and put the shaft inside; then wrap fabrics around it, and leave it for 3 or 4 days, and it will heal quickly.
de brisure avec plaie	of a break with a wound
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	It is necessary for the one who has a break with a wound, especially if it is large, such as the bone of the leg or shoulder or similar, that it should be treated immediately, as the writings we have said bear witness to.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound is healed, anoint it with vitriol, unless you have something else, then immediately proceed to restore the break in that same hour, or the next day, if abscesses do not come.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if abscesses come, let the restoration wait until the ninth day, until the abscess is appeased, and do not touch it on the third or fourth day, for you would cause bad accidents.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the bone is broken and appears on the surface near the opening, it should be set gently with light pressure, at a small extension.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a .vij. dois ou .viij. de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne .iii. ou iiij., selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	And if the limbs are not aligned to be set evenly by your hands, it should be realigned with this tool made of iron, which is about 7 or 8 inches long, and the width according to the size of the wound; and therefore, the mirror must grasp 3 or 4, according to what is needed in each case of bone setting; and it should be round and slightly larger than required, so that it does not bend when compressed on the limb during your work, and sharp at the front, and large in the middle towards the wound, like this:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre. Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	And it is called "palainche," so the curved limb should be placed on top of the visible bone; push it once until it returns to its original position and align it evenly with the other one. If the fracture is subtle, and the tool cannot grasp the bone properly, you must cut the visible part of the bone until the tool can take hold of it.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	And if you cannot reset the bone, as we have said, strike it with an appropriate instrument, either chisel or saw, within your power; then remove what remains in the bone with sharpness and small shavings.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil. Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille .i. drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	And when the bone is reset and the patient feels great pain afterward, know that it is not in its natural place. Make sure it is in its proper place, then moisten a clean cloth in black, sticky wine (if it is summer) or alcohol; do not apply any oil to the wound, as it will cause pus and corruption; then administer splints when you have restored the bone, leave the wound open, cover the area completely according to the size of the wound, and take care that the wound is not strained with a fracture. Many fools have done this, causing either death or further injury to the patient; therefore, let the bandages be softer and more flexible than other fractures.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie. Et quant tu vois aprés .i. jor ou .ij. enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	If the wound is large or bad and you fear that an accident may occur, as we have said, and if you feel pain at the site, do not apply splints; instead, wrap it without splints, using hard cloths and tie them. After one or two days, if you see pus coming out of the wound, remove what you had put on it and apply a healing ointment such as tetrafarmaçon and similar ones.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre .ij. fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And it is necessary that you dislocate the member twice a day, in the morning and at evening, until it heals and becomes healthy.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And the limbs should be set in such a way that the bone moves downward slightly.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	If it passes many days and the bone cannot heal but keeps bowing out again, as there are small fragments of bones; therefore, you must press the wound firmly and remove all the dislocated pieces causing pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant. Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés .xx. jors ou .xxx., puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	And if there is an abscess or other corruption at the site, you must treat it according to what was said in its chapter earlier. And when a bone is broken and open on the limb, such as the bones of the thigh or shoulder, and similar large members, do not drain it, as many times death follows; but leave it until it can be drained; perhaps it will heal by itself after 20 or 30 days. Then treat the wound if possible; otherwise, leave it.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	The swellings that come upon the sore
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	We often come after the healing of the break, especially when it is near the joint, and the appearance of the limb is dreadful to see; and unfortunately, the limb cannot perform its natural functions.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Therefore, take care with him if he is weak: administer medicines such as aloes, incense, myrrh, and saracolle, acacia, and similar others, so that you choose one of these things or all together, grind them into powder with wine steeped in alcohol or egg whites or oil; place it on the sore in poultices, press it well and do not remove it for many days; then loosen it, and start another, until the swelling is removed; or you strain over a piece of plank well made; because the properties of wood are such that it removes all inflammations from the limbs; and if the nodation has turned into hardness like stone, and it is necessary to remove it, you chop off the top, and reveal the superfluous parts; or you shave it at any rasp, until it is removed, and cure it until it is healed.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	The weak limb after treatment
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	When the fracture of the bone is restored and remains after the limbs are weak and delicate, it happens for many reasons: one reason being that it was tied too tightly, and was not bound as it should have been; or because there were too many ligaments, and the nutrients could not reach the member; or because of excessive bleeding; or because of excessive movement, not in its proper time; or because the patient has little blood in his body, making him weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	And the remedy is to make the sick person eat, and make his body lean, until the wounds multiply in him; provide baths, and give joy and cheerfulness; then apply balm to the limb, so that the balm attracts great nutrients to it, and irrigate it with cold water often, until the nutrients reach the limb; return it to its natural form.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	The twisted limb after health
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai .i. emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	When the limb is twisted after restoration, and the bones are broken open, and the shape of the limb is misshapen, nevertheless do not lose hope; do not believe the foolish who say one should break the limb new, and many foolish people have done this in our land; and this practice is blamed, and great harm comes from it, and perhaps death; however, if the swelling and twisting are fresh, you must anoint with warm water, or softening herbs such as marshmallow leaves, roots, clover, and similar things, and make a poultice. You should prepare one soothing poultice, such as daisy, and take the musk oil of comfrey, and mix it with ginger oil or sesame oil, and apply the poultice; or you can grind ripe figs with wheat bran, and similar medicines that reduce swelling.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes. Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And sometimes the swelling is removed by rubbing continuously and for a long time with moist hands. It should be moved in the limb every hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.
